Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Imam's Position in Women's and Naked People's Congregation
Rulings on imam's position for women and naked people in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the imam must stand in the middle when leading women or naked people, and explain the proof and consequences.

Core Idea
The imam must stand in the middle of women or naked followers to minimize exposure; it is wajib, not just recommended.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the position of the imam in two special congregational settings: when the followers are all women, and when they are naked (unable to cover properly). The ruling is that the imam must stand in the middle of the row, not ahead, to reduce the risk of exposure. The proof comes from the practice of Aisha (RA) and from the principle of avoiding the greater harm. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the Hanafi emphasis on avoiding even the appearance of impropriety in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is the imam's position in the row. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) for the imam to stand in the middle when leading women or naked people, not ahead.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary evidence is the action of Aisha (RA) who, when leading women, stood in the middle. This is a Sunnah action (fi'li) of a Companion, considered proof.
The text says 'because Aisha did so' and interprets it as establishing the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The reasoning behind the ruling is that going forward increases exposure of the imam's figure (and for women, this is problematic). Standing in the middle minimizes exposure. For the naked, the same principle applies to avoid seeing each other's private parts.
For women, the karahah (dislike) of congregation remains, but standing in the middle is the lesser of two evils.
4
Analyze the consequence of omission
If the imam goes forward, she commits a sin but the prayer remains valid (sahih). If she stands behind the row, the followers' prayer is invalid because the follower cannot be ahead of the imam.
This shows the distinction between wajib and rukn.
5
Contrast with the naked people's case
For the naked, congregation itself is discouraged; individual prayer is preferable. But if they do pray in congregation, the imam must also stand in the middle. The ruling is analogized to women's case.
Al-Hasan al-Basri's objection (lowering gaze) is rejected because lowering gaze in prayer is itself disliked.

Source Text

قوله (فإن فعلن تقف الإمام وسطهن كالعرات لأن عائشة رضي الله عنها فعلت كذلك وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابتداء الاسلام ولأن في التقدم زيادة الكشف. وأفاد بالتعبير بقوله «تقف» أنه واجب فلو تقدمت أثمت كما صرح به في فتح القدير والصلاة صحيحة، فإذا توسطت لا تزول الكراهة وإنما أرشدوا إلى التوسط لأنه أقل كراهية من التقدم. كذا في السراج الوهاج. ولو تأخرت لم يصح الاقتداء بها عندنا لعدم شرطه وهو عدم التأخر عن المأموم. وذكر في المغرب الإمام من يؤتم به أي يقتدى به ذكراً كان أو أنثى . وفي الواو مع السين الوسط بالتحريك اسم لعين ما بين طرفي الشيء كمركز الدائرة وبالسكون اسم مبهم لداخل الدائرة مثلاً ولذلك كان بالأول مستوياً فيه المذكر المؤنث والاثنان والجمع . قال الله تعالى جعلناكم أمة وسطاً) [البقرة: ١٤٣] ولله علي أن أهدي شاتين وسطاً إلى بيت الله أو أعتق عبدين وسطاً. وقد بنى منه أفعل التفضيل فقيل للذكر الأوسط وللمؤنث الوسطى قال تعالى من أوسط ما تطعمون أهليكم [المائدة: ۸۹] يعني المتوسط بين الإسراف والتقتير. وقد أكثروا في ذلك وهو في محل الرفع على البدل من اطعام أو كسوتهم معطوف عليه والصلاة الوسطى العصر وهو المشهور .اهـ. وضبطه هنا في السراج الوهاج بسكون السين لا غير. وفي الصحاح : كل موضع صلح فيه بين فهو وسط بالتسكين كجلست وسط القوم ، وإن لم يصلح فيه فهو بالتحريك كجلست وسط الدار بما سكن وليس بالوجه اهـ. وفي ضياء الحلوم الوسط بالسكون ظرف مكان، وبفتح السين اسم تقول وَسْطَ هو على ظاهره وجب بمعنى ثبت ولزم أي لما دار الأمر بين المحذورين ثبت وتعين الأول وهو جماعتهن. هذا ولا يخفى ما في تسمية جماعتهن بالفرض من البعد وكذا بالواجب لما سيصرح به المؤلف في الجنائز من أن الجماعة فيها غير واجبة. قوله : (وفي معراج الدراية والتشبيه الخ) فيه​ الإمام وسطهن كالعرات ويقف الواحد عن يمينه والاثنان خلفه ويصف الرجال ثم رأسدهن بسكون السين وفتح الطاء فهذا ظرف، فإذا فتحت السين رفعت الطاء وقلت وَسَطُ رأسه دهن فهذا اسم اهـ. وفي معراج الدراية والتشبيه بالعراة ليس من كل وجه بل في أفضلية الإفراد وأفضلية قيام الإمام وسطهن، وأما العراة فيصلون قعوداً وهو أفضل والنساء قائمات. وفي الخلاصة : يصلون قعوداً بإيماء وإن صلوا بقيام وركوع وسجود بجماعة أجزأهم. وذكر الاسبيجابي : وكذلك يكره أن يؤم النساء في بيت وليس معهن رجل ولا محرم منه مثل زوجته وأمته وأخته فإن كانت واحدة منهن فلا يكره، وكذلك إذا أمهن في المسجد لا يكره، وإطلاق المحرم على من ذكر تغليب وإلا فليس هو محرماً لزوجته وأمته . قوله (ويقف الواحد عن يمينه والأثنان خلفه لحديث ابن عباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى به وأقامه عن يمينه، وهو ظاهر في محاذاة اليمين وهي المساواة وهذا هو المذهب خلافاً لما من يجعل أصبعه عند عقب الإمام. وأفاد الشارح أنه لو وقف عن يساره فإنه يكره اتفاقاً، ولو وقف خلفه فيه روايتان أصحهما الكراهة وأطلق في الواحد فشمل البالغ والصبي واحترز به عن المرأة فإنها لا تكون إلا خلفه . فلو كان معه رجل وامرأة فإنه يقيم الرجل إشعار بأن وقوفه وسطهم واجب كالنساء لأنه شبه صلاتهم وقيام إمامهم بالنساء، وقد علل قبله كراهة جماعتهن بقول : ولأن جماعتهن لا تخلو عن ارتكاب محرم لأن في التقدم زيادة كسف وفي التوسط ترك المقام وكل ذلك حرام، وصدر عبارته يدل على هذا حيث قال: وله «كالعراة فإنهم أمروا بترك الجماعة ليتباعد بعضهم عن بعض فلا يقع بصر بعضهم على عورة البعض لأن الستر يحصل به، ولكن الأولى لإمامهم إذا أمهم أن يقوم وسطهم وإن تقدمهم جاز، وحالهم في هذا الموضع كحال النساء. كذا في المبسوطين. وقال الحسن البصري رحمه الله تعالى : يصلون بالجماعة لأنهم يتوصلون إلى إقامتها من غير ارتكاب مكروه بأن يقدموا إمامهم ويغضوا أبصارهم قلنا : غض البصر مكروه حالة الاختيار كقيام الإمام وسط الصف فصح أنهم لا يتوصلون إلى إقامتها بدون ارتكاب أمر مكروه، والجماعة سنة فترك السنة أولى من ارتكاب المكروه. فعلم بهذا كله أن التشبيه الخ فظهر أن قوله بل في أفضلية الإفراد الخ ليس المراد أنه جائز والإفراد والقيام أفضل بل المراد بالأفضلية الوجوب، وكذا قول المبسوطين أولى لقولهما وحالهم في هذا الموضع كحال النساء» تأمل. وفي النهر : وفي كلام المصنف إيماء إلى كراهة جماعة العراة أيضاً كراهة تحريم لاتحاد اللازم وهو إما ترك واجب التقدم أو زيادة الكشف كذا في الفتح لكن في السراج الأولى أن يصلوا وحداناً، وفي الخلاصة الأولى لإمام العراة أن يقف وسطهم، ومقتضى ما في الفتح أن يكون تحريماً بالأولى وهو أولى اهـ. أقول : يمكن أن يكون المراد بالأولى في كلام السراج والخلاصة كما هو المراد من كلام المبسوطين تأمل . قوله : (وإطلاق المحرم على من ذكر تغليب الخ) قال في النهر : ذكر بعض المتأخرين أن الزوج محرم مستنداً لما في الذخيرة والمحرم الزوج ومن لا يجوز مناكحتها على التأبيد وسيأتي تحقيقه في الحج إن شاء الله تعالى .
His saying: (If they do so, the imam stands in their middle like the naked people) because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) did so, and her action is interpreted as being at the beginning of Islam, and because going forward increases exposure. And by using the word 'stands' it indicates that it is obligatory, so if she goes forward she sins, as stated in Fath al-Qadir, but the prayer is valid. When she stands in the middle, the dislike does not cease; they only guide to the middle because it is less disliked than going forward. Likewise in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And if she stands behind, following her is not valid according to us due to the absence of its condition, which is not being behind the follower. And it is mentioned in al-Mughrib that the imam is the one who is followed, whether male or female. And regarding the letter waw and sin, 'al-wasat' with a fatha on the sin is a noun for the exact middle between two ends, like the center of a circle; with sukun it is an ambiguous noun for the inside of the circle, for example, and therefore is an adverb. The first is used as a subject, object, or with a preposition; none of this is valid for the second. You say 'Its middle is better than its edges' and 'its middle expanded' and 'I hit its middle' and 'I sat in the middle of the house' and 'I sat in its middle' with sukun only. It is described with the first, being uniform for masculine, feminine, dual, and plural. Allah said: 'Thus We have made you a middle nation' (2:143) and 'I have vowed to sacrifice two middle sheep' and 'free two middle slaves'. The comparative was derived from it: 'al-awsat' for masculine and 'al-wusta' for feminine. Allah said: 'from the middle of what you feed your families' (5:89), meaning the moderate between extravagance and stinginess. They spoke much about this, and it is in the nominative case as a substitute for 'feeding' or 'clothing'. The middle prayer is Asr, which is well-known. End. And its voweling here in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is with sukun of the sin only. In al-Sihah: every place where 'between' is suitable, it is 'wasat' with sukun, like 'I sat in the middle of the people'; if not suitable, it is with fatha, like 'I sat in the middle of the house' with sukun, but that is not correct. End. In Diya' al-Hulum: 'al-wasat' with sukun is an adverb of place; with fatha of the sin it is a noun. You say 'Wasatu ra'sihi duhn' (the middle of his head is oil) with fatha and raf' of 'ra's', so it is a noun. It is apparent that it is obligatory, meaning established and necessary, i.e., when the matter is between two prohibitions, the first is established and determined, which is their congregation. This, and it is not hidden that calling their congregation an obligation is far-fetched, likewise an obligatory act, because the author will clarify in the funeral chapter that congregation is not obligatory. His saying: (And in Mi'raj al-Dirayah, the comparison with the naked is not from every aspect, but rather in the superiority of individual prayer and the superiority of the imam standing in their middle. As for the naked, they pray sitting, which is better, while the women stand. In al-Khulasa: They pray sitting with gestures, and if they pray with standing, bowing, and prostrating in congregation, it suffices them. And al-Asbijabi mentioned: Likewise it is disliked for a man to lead women in a house where there is no man or mahram with them, like his wife, slave woman, or sister; if one of them is present, it is not disliked. Likewise, if he leads them in the mosque, it is not disliked. The application of 'mahram' to those mentioned is a generalization, otherwise the husband is not a mahram for his wife or slave woman. His saying: (And the one man stands on his right, and two behind him) due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed with him and stood him on his right, which is apparent in alignment with the right, which is equality, and this is the school, contrary to those who place his fingers at the imam's heel. The commentator stated that if he stands on his left, it is disliked by agreement, and if he stands behind him, there are two narrations, the soundest being dislike. He used the word 'one' absolutely, including the adult and the child, and excluded the woman, who is only behind him. If there is a man and a woman with him, he places the man... An indication that his standing in their middle is obligatory like the women, because their prayer and the standing of their imam are compared to the women. He earlier explained the dislike of their congregation by saying: 'Their congregation is not free from committing something forbidden, because going forward increases exposure, and standing in the middle abandons the standing place, and all that is haram.' The beginning of his statement indicates this when he said: 'And for them, like the naked, they are commanded to abandon congregation to distance themselves from each other so that their sight does not fall on each other's private parts, because covering is achieved by that, but it is preferred for their imam, when he leads them, to stand in their middle, and if he goes forward, it is permissible. Their situation in this regard is like that of women.' Thus in al-Mabsutayn. And al-Hasan al-Basri (may Allah have mercy on him) said: They pray in congregation because they can achieve it without committing a disliked act by advancing their imam and lowering their gaze. We say: Lowering the gaze is disliked in a state of choice, like the imam standing in the middle of the row, so it is established that they cannot achieve it without committing a disliked act. Congregation is sunnah, so abandoning the sunnah is better than committing a disliked act. By all this, it is known that the comparison... So it appears that his statement 'rather in the superiority of individual prayer' is not intended to mean that it is permissible and individual prayer is better; rather, by 'superiority' he means obligation. Likewise, the statement of al-Mabsutayn 'preferable' is due to their saying 'their situation in this regard is like that of women'; reflect. In al-Nahr: In the author's speech there is an indication of the dislike of the congregation of the naked, also a prohibitional dislike, due to the unity of the necessary consequence, which is either abandoning the obligatory advancement or increasing exposure. Thus in al-Fath, but in al-Siraj, it is preferred that they pray individually. In al-Khulasa, it is preferred for the imam of the naked to stand in their middle, and the requirement of what is in al-Fath is that it is a prohibition by priority, which is better. End. I say: It is possible that what is meant by 'preferable' in the words of al-Siraj and al-Khulasa is what is meant by the words of al-Mabsutayn; reflect. His saying: (And the application of 'mahram' to those mentioned is a generalization) etc. He said in al-Nahr: Some later scholars mentioned that the husband is a mahram, based on what is in al-Dhakhirah: the mahram is the husband and one whom it is permanently forbidden to marry. Its verification will come in Hajj, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 615

Commentary
This extended passage comprises several rulings connected to the imam's position in congregational prayer. The first part deals with women's congregation: when women pray together, the imam (a woman) must stand in the middle of the row, not ahead. This is based on the practice of Aisha (RA) and because going forward increases exposure of her figure, which is discouraged. The word 'stands' indicates obligation (wajib), so if the imam goes forward, she sins, but the prayer remains valid. Standing in the middle does not remove the inherent dislike (karahah) of women's congregation, but it is the lesser of two evils compared to going forward. If she stands behind the row, following her is invalid because the follower must not be ahead of the imam. The passage then offers a lengthy linguistic analysis of the word 'wasat' (middle) distinguishing its use as a noun and adverb. This is relevant to interpreting the legal texts. The second main topic is the ruling for naked people (al-urât) who must pray together. They are commanded to pray individually because they cannot cover their private parts, but if they do pray in congregation, the imam should stand in their middle to minimize exposure. The discussion contrasts the preference for individual prayer (to avoid seeing each other's private parts) with the obligation of the imam to stand in the middle. Al-Hasan al-Basri argued for congregation with lowered gaze, but the Hanafi response is that lowering the gaze is itself disliked in prayer, so abandoning congregation (which is sunnah) is better than committing a disliked act. The passage concludes with a ruling about a man leading women in a house without a mahram: it is disliked (karahah) unless the women include his wife, slave woman, or sister, or if it is in a mosque. Finally, there is a note on the term 'mahram' and a discussion that the husband is not technically a mahram, though some later scholars treat him as such. Throughout, the legal nuance of 'obligation' vs. 'preference' is carefully maintained.

Key Terms
وسط (wasat): The middle; when used with sukun (wasṭ) it is an adverb meaning 'in the middle'; with fatha (wasat) it is a noun meaning the exact middle portion.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently forbidden, thus permissible to be alone with; husband is not technically a mahram but is included by extension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if the imam of women stands ahead of the row instead of in the middle?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The imam sins, but the prayer is valid.
C) The prayer is valid and there is no sin.
D) The congregation is invalid but individual prayers are valid.

Key Takeaway
The imam of a women's or naked congregation must stand in the middle of the row; doing otherwise is sinful but prayer remains valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Imam Must Stand in the Middle When Leading Women
Ruling with proof using qiyas (analogy) and intra-madhhab tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's position for women, explain the analogy with naked people, and apply the tarjih between afdaliyyah as wajib vs mandub.

Core Idea
The imam must stand in the middle of the women’s row (wajib) by analogy with naked people to avoid forbidden exposure.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi ruling: when leading women in congregational prayer, the imam should not stand in front but in the middle of their row. The proof is an analogy with naked people praying together, which also requires the imam to be in the middle to prevent impermissible looking. We will unpack the reasoning and the debate over whether this is merely preferred (mandub) or obligatory (wajib).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Find the passage's statement about the imam's position for women. Note that the author uses an analogy (tashbih) with naked people (al-urāt). What is the exact ruling?
The ruling is that the imam should stand in the middle of the women's row.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
Break down the analogy: asl = naked people, hukm = imam must be in middle to avoid looking at awrah; illa = preventing forbidden exposure; far' = women praying in congregation; hukm far' = imam must be in middle.
The illa (effective cause) is prevention of exposure (haraj).
3
Differentiate afdaliyyah
The text says 'afdaliyyah' (preferability) but the later Hanafis interpret this as wajib (obligation) due to the threat of sin. Identify the dispute and the mufta bihi.
Some earlier scholars considered it merely mandub; the tarjih is wajib.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a woman's jama'ah where the imam stands in front. According to the mufta bihi view, the prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi. Confirm this from the madhhab dispute map.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the ruling of makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتشبيه بالعراة ليس من كل وجه بل في أفضلية الإفراد وأفضلية قيام الإمام وسطهن، وأما العراة فيصلون قعوداً وهو أفضل والنساء قائمات. وفي الخلاصة : يصلون قعوداً بإيماء وإن صلوا بقيام وركوع وسجود بجماعة أجزأهم. وذكر الاسبيجابي : وكذلك يكره أن يؤم النساء في بيت وليس معهن رجل ولا محرم منه مثل زوجته وأمته وأخته فإن كانت واحدة منهن فلا يكره، وكذلك إذا أمهن في المسجد لا يكره، وإطلاق المحرم على من ذكر تغليب وإلا فليس هو محرماً لزوجته وأمته . قوله (ويقف الواحد عن يمينه والأثنان خلفه لحديث ابن عباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى به وأقامه عن يمينه، وهو ظاهر في محاذاة اليمين وهي المساواة وهذا هو المذهب خلافاً لما من يجعل أصبعه عند عقب الإمام. وأفاد الشارح أنه لو وقف عن يساره فإنه يكره اتفاقاً، ولو وقف خلفه فيه روايتان أصحهما الكراهة وأطلق في الواحد فشمل البالغ والصبي واحترز به عن المرأة فإنها لا تكون إلا خلفه . فلو كان معه رجل وامرأة فإنه يقيم الرجل عن يمينه والمرأة خلفهما، وإن كان رجلان وامرأة أقام الرجلين خلفه والمرأة خلفهما. وإنما يتقدم الرجلين لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام تقدم على أنس واليتيم حين صلى بهما وهو دليل الأفضلية، وما ورد من فعل ابن مسعود من أنه توسطهما فهو دليل الإباحة. كذا في الهداية وغيرها. وذكر الاسبيجابي أنه لو كان معه رجلان فإمامهم بالخيار إن شاء تقدم وإن شاء أقام فيما بينهما. ولو كانوا جماعة فينبغي للإمام أن يتقدم ولو لم يتقدم إلا أنه أقام على ميمنة الصف أو على ميسرته أو قام في وسط الصف فإنه يجوز ويكره. وينبغي أن يكون بحذاء الإمام من هو أفضل. ولو قال المصنف كما في النقاية لكان أولى والزائد خلفه لشمول الزائد الاثنين والأكثر . وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان المقتدي عن يمين الإمام فجاء ثالث وجذب المؤتم إلى نفسه بعدما كبر الثالث لا تفسد صلاته. وأشار المصنف إلى أن العبرة إنما هو للقدم لا للرأس فلو كان الإمام أقصر من المقتدي تقع رأس المقتدي قدام الإمام يجوز بعد أن يكون محاذياً بقدمه أو متأخراً قليلاً، وكذا في محاذاة المرأة كما سيأتي. وإن تفاوتت الأقدام صغراً وكبراً فالعبرة بالساق والكعب، والأصح ما لم يتقدم أكثر قدم المقتدي لا تفسد صلاته . كذا في المجتبى. وفي الظهيرية : ولو جاء والصف متصل انتظر حتى يجيء الآخر فإن خاف فوت الركعة جذب واحداً من الصف إن علم أنه لا يؤذيه، وإن اقتدى به خلف الصفوف جاز لما روي أن أبا بكرة قام خلف الصف فدب راكعاً حتى التحق بالصف ، فلما فرغ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : يا أبا بكرة زادك الله حرصاً في الدين. ولو كان في الصحراء ينبغي أن يكبر أولاً ثم يجذبه ولو جذبه أولاً فتأخر ثم كبر هو قيل تفسد صلاة الذي تأخر . ذكره الزندوستي في نظمه والمعنى فيه أن هذا إجابة بالفعل فيعتبر بالإجابة بالقول، ولو أجاب بالقول فسدت كما إذا أخبر بخبر يسره فقال : الحمد لله. والأصح أنه لا تفسد صلاته .اهـ. وفي القنية : والقيام وحده أولى في زماننا لغلبة الجهل على العوام . قوله (ويصف الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم النساء لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهي ) (۱) ولأن المحاذاة مفسدة فيؤخرون وليلني أمر الغائب من الولي وهو
And the comparison with naked people is not in every aspect, but in the preference of being alone and the preference of the imam standing in their middle. As for naked people, they pray sitting, and that is better, while women pray standing. In al-Khulasa: They pray sitting with gesture, and if they pray with standing, bowing, and prostration in congregation, it suffices them. Al-Isbijabi mentioned: Likewise, it is disliked for a man to lead women in prayer in a house where there is no man or mahram from him, like his wife, his slave, or his sister; if one of them is present, it is not disliked. Similarly, if he leads them in the mosque, it is not disliked. The use of 'mahram' for those mentioned is predominant, otherwise, he is not a mahram for his wife and his slave. His statement: 'And the one (follower) stands on his right, and the two behind him, due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed with him and placed him on his right, and it is apparent in alignment with the right, which is equality, and this is the madhhab, contrary to those who place his finger at the heel of the imam.' And the commentator indicated that if he stood on his left, it is disliked by agreement, and if he stood behind him, there are two narrations, the more correct is disliked. He gave absolute statement for one, so it includes adult and child, and he excluded woman, for she is only behind him. So if there is a man and a woman with him, he places the man on his right and the woman behind both. If there are two men and a woman, he places the two men behind him and the woman behind them. The two men are placed ahead because the Prophet (peace be upon him) led Anas and the orphan in prayer and placed them ahead, which is evidence of preference, and what is reported from Ibn Mas'ud that he stood between them is evidence of permissibility. Thus in al-Hidayah and others. Al-Isbijabi mentioned that if there are two men with him, the imam has the choice to stand ahead or between them. If there is a congregation, the imam should stand ahead; if he does not stand ahead but stands on the right side of the row or on the left side or in the middle of the row, it is permissible but disliked. The best should be opposite the imam. If the author had said as in al-Niqayah, it would be better: 'and the additional (followers) behind him' because the additional includes two and more. In al-Khulasa: If the follower is on the right of the imam and a third comes and pulls the follower to himself after the third's takbir, his prayer is not invalidated. The author indicated that consideration is for the foot, not the head; so if the imam is shorter than the follower, the follower's head is in front of the imam, it is permissible as long as his foot is aligned or slightly behind. Similarly for the alignment of a woman as will come. If the feet differ in size, consideration is for the shin and ankle. The most correct is that as long as the follower's foot is not more than a foot ahead, his prayer is not invalidated. Thus in al-Mujtaba. In al-Zahiriyya: If one comes and the row is continuous, he waits until another comes; if he fears missing the rak'ah, he pulls one from the row if he knows he will not hurt him. If he prays behind the rows, it is permissible due to the narration that Abu Bakra stood behind the row and crawled bowing until he joined the row, and when the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) finished, he said: 'O Abu Bakra, may Allah increase you in eagerness for the religion.' If in an open space, he should first say the takbir then pull him; if he pulls him first then he steps back and then says the takbir, it is said that the prayer of the one who stepped back is invalidated. Mentioned by al-Zindawasti in his poem, and the meaning is that this is a response by action, so it is considered like a response by speech; if he responded by speech, his prayer would be invalidated, as when he hears good news and says 'Alhamdulillah'. The most correct is that his prayer is not invalidated. End. In al-Qunyah: Standing alone is better in our time due to the prevalence of ignorance among the common people. His statement: 'And he arranges the men, then the boys, then the women, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Let those of you who are of understanding and reason be near me.' And because alignment is corruptive, so they are delayed. 'Liyalni' is a command to the absent from the one who is in charge, and it is
Source pages p. 616

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses several rulings regarding the arrangement of worshippers in congregational prayer. The author (Ibn Nujaym) explains the preferred positions for the imam and followers, starting with the analogy between women praying in congregation and naked people (al-urāt) who must avoid exposing their private parts. The comparison is not absolute but highlights that like naked people who are better off praying individually to avoid looking at each other's awrah, women are similarly advised to have the imam stand in their midst rather than in front. However, unlike naked people who pray sitting, women stand. The imam's position in the middle is considered obligatory (wajib) based on the reasoning that standing in front would involve forbidden exposure or leaving the proper place. The author then discusses the ruling for a single male follower: he stands on the imam's right, aligned equally (shoulder to shoulder). Standing on the left is disliked by agreement, and standing behind has two narrations, the more authentic being disliked. If there are two men, they stand behind the imam, and a woman stands behind them. The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and the practice of Anas and the orphan are cited. The author also addresses the ruling when a third person arrives and pulls a follower, as well as the consideration of foot alignment rather than head alignment. Finally, he mentions the order of rows: men first, then boys, then women, based on the hadith 'Let those of understanding be near me.'

Key Terms
العراة (al-urāt): People who are naked, with their private parts exposed, who are praying in congregation.
محاذاة (muḥādāh): Alignment of the feet; the follower's foot should be in line with the imam's foot, not the head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in the text, where should the imam stand when leading women in congregational prayer?
A) In front of the women's row
B) In the middle of the women's row
C) Behind the women's row
D) Anywhere in the mosque

Key Takeaway
The imam leading women in prayer must stand in the middle of the row (wajib) to avoid forbidden exposure, by analogy with naked people.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Arranging Followers in Congregational Prayer: Rows and Alignment
Rulings with proofs from hadith and practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for where followers stand relative to the imam, explain the foot alignment criterion, and apply the order of rows (men, boys, women).

Core Idea
One follower stands on the imam’s right, two or more behind; alignment is by the foot, not the head.

This lesson covers the precise arrangement of followers in congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school. We will examine the hadith evidence for a single follower on the right, the ruling for two or more behind, and the important distinction that alignment is judged by the foot, not the head. We will also learn the order of rows: men, then boys, then women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a single male follower
Locate the text about 'al-wahid' (the single follower). What is his prescribed position and the proof?
He stands on the imam's right, aligned equally; hadith of Ibn Abbas.
2
Determine the ruling for two followers
How are two male followers arranged? What is the evidence from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with Anas and the orphan?
They stand behind the imam (the imam is ahead of them).
3
Analyze the mixed gender scenario
If there are men and women, where does each stand? What is the general rule for women?
Women are always behind the men.
4
Apply the alignment criterion
The text emphasizes that alignment is by the foot, not the head. What are the specific rulings for foot placement? Consider differences in height.
If the follower's foot is aligned or slightly behind, it is valid; the head may be ahead.
5
Arrange the rows in order
What is the sequence of rows? Cite the hadith that supports it.
Men first, then boys, then women.

الصبيان (al-ṣibyān): Boys who have not reached puberty but can pray; they stand in rows before women.

Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on the arrangement of men, boys, and women in prayer rows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer and explain the evidence from the hadith and the rationale for prioritising maturity and intellect.

Core Idea
The Prophet commanded that mature sane men stand nearest, then boys, then women — prioritising intellect and responsibility.

In congregational prayer, the arrangement of rows reflects a careful balance between honour, maturity, and preventing distraction. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on who stands where, drawing on the Prophet's command and the detailed classifications found in later works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. Determine the hukm level: fard, wajib, or sunnah?
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah — the prayer is valid even if rows are disordered.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'Liyalni minkum ulu al-ahlam wa al-nuha'. Identify its source and chain strength.
This is a hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the imperative 'liyalni' and the phrase 'ulu al-ahlam wa al-nuha' yield the preference for adult sane males?
Hanafi usul: a command indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation. 'Ahlam' (dreams) metaphorically indicates puberty; 'nuha' indicates intellect.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions internal Hanafi differences: inclusion of hermaphrodites and the comprehensive twelve-category order. Identify what is contested.
Some scholars include hermaphrodites; others omit them due to rarity. The comprehensive order adds free/slave and age distinctions.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi and why?
The relied-upon order is: free adult men, free boys, adult slaves, boy slaves, hermaphrodites, free women, female slaves. This balances the hadith and practical simplicity.

ويصف الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم النساء لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهي» ولأن المحاذاة مفسدة فيؤخرون. وليلني أمر الغائب من الولي وهو القرب، والأحلام جمع حلم بضم الحاء وهو ما يراه النائم أريد به البالغون مجازاً لأن الحلم سبب البلوغ والنهي جمع نهية وهي العقل كذا في غاية البيان. ولم يذكر الخناثى كما في المجمع وغيره لندرة وجوده. وذكر الاسبيجابي أنه يقوم الرجال صفاً مما يلي الإمام، ثم الصبيان بعدهم، ثم الخناثى، ثم الإناث، ثم الصبيات المراهقات. وفي شرح منية المصلي : المذكور في عامة الكتب أربعة أقسام، قيل وليس هذا الترتيب لهذه الأقسام بحاصر لجملة الأقسام الممكنة فإنها تنتهي إلى أثني عشر قسماً. والترتيب الحاصر لها أن يقدم الأحرار البالغون ثم الأحرار الصبيان ثم العبيد البالغون ثم العبيد الصبيان ثم الأحرار الخناثي الكبار ثم الأحرار الخنائى الصغار ثم الأرقاء الخناثى الكبار ثم الأرقاء الخناثي الصغار ثم الحرائر الكبار ثم الحرائر الصغار ثم الإماء الكبار ثم الإماء الصغار .اهـ. وظاهر كلامهم متوناً وشروحاً تقديم الرجال على الصبيان مطلقاً، سواء كانوا أحراراً أو عبيداً، فإن الصبي الحر وإن كان له شرف الحرية لكن المطلوب هنا قرب البالغ العاقل بالحديث السابق. نعم يقدم البالغ الحر على البالغ العبد، والصبي الحر على الصبي العبد والحرة البالغة على الأمة البالغة، والصبية الحرة على الصبية الأمة لشرف الحرية من غير معارض، ولم أر صريحاً حكم ما إذا صلى ومعه رجل وصبي وإن كان داخلاً تحت قوله والاثنان خلفه، وظاهر حديث أنس أنه يسوي بين الرجل والصبي ويكونان خلفه فإنه قال : فصففت أنا واليتيم وراءه والعجوز من وراثنا . ويقتضي أيضاً أن الصبي الواحد لا يكون منفرداً عن صف الرجال بل يدخل في صفهم، وأن محل هذا الترتيب إنما هو عند حضور جمع من الرجال وجمع من الصبيان فحينئذ تؤخر الصبيان بخلاف المرأة الواحدة فإنها تتأخر عن الصفوف كجماعتهن.
And he arranges the men, then the boys, then the women, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Let those among you who are possessors of dreams and intellect be near me' and because alignment (with women) is corrupting, so they are delayed. 'Liyalni' is a command to the absent from 'wali' meaning closeness, and 'al-ahlam' is the plural of 'hulm' with a damma on the ha, which is what the sleeper sees; by metaphor those who have reached puberty are intended because dreaming is a cause of puberty, and 'al-nuha' is the plural of 'nuhya' which is the intellect, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. He did not mention the hermaphrodites, as in al-Majma' and others, due to their rarity. Al-Isbijabi mentioned that men stand in a row next to the imam, then the boys after them, then the hermaphrodites, then the females, then the adolescent girls. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: it is mentioned in most books as four categories; it is said that this order does not encompass all possible categories, for they amount to twelve categories. The comprehensive order is that free adult men are advanced, then free boys, then adult slaves, then boy slaves, then free adult hermaphrodites, then free child hermaphrodites, then adult slave hermaphrodites, then child slave hermaphrodites, then free adult women, then free girls, then adult female slaves, then young female slaves. End quote. And the apparent meaning of their words, both in matn and sharh, is the absolute precedence of men over boys, whether they are free or slaves; for the free boy, though he has the honor of freedom, what is sought here is closeness of the adult sane person due to the previous hadith. Yes, the free adult is advanced over the adult slave, the free boy over the slave boy, the free adult woman over the adult female slave, and the free girl over the young female slave, due to the honor of freedom without opposition. And I have not seen explicitly the ruling when one prays with a man and a boy, although it is included under his statement 'and the two behind him'; and the apparent meaning of the hadith of Anas is that he equalizes between the man and the boy, and they are both behind him, for he said: 'I and the orphan stood behind him, and the old woman behind us.' It also implies that a single boy is not isolated from the row of men but rather enters into their row, and that this order applies only when there is a gathering of men and a gathering of boys; then the boys are delayed, unlike a single woman, who is delayed from the rows like their group.
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. The primary ruling is that men stand in the first row, then boys, then women. The proof is the Prophet's command 'Let those among you who are possessors of dreams and intellect be near me,' where 'ahlam' (dreams) is a metaphor for puberty, and 'nuha' (intellect) indicates sanity. This prioritizes mature, sane individuals. The text explains that hermaphrodites are not mentioned in many books due to rarity, but al-Isbijabi includes them between boys and females. A more comprehensive classification from Sharh Munyat al-Musalli lists twelve categories including free/slave, adult/child, and male/female/hermaphrodite. The commentary clarifies that despite a boy's freedom, maturity is the primary criterion for closeness, but within the same category, free persons are preferred over slaves. The hadith of Anas (where he and an orphan stood behind the Prophet, with an old woman behind them) shows that a single boy joins the men's row, not isolated. This ordering applies when there are multiple men and multiple boys; otherwise, a single woman (or boy?) is delayed. The passage emphasizes that the general rule is to prioritize adult sane males, then others accordingly.

Key Terms
ليلني (liyalni): A command meaning 'let him be near me' from the root w-l-y indicating closeness.
الأحلام (al-ahlam): Plural of hulm, dreams; metaphorically refers to those who have reached puberty, as dreaming is a sign of puberty.
النهي (al-nuha): Plural of nuhya, meaning intellect or reason.
الخناثى (al-khunatha): Hermaphrodites; individuals with ambiguous gender characteristics.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In congregational prayer, who stands in the first row according to the Hanafi school?
A) Free men, then slave men, then women
B) Adult sane men, then boys, then women
C) Men, then women, then children
D) Only free adult men, no one else

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritises mature sane men in the first row, then boys, then women, based on the Prophet's command; free/slave distinctions apply within categories.

Alignment and Latecomer in Congregational Prayer
Rulings on imam standing forward, alignment by feet, and latecomer pulling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for alignment in congregational prayer, explain the ruling on a latecomer pulling a person from the row, and identify the proof from the hadith of Abu Bakra.

Core Idea
Alignment is by the foot, not the head; pulling a latecomer does not invalidate the prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two important practical aspects of congregational prayer: the precise criterion for alignment (the foot) and the rules for a latecomer who fears missing the rak'a. The author also cites the hadith of Abu Bakra to support permissibility of praying behind rows. Understanding these rulings helps avoid invalidating prayer inadvertently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the text is ruling on: alignment in congregational prayer and the action of pulling a latecomer into the row.
Alignment is a sunnah muakkadah; the prayer is valid without it but recommended.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abu Bakra (ra) as proof for the permissibility of praying behind rows when necessary.
The hadith is ahad, but it provides a clear precedent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's (saw) approval of Abu Bakra's action (standing behind the row and joining while bowing) indicates that such action is permissible and does not invalidate the prayer.
The criterion for alignment is the foot, as indicated by the author's note about the head position.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars say that if a latecomer pulls a person and that person steps back, his prayer becomes invalid by analogy to responding by speech. The most correct view holds it does not invalidate.
The tarjih is based on the principle that the action is not excessive and the hadith of Abu Bakra supports leniency.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that pulling does not invalidate the pulled person's prayer, and it is recommended to wait for another if possible, especially in our time due to ignorance.
The authority weight is from al-Mujtaba, al-Zahiriyya, and other later texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أن العبرة إنما هو للقدم لا للرأس فلو كان الإمام أقصر من المقتدي تقع رأس المقتدي قدام الإمام يجوز بعد أن يكون محاذياً بقدمه أو متأخراً قليلاً، وكذا في محاذاة المرأة كما سيأتي. وإن تفاوتت الأقدام صغراً وكبراً فالعبرة بالساق والكعب، والأصح ما لم يتقدم أكثر قدم المقتدي لا تفسد صلاته. كذا في المجتبى. وفي الظهيرية : ولو جاء والصف متصل انتظر حتى يجيء الآخر فإن خاف فوت الركعة جذب واحداً من الصف إن علم أنه لا يؤذيه، وإن اقتدى به خلف الصفوف جاز لما روي أن أبا بكرة قام خلف الصف فدب راكعاً حتى التحق بالصف ، فلما فرغ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : يا أبا بكرة زادك الله حرصاً في الدين. ولو كان في الصحراء ينبغي أن يكبر أولاً ثم يجذبه ولو جذبه أولاً فتأخر ثم كبر هو قيل تفسد صلاة الذي تأخر. ذكره الزندوستي في نظمه والمعنى فيه أن هذا إجابة بالفعل فيعتبر بالإجابة بالقول، ولو أجاب بالقول فسدت كما إذا أخبر بخبر يسره فقال : الحمد لله. والأصح أنه لا تفسد صلاته .اهـ. وفي القنية : والقيام وحده أولى في زماننا لغلبة الجهل على العوام. وينبغي للقوم إذا قاموا إلى الصلاة أن يتراصوا ويسدوا الخلل ويسووا بين مناكبهم في الصفوف، ولا بأس أن يأمرهم الإمام بذلك. وينبغي أن يكملوا ما يلي الإمام من الصفوف ثم ما يلي ما يليه وهلم جراً. وإذا استوى جانباً الإمام فإنه يقوم الجائي عن يمينه وإن ترجح اليمين فإنه يقوم عن يساره، وإن وجد في الصف فرجه سدها وإلا فينتظر حتى يجيء آخر كما قدمناه.
And the author indicated that the criterion is for the foot, not the head; so if the imam is shorter than the follower, the follower's head may be in front of the imam, it is permissible as long as he is aligned with his foot or slightly behind, and likewise in alignment with a woman as will come. And if the feet differ in size, the criterion is the shin and the ankle; the most correct is that unless the follower's foot is more than a foot ahead, his prayer is not invalidated. Thus in al-Mujtaba. In al-Zahiriyya: If someone comes while the row is connected, he should wait until another comes; if he fears missing the rak'a, he may pull one from the row if he knows it will not harm him. And if he prays behind the rows, it is permissible because it is narrated that Abu Bakra stood behind the row and crept while bowing until he joined the row, and when the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) finished, he said: 'O Abu Bakra, may Allah increase you in keenness for the religion.' If it is in the open country, he should first say the takbir then pull him; if he pulls him first and he steps back and then he says the takbir, it is said that the prayer of the one who stepped back becomes invalid. Al-Zandawasti mentioned this in his poem, and the meaning is that this is a response by action, so it is considered like a response by speech; if he responds by speech, it becomes invalid, as when he is told good news and says 'Alhamdulillah'. But the most correct view is that his prayer is not invalidated. End quote. In al-Qunyah: Standing alone is better in our time due to the prevalence of ignorance among the common people. And it is fitting that when people stand for prayer, they should stand close together, fill gaps, and align their shoulders in the rows, and there is no harm in the imam ordering them to do so. And they should complete the rows nearest the imam, then the next, etc. And if the two sides of the imam become equal, then the newcomer should stand on his right side, and if the right side is already filled, then he stands on his left; and if he finds a gap in the row, he fills it, otherwise he waits until another comes, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings related to the imam's position and alignment in congregational prayer. First, the criterion for alignment is the foot, not the head. If the imam is shorter, it is permissible for the follower's head to be ahead as long as his foot is aligned or slightly behind. If feet differ in size, the criterion is the shin and ankle. The prayer is not invalidated unless the follower's foot is more than a foot ahead. Second, regarding a latecomer: if the row is connected, he should wait for another person; if he fears missing the rak'a, he may pull someone from the row, provided it does not harm that person. It is also permissible to pray behind the rows, based on the hadith of Abu Bakra. In open country, the correct order is to say takbir first, then pull; if he pulls first and the pulled person steps back, there is a difference of opinion: some say the pulled person's prayer is invalid because it is a response by action, but the most correct view is that it is not invalidated. Finally, the passage recommends that in our time, due to ignorance, standing alone (i.e., not joining a congregation with improper practices) is better. It also emphasizes proper row formation: close together, filling gaps, aligning shoulders, and completing rows from the front.

Key Terms
المحاذاة (al-muhadhat): Alignment; specifically, the alignment of the follower's foot with the imam's foot or ankle.
جذب (jadhb): Pulling; the act of a latecomer pulling a person from the row to join the row.
الفساد (al-fasad): Invalidation of prayer; here, whether the prayer of the pulled person becomes invalid due to stepping back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a latecomer fears missing the rak'a and pulls someone from a connected row, what is the most correct Hanafi ruling on the pulled person's prayer?
A) It becomes invalid because it is a response by action
B) It becomes invalid because it is like a response by speech
C) It does not become invalid
D) It becomes invalid only in the open country

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes precise physical alignment by the foot and allows a latecomer to pull a person without invalidating the pulled person's prayer, based on the Prophetic precedent.

Order of Rows and Straightening in Congregational Prayer
Explains preferred row order and sunnah of straightening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred order of rows in Hanafi fiqh and explain the rulings on straightening and filling gaps in congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Adults precede boys in rows; within the same age, free persons precede slaves. Straightening rows and filling gaps is sunnah.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of row arrangement in congregational prayer. It details the preferred sequence of worshippers based on their status and emphasizes the importance of straightening the rows, aligning shoulders, and filling gaps as part of perfecting the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary criteria for row precedence
Read the text to determine which factor takes priority: adulthood or freedom. Note that the author states 'what is desired here is nearness of the adult sane person', indicating adulthood is primary.
The hadith cited supports giving precedence to adults, as the Prophet placed a man and an orphan boy equally behind him.
2
Distinguish the secondary criteria within the same age group
Within adults, free persons precede slaves; within boys, free boys precede slave boys. Similarly for women and girls. This is due to the honor of freedom when there is no opposing factor.
The comprehensive list of twelve categories includes these distinctions.
3
Recognize the recommended actions for the congregation
The text lists pressing together (tarassus), filling gaps (sadd al-khalal), and aligning shoulders (musawat al-manakib). These are sunnah and the imam may command them.
The hadith from Ibn Umar emphasizes straightening and not leaving gaps for the devil.
4
Understand the ruling on alignment of feet
The author discusses a case where one foot is aligned and the other is not. He notes that alignment is considered by one foot, but if one foot is forward, there is a difference of opinion among Shafi'is.
This is a nuanced point; the general ruling is that alignment is recommended.

They should complete the rows nearest the imam, then those next, and so on. If the two sides of the imam are equal, the newcomer stands to his right; if the right side is preponderant, he stands to his left. If he finds a gap in the row, he fills it; otherwise he waits until another comes, as we have mentioned. In Fath al-Qadir: Abu Dawud and Imam Ahmad narrated from Ibn 'Umar that he said: 'Straighten the rows, align the shoulders, fill the gaps, and be soft with your hands towards your brothers. Do not leave gaps for the devil. Whoever connects a row by his foot or is slightly behind...' I say: He specified the foot, so that indicates that alignment is considered by one foot, and I did not see it explicitly. The apparent is that if he is leaning on one foot, then the consideration is that foot; if he leans on both feet, then if one is aligned and the other is behind, there is no argument about validity; but if the other is forward, is it valid considering the aligned one or the forward one? That is a point of consideration. I saw disagreement and weighting in the books of the Shafi'is. His statement: 'Let him be near me (laylani)' etc. Al-Ramli said: It is permissible to affirm the ya with fatha and shaddah on the nun, and to drop the ya with kasra on the lam and tashdid on the nun.
Source pages p. 618

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the rulings of row arrangement in congregational prayer. The author begins by explaining the terms 'qurb' (nearness) and 'ahlam' (adults) from the matn, noting that 'ahlam' metaphorically means adults because dreams cause puberty. The author mentions that hermaphrodites are omitted due to rarity, but then provides a detailed twelve-category arrangement from al-Isbijabi's student. The preferable order for rows is: first free adult men, then free boys, then adult male slaves, then boy slaves, then adult male hermaphrodites (free then slave), then female adult hermaphrodites, then free adult women, then free girls, then slave women, then slave girls. However, the author notes that the general rule from the texts is that men always precede boys regardless of free/slave status, because the desired quality is sanity and adulthood. But within the same age group, free persons precede slaves due to the honor of freedom. The author discusses a specific case from the hadith of Anas where the Prophet placed a man and an orphan boy behind him, indicating equality between a man and a boy in a single row, and also that a single woman is placed behind all rows. The passage then gives recommended actions for the congregation: pressing together, aligning shoulders, and filling gaps. The imam may command this. If one finds a gap, he fills it; otherwise he should wait. The author quotes a hadith from Fath al-Qadir about straightening rows. He also discusses the ruling on alignment when one foot is forward or back, noting differing opinions among Shafi'is. Finally, he comments on the phrase 'laylani' from the matn regarding how it is recited.

Key Terms
مناكب (manakib): Shoulders; the part of the body between the neck and arm. The command is to align them in the row.
خلل (khalal): Gaps or empty spaces in the row between worshippers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on straightening the rows and aligning shoulders in congregational prayer?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah (recommended)
C) It is mubah (permissible)
D) It is makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
Row precedence is based first on adulthood, then freedom; straightening rows and filling gaps is sunnah and part of perfecting congregational prayer.

When a Woman Parallel to a Man Invalidates the Prayer
Ruling with proof explaining the Hanafi position via istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's parallelism invalidates a man's prayer and explain the istihsan-based proof that overrides the default qiyas.

Core Idea
If a desirable woman stands parallel to a man in the same row without a barrier and he intended to lead her, his prayer is invalid — an exception by istihsan.

The Hanafi school has a unique ruling regarding women standing alongside men in prayer. While analogy (qiyas) might suggest no invalidation, the school adopts istihsan based on a hadith about an old woman placed behind the row. This lesson unpacks the conditions for the ruling, the internal ikhtilaf with Imam Muhammad, and the juristic reasoning that makes this an exception to the general rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for invalidation
List the five conditions mentioned: the woman must be desirable (mushtahāt), the prayer must be absolute and shared (same start and end times), in a single place, without a barrier, and the man must have intended to lead her.
If any condition is missing, the prayer is not invalidated. For example, if the woman is a mahram or unattractive, or if there is a barrier, the ruling does not apply.
2
Understand the default analogy (qiyas)
The author states 'the analogy is that it should not invalidate' by considering the woman's own prayer (valid when alone) and the case of a beardless youth (amrad) whose parallelism does not invalidate. Recognize that qiyas alone would yield a different ruling.
This sets up the need for istihsan to override the qiyas.
3
Analyze the istihsan proof from the hadith
The istihsan is based on the hadith in Muslim where the Prophet placed an old woman behind the row. The reasoning: if parallelism were not invalidating, she would not have been placed behind the row, because standing alone behind the row is disliked (makruh). She endured a disliked act to avoid a greater harm (invalidation).
This shows that istihsan prioritizes the hadith over the qiyas.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani held that the prayer is not invalidated, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the invalidation position. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that it is invalidated, as preferred by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
The practical implication: a Hanafi mufti will give the fatwa of invalidation.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a congregational prayer where a non-mahram woman accidentally stands to the right of a man in the same row, with no barrier. The man had the intention to lead the congregation. According to the Hanafi position, his prayer becomes invalid (batil). He must repeat the prayer.
Note that the woman's own prayer remains valid; only the man's prayer is affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وإن حاذته مشتهاة في صلاة مطلقة مشتركة تحريمة وإداء في مكان متحد بلا حائل فسدت صلاته أن نوى إمامتها بيان لفائدة تأخيرها ولحكم محاذاتها للرجل، والقياس أن لا تفسد اعتباراً بصلاتها وبمحاذاة الأمرد وجه الاستحسان حديث مسلم السابق من جعل العجوز خلف الصف ولولا أن المحاذاة مفسدة ما تأخرت العجوز لأن الانفراد خلف الصف مكروه فتركه للأفضل لقصد دفع المفنيد أولى. وانظر لما كتبنا في حاشيتنا على العيني.
His statement: 'And if a desirable woman is parallel to him in an absolute, shared prayer with the same beginning and ending, in a single place without a barrier, his prayer becomes invalid if he intended to lead her' – explaining the benefit of delaying her and the ruling of her parallelism with the man. The analogy is that it should not invalidate, considering her prayer and the parallelism of a beardless youth. The istihsan is the previous hadith of Muslim, about placing the old woman behind the row. Were it not that parallelism is invalidating, the old woman would not have delayed, because standing alone behind the row is disliked, so she left that for the superior out of avoiding the corrupting factor, which is more appropriate. Look at what we wrote in our hashya on al-‘Ayni.
Source pages p. 618

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the author's commentary on a matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The ruling states that if a woman who is desirable (i.e., one whom the man is prohibited from looking at due to desire) stands parallel to a man in the same row during a congregational prayer that is identical in start and end time, in a single place without a barrier, then the man's prayer is invalidated if he intended to lead her in prayer. The author explains the benefit of delaying women behind men is to avoid this invalidation. The original analogy would be that her parallelism should not invalidate, by analogy with her own prayer being valid when prayed alone, and by analogy with a beardless youth (amrad) who does not invalidate the prayer if parallel. However, the istihsan (juristic preference) relies on the hadith of Muslim where the Prophet placed the old woman behind the row. The reasoning is that if parallelism were not a cause of invalidation, the old woman would not have been placed behind the row, because praying alone behind the row is disliked (makruh). So she endured a disliked action to avoid the greater evil of invalidation. Thus, the istihsan overrides the analogy. The author refers to his own hashya on al-‘Ayni for further details.

Key Terms
مشتهایة (mushtahāt): A woman who is desirable, i.e., one whom it is unlawful for the man to look at due to desire, typically a non-mahram woman who is attractive.
حاذته (ḥādhat): She stands parallel to him; i.e., her shoulder aligns with his shoulder in the same row.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the old woman in the hadith stand behind the row, even though standing alone is disliked?
A) She was forced to do so
B) To avoid the invalidation of the man's prayer if she stood parallel
C) She was not part of the congregation
D) The row was already full

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that a desirable woman parallel to a man in prayer invalidates his prayer is an exception to qiyas, established by istihsan from the hadith of the old woman placed behind the row.

Preference of First Row and Dispute on Ithar
Discusses the virtue of the first row and the ruling on giving one's place to another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving up one's place in the first row and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Giving up your place in the first row for a scholar is commendable in the Hanafi school, not disliked.

The passage discusses a point of etiquette in congregational prayer: whether one should vacate his spot in the first row for a more deserving person. The Hanafi school, drawing on the general Quranic principle of preferring others, permits and even recommends it, while the Shafi'i school considers it disliked. We will examine the proofs behind each view and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds: it is permissible and even recommended (mustahabb) to give up one's place in the first row if the incoming person is older or more learned.
2
Identify the opponent’s view
The Shafi'i school holds that giving up one's place in the first row is disliked (makruh) because it involves leaving a recommended act without necessity.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument is based on the general rule that leaving a recommended act without a valid reason is disliked; they analogize it to other cases.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by citing the Quranic verse on ithar (59:9) and the principle of respecting elders/scholars, which overrides the general dislike. They also provide practical examples showing the permissibility.
The response is grounded in the general command of preferring others.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, one is encouraged to give his place to a scholar or elder; in the Shafi'i school, such action is disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والقيام في الصف الأول أفضل من الثاني الخ) قال في النهر : واعلم أن الشافعية ذكروا أن الإيثار بالقرب مكروه كما لو كان في الأول فلما أقيمت أثر غيره وقواعدنا لا تأباه لما قد علمت .اهـ. قلت ذكر المؤلف هذه القاعدة في كتابه الأشباه والنظائر وقال : لم أرها الآن لأصحابنا، ونقل فروعاً عن الشافعية قال : ثم رأيت في الهبة من منية المفتي: فقير محتاج دراهم فأراد أن يؤثر الفقراء على نفسه إن علم أنه يصبر على الشدة فالإيثار أفضل وإلا فالإنفاق على نفسه أفضل .اهـ. وفي حاشيتها للسيد الحموي عن المضمرات نقلاً عن النصاب : وإن سبق أ بالدخول إلى المسجد مكانه في الصف الأول فدخل رجل أكبر منه سناً أو أهل علم ينبغي أن يتأخر ويقدمه تعظيماً له اهـ . قال : فهذا مفيد لجواز الإيثار في القرب عملاً بعموم قوله تعالى ويؤثرون على أنفسهم ولو كان بهم خصاصة .
His statement: 'And standing in the first row is better than the second, etc.' He said in al-Nahr: Know that the Shafi'is mentioned that preferring others in proximity (to the imam) is disliked, as if one is in the first row and then gives way to someone else. Our principles do not prohibit it for what you have known. End. I (the author) said: The author mentioned this principle in his book al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and said: 'I have not seen it among our scholars.' And he quoted branches from the Shafi'is. He said: Then I saw in al-Hiba from Munyat al-Mufti: 'A poor man who needs dirhams wanted to prefer the poor over himself; if he knows he can bear hardship, then preference (ithar) is better; otherwise, spending on himself is better.' End. And in its hashya by al-Sayyid al-Hamawi from al-Mudmarat quoting from al-Nisab: 'If someone precedes in entering the mosque and takes his place in the first row, and then a man older or more learned enters, he should move back and let him forward out of respect for him.' He said: This indicates the permissibility of preferring others in proximity, acting on the general verse 'And they prefer others over themselves, even if they are in need.'
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the ruling of isar (giving preference) in the context of the first row in prayer. The author quotes al-Nahr stating that Shafi'is consider it disliked (makruh) to give up one's place in the first row to another person, because it may involve leaving a recommended act. However, the Hanafi position is that it is not disliked, based on their principles. The author supports the Hanafi view by citing his own work al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and then quoting a fatwa from Munyat al-Mufti about a poor man preferring others in charity; this analogy shows that isar is commendable when one can bear the difficulty. Furthermore, a statement from al-Mudmarat via al-Nisab advises that if someone older or more learned arrives, one should give up his place out of respect. The author concludes that this establishes the permissibility of isar in proximity based on the general Quranic principle: 'And they prefer others over themselves, even if they are in need' (Quran 59:9). Thus, the Hanafi school permits giving up one's place in the first row to a more deserving person, unlike the Shafi'i view that it is disliked.

Key Terms
الإيثار (al-īthār): Preferring others over oneself in matters of worldly benefit or worship, based on the Quranic verse.
القرب (al-qurb): Proximity to the imam, i.e., the first row or near the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Remain in his place, as the first row is better
B) Move back and let the man take his place
C) It is disliked to move
D) Only move if the imam asks him

Key Takeaway
Ithar in the first row is a commendable act in the Hanafi school, especially for elders or scholars, based on the Quranic principle of preferring others.
