Ruling on Women Aligning with Men in Prayer: The Proof and Basic Rule
Explains Hanafi ruling on invalidation due to alignment and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman aligning with a man in prayer and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Leaving fard al-maqam by not positioning women behind men invalidates the prayer.

The Hanafi school holds that a woman's alignment with a man in congregational prayer invalidates the man's prayer if she is not behind him. This ruling is derived from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, which the Hanafis treat as an explanation of the Qur'anic degree. In this lesson, we examine the proof and the basic application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman aligning with a man in prayer. Determine the hukm level: the man's prayer becomes fasid (invalid) if he is aligned with her without a barrier. The woman's prayer also becomes invalid if she ignores his gesture to step back.
Note the distinction between imam and non-imam.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Hanafis cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'أخروهن من حيث أخرهن الله' (Delay them from where Allah delayed them). Although Ibn al-Humam considered it mawquf, it is used as a bayan for the mujmal verse 2:228.
The hadith is ahad but serves as an explanation.
3
Understand the usul principle
The imperative 'akhkhiruhunna' indicates wujub in Hanafi usul. Thus, it obligates women to be behind men. If the imam does not enforce this, he leaves fard al-maqam.
4
Distinguish between imam and non-imam
If the man is the imam, his prayer is invalid if he fails to gesture for the woman to step back. If he gestures and she refuses, her prayer becomes invalid, not his. For a non-imam, the same rule applies.
The imam cannot step forward because it is makruh.
5
Note the disagreement with Hanbalis
Imam Ahmad considers the row itself invalidating. Hanafis restrict invalidation to actual alignment without barrier, not mere presence in the row.
This difference has practical consequences in congregational prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
الصف مكروه عندنا ومفسد عند أحمد ولحديث ابن مسعود أخروهن من حيث أخرهن الله والحنفية يذكرونه مرفوعاً. والمحقق ابن الهمام منع رفعه بل هو موقوف على ابن مسعود، وهو يفيد افتراض تأخرهن عن الرجال لأنه وإن كان آحاداً وقع بياناً لمجمل الكتاب وهو قوله تعالى ﴿ وللرجال عليهن درجة ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۸] فإذا لم يشر إليها بالتأخر بعدما دخلت الصلاة ونوى الإمام إمامتها فقد ترك فرض المقام فبطلت صلاته، وإذا أشار إليها بالتأخر فلم تتأخر تركت حينئذ فرض المقام فبطلت صلاتها دونه ولم يمكنه التقدم بخطوة أو خطوتين لأنه مكروه فلا يؤمر به، وهذا هو الفرق بينها وبينه. وهذا في محاذاة غير الإمام، أما في محاذاة إمامها فصلاتهما فاسدة أيضاً لأنه إذا فسدت صلاة الإمام فسدت صلاة المأموم. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : المرأة إذا صلت مع زوجها في البيت إن كان قدمها بحذاء قدم الزوج صلاتهما بالجماعة. وفي المحيط : إذا حاذت إمامها فسدت صلاة الكل. وأما محاذاة الأمرد فقال في فتح القدير: صرح الكل بعدم الفساد إلا من شذ ولا متمسك له في الرواية ما صرحوا به، ولا في الدراية لتصريحهم بأن الفساد في المرأة غير معلول بعروض الشهوة بل لترك فرض المقام، وليس هذا في الصبي، ومن تساهل فعلل به صرح بنفيه في الصبي مدعياً عدم اشتهائه .اهـ. وعلى هذا فما في معراج الدراية عن الملتقط أن من الأمرد من قرنه إلى قدمه عورة مبني على القول الشاذ الذي يلحقه بالمرأة. وذكر الشارح وغيره أن المعتبر في المحاذاة الساق والكعب في الأصح وبعضهم اعتبر القدم .اهـ وهو قاصر الإفادة فإنه كما هو على أنفسهم ولو كان بهم خصاصة [الحشر : ۹] إلا إذا قام دليل تخصيص. قوله: (والحنفية يذكرونه مرفوعاً الخ) قال البلباني في شرح تلخيص الجامع : ذكر هذا الحديث في جامع الأصول وعزاه إلى كتاب رزين بن معاوية العبدري الذي جمع فيه بين الكتب الستة. وإنما عزاه ابن الأثير إليه وإن كان له فيه سند بالإجازة لأنه أشار في كتابه إلى أنه لم يجده في أصوله التي سمعها، وهذا الحديث مشهور مذكور في عامة كتب أصحابنا المصنفة في شرح الجامع الكبير. وذكره الكيا الهراسي في بعض ما تفرد به الإمام أحمد والموفق بن قلامة في المغني وهو وإن كان منقطعاً عند أهل الحديث إلا أن استدلال عامة الفحول من علمائنا والعدول من أصحابنا وفقهائنا مع توفر دواعي المخالفين على رد مثله يرفع وهم من يتوهم ضعفه كيف وإطلاقهم القول بشهرته ظاهر في الدلالة على ثبوته في نفس الأمر وإن انقطع بعد ذلك طريق سنده كما في مستند الإجماع من النصوص اهـ. قوله : (وهو قاصر) أي اعتبار الساق والكعب أو القدم. وفي النهر أقول: لا نسلم أنه قاصر لأن من خلفها إنما تفسد صلاته إذا كان محاذياً لها كما قيد به الشارح، وذكره في السراج أيضاً، وصرح به الحاكم الشهيد في كافية يعني بالساق والكعب. نعم هذا التخصيص يحتاج إلى دليل ومقتضى دليلهم الإطلاق اهـ. أقول: وحاصله أن المحاذاة تتحقق فيمن خلفها أيضاً بأن يكون في الصف الثاني وصرحوا به المرأة الواحدة تفسد صلاة ثلاثة إذا وقفت في الصف من عن يمينها ومن عن يسارها ومن خلفها ولا شك إن المحاذاة بالساق والكعب لم تتحقق فيمن خلفها فالتفسير الصحيح للمحاذاة ما في المجتبى والمحاذاة المفسدة أن تقوم بجنب الرجل من غير حائل أو قدامه اهـ. فالحاصل أن مماسة بدنها لبدنه ليست بشرط بل أن تكون عن جنبه بلا حائل ولا فرجة، وسيأتي تفسير الحائل والفرجة ولهذا لو كان أحدهما على الدكان دون القامة والآخر على الأرض فسدت صلاته لوجود المحاذاة لبعض بدنها لكونها عن جنبه، وليس هنا محاذاة بالساق والكعب ولا بالقدم وفي الخانية والظهيرية : المرأة إذا صلت في بيتها مع زوجها إن كانت قدماها خلف قدم الزوج إلا أنها طويلة يقع رأسها في السجود قبل رأس الإمام جازت صلاتهما لأن العبرة للقدم اهـ . وقال قاضيخان في باب ما يفسد الصلاة وحد المحاذاة أن يحاذي عضو منها عضواً من الرجل حتى لو كانت المرأة على الظلة والرجل بحذائها أسفل منها أو خلفها إن كان يحاذي الرجل شيئاً منها تفسد صلاته وقيد بالمشتهاة لأن غير المشتهاة لا تفسد صلاته وإن هذا هذا الآخر وهو مسامتاً لها بالساق والكعب أي غير منحرف عن يمنة أو يسرة، فلو كان خلفها لكنه منحرف يمنة أو يسرة لم يكن محاذياً لها بالساق والكعب فلا تفسد صلاته في الأصح لوجود الفرجة بذلك الانحراف، وهذا المعنى سيذكره المؤلف توفيقاً بين كلامهم كما سننبه عليه قوله : (وفي الخانية والظهيرية الخ) مبني على أن المراد بالمحاذاة القدم فقط كما هو مصرح به في آخر العبارة، وما ذكره بعده عن قاضيخان محمول عليه أيضاً. قال في السراج عن النهاية : نص في فتاوى قاضيخان أن المراد بقوله أن يحاذي عضواً منها هو قدمها لا غيرها فإن محاذاة غير قدمها لشيء من الرجل لا توجب فساد صلاته اهـ . لكنه لا يناسبه التفريع عليه بقوله حتى لو كانت الخ. بل الظاهر أنه مبني على القول الفساد بمحاذاة أي عضو منها لا بقيد كونه الساق والكعب يدل عليه قوله في المعراج : شرطنا المحاذاة مطلقاً ليتناول كل الأعضاء وبعضها فإنه ذكر أبو علي النسفي المحاذاة أن يحاذي عضواً منها عضو منه حتى لو كانت المرأة على الظلة ورجل بحذائها أسفل منها إن كان يحاذي الرجل شيء منها تفسد صلاة الرجل .اهـ لكن قال في النهاية بعد نقله ذلك : وإنما عين هذه الصورة لتكون قدم المرأة محاذية للرجل لأن المراد بقوله أن يحاذي عضواً منها هو قدم المرأة لا غيرها فإن محاذاة غير قدمها لشيء من الرجل لا يوجب فساد صلاة الرجل. نص على هذا في فتاوى الإمام قاضيخان في أواسط فصل من يصح يصح وقال : المرأة إذا صلت مع زوجها في البيت الخ. به و من فهذا صريح في أن إطلاق العضو غير مراد خلافاً لما فهمه المؤلف ونقل في السراج كلام النهاية وأقره، وبه علم أن ما نقله المؤلف ثانياً عن قاضيخان أيضاً من قوله وحد المحاذاة الخ» محمول على هذا أيضاً بدليل الصورة التي ذكرها فإن تعيين هذه الصورة دليل على أن المراد بعضو المرأة القدم لا غير كما قاله صاحب النهاية والله اعلم قوله : (لأن العبرة للقدم أي وهي هنا غير محاذية بسبب الاقتداء لا
Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. The row is disliked (makruh) according to us and invalidating according to Ahmad, and due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Delay them from where Allah delayed them.' The Hanafis mention it as marfu'. The investigator Ibn al-Humam denied its raising; rather it is mawquf on Ibn Mas'ud. It indicates the obligation of women being behind men because, although it is ahad, it is an explanation (bayan) of the mujmal of the Book, which is His saying, 'And for men is a degree over them' [2:228]. So if he does not gesture to her to delay after entering the prayer and intends to lead her, he has left the fard of position, so his prayer is invalid. If he gestures to her to delay and she does not delay, then she leaves the fard of position, so her prayer is invalid but not his, and he cannot step forward one or two steps because it is makruh, so he is not commanded to do so. This is the distinction between her and him. This is regarding alignment (muhadha) with someone other than the imam. As for alignment with her imam, the prayer of both is invalid because if the imam's prayer is invalid, the prayer of the follower is invalid. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a woman prays with her husband in the house, if her foot is parallel to her husband's foot, their congregational prayer is valid. In al-Muhit: If she aligns with her imam, the prayer of all is invalid. As for alignment with an amrad (beardless youth), in Fath al-Qadir: They all explicitly state there is no invalidation except from an anomalous opinion, and there is no support for it in riwaya or diraya because they explicitly state that invalidation in a woman is not caused by arousal of desire but by leaving the fard of position, and this is not the case for a boy. Whoever is lenient and causal about it, he explicitly negates it for the boy, claiming he does not desire [women]. End quote. Therefore, what is in Mi'raj al-Diraya from al-Multaqat that from the amrad his head to his foot is 'awra is based on the anomalous opinion that joins him to a woman. The commentator and others mentioned that the valid consideration in alignment is the shin and ankle in the most correct view, and some considered the foot. End quote. And it is deficient in benefit, as it is according to themselves even if they have privation [59:9] unless evidence for specification exists. His statement: (And the Hanafis mention it as marfu' etc.) Al-Bulbani said in Sharh Talkhis al-Jami': This hadith is mentioned in Jami' al-Usul and attributed to the book of Razin ibn Mu'awiya al-Abdari who compiled the six books. Ibn al-Athir attributed it to him because he indicated in his book that he did not find it in his fundamentals which he heard; this hadith is famous and mentioned in most of our companions' books composed in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir. Al-Kiya al-Harasi mentioned it in some things unique to Imam Ahmad, and al-Muwaffaq ibn Qudama in al-Mughni. Although it is disconnected (munqati') according to hadith scholars, the deduction of the general giants of our scholars and the just among our companions and jurists, despite the abundant motives of opponents to reject the likes of it, removes the suspicion of those who suspect its weakness. How can it be that their absolute statement of its fame is apparent evidence of its authenticity in reality even if after that the path of its chain is disconnected, as in the basis of ijma from texts. End quote. His statement: (and it is deficient) meaning considering the shin and ankle or foot. In al-Nahr: I say: we do not concede that it is deficient because the one behind her only has his prayer invalid if he is aligned with her as the commentator restricted, and mentioned it in al-Siraj, and al-Hakim al-Shahid explicitly stated it in al-Kafiya, meaning by shin and ankle. Yes, this specification needs evidence, and the implication of their evidence is absolute. End quote. I say: The summary is that alignment can occur with the one behind her also by being in the second row, and they explicitly stated that a single woman invalidates the prayer of three: the one on her right, the one on her left, and the one behind her. There is no doubt that alignment by shin and ankle is not realized for the one behind her. So the correct interpretation of alignment is what is in al-Mujtaba: invalidating alignment is that she stands next to the man without a barrier or in front of him. End quote. The bottom line is that body contact with his body is not a condition, but rather that she be by his side without a barrier or gap. The interpretation of barrier and gap will come. So if one of them is on a platform less than a cubit and the other on the ground, his prayer is invalid due to the existence of alignment of some of her body because she is by his side, and here there is no alignment by shin and ankle nor by foot. In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya: A woman if she prays in her house with her husband, if her feet are behind her husband's feet, but she is tall so her head falls in prostration before the imam's head, their prayer is valid because the criterion is the foot. End quote. And Qadikhan said in the chapter on what invalidates prayer: The limit of alignment is that any limb of hers aligns with any limb of the man, even if the woman is on a balcony and the man is parallel to her below her or behind her, if any part of her aligns with the man, his prayer is invalid. And he restricted it to a desirable woman, because a non-desirable woman does not invalidate his prayer. And this, this, the other, and it is aligned with her by shin and ankle, i.e., not deviating right or left. So if he is behind her but deviating right or left, he is not aligned with her by shin and ankle, so his prayer is not invalid in the more correct view due to the existence of a gap by that deviation. This meaning will be mentioned by the author reconciling between their statements as we will point out. His statement: (In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya etc.) is based on the meaning that the intended meaning of alignment is only the foot, as explicitly stated in the end of the expression. What he mentioned after that from Qadikhan is also interpreted accordingly. He said in al-Siraj from al-Nihaya: The text in Fatawa Qadikhan states that the meaning of his statement 'any limb of hers aligns' is her foot, not other, because alignment of other than her foot with something of the man does not necessitate invalidation of his prayer. End quote. But the derivation based on his statement 'even if...' does not suit it. Rather, apparently it is based on the opinion of invalidation by alignment of any limb of hers without the restriction of shin and ankle, as indicated by his statement in al-Mi'raj: We made the condition of alignment absolute to include all limbs and some of them. Abu Ali al-Nasafi mentioned alignment: that any limb of hers aligns with a limb of his, so if the woman is on a balcony and a man is parallel to her below her, if any part of her aligns with the man, the man's prayer is invalid. End quote. But he said in al-Nihaya after quoting that: He only specified this image so that the woman's foot is aligned with the man, because the meaning of his statement 'any limb of hers' is the woman's foot, nothing else, because alignment of other than her foot with something of the man does not necessitate invalidation of the man's prayer. This is textually stated in Fatawa of Imam Qadikhan in the middle of the chapter on who is valid to lead, and he said: The woman if she prays with her husband in the house etc. with it and from it. So this is explicit that the absolute limb is not intended, contrary to what the author understood. And he quoted in al-Siraj the statement of al-Nihaya and approved it. By this it is known that what the author quoted secondly from Qadikhan also, from his statement 'the limit of alignment etc.' is also interpreted in this way, as evidence of the image he mentioned, because specifying this image is evidence that the intended part of the woman is the foot only, as the author of al-Nihaya said. And Allah knows best. His statement: (because the criterion is the foot) meaning here it is not aligned due to the act of iqtida, not.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the ruling on a woman aligning (muhadha) with a man in congregational prayer. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining textual evidence and legal reasoning. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi position: a woman standing in the same row as men is makruh (disliked) according to the Hanafis, but invalidates the prayer according to Imam Ahmad. The Hanafis cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, 'Delay them from where Allah delayed them.' While the hadith is often considered marfu' (raised to the Prophet) by Hanafis, Ibn al-Humam argued it is mawquf (a saying of Ibn Mas'ud). Nevertheless, it serves as a bayan (explanation) of the Qur'anic verse 'For men is a degree over them,' indicating that women must be behind men. The ruling: if the imam intends to lead a woman and does not gesture for her to step back, his prayer becomes invalid because he has left the fard of position (fard al-maqam). If he gestures and she does not comply, her prayer is invalid but his remains valid. This applies when the woman aligns with a man other than the imam. If she aligns with the imam himself, both prayers are invalid because when the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's is as well. The passage then contrasts this with a scenario from Fatawa Qadikhan: if a woman's foot is parallel to her husband's foot in a home prayer, their congregation is valid. Later, the author discusses the definition of muhadha. The most correct view is that alignment occurs when the woman's shin and ankle are aligned with the man's, though some say only the foot. This is challenged by citing that a woman in the second row can invalidate the prayers of three men (right, left, behind), even though alignment by shin and ankle is not present. Thus, the correct definition, as in al-Mujtaba, is that invalidating alignment occurs when the woman stands side by side with a man without a barrier or in front of him. The condition of physical contact is not required; simply being next to him without a gap suffices. The passage then addresses the amrad (beardless youth): the majority rule no invalidation if he aligns with a woman, because the invalidation for a woman is due to leaving fard al-maqam, not desire. A stray opinion that treats him as a woman is rejected. Finally, the discussion reconciles different definitions of alignment, noting that the foot is the criterion in some works, but the more reliable position is that any limb can cause invalidation if it leads to desire, though the text emphasizes that the primary cause is the duty of positioning. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that alignment with a non-mahram woman invalidates the prayer, with the condition that the woman is desirable (mashuta).

Key Terms
محاذاة (muḥādha): Alignment: a woman standing beside or in front of a man in prayer without a barrier, causing invalidation.
فرض المقام (farḍ al-maqām): Obligatory positioning: the duty of men to lead and women to be behind in congregational prayer.
مشتهاة (mushtāhā): Desirable woman: one whom men normally desire, as opposed to an old or unattractive woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basic ruling when a woman aligns with a man in prayer without a barrier?
A) The man's prayer is valid but makruh.
B) The man's prayer is invalid (fasid).
C) The woman's prayer is always invalid.
D) Both prayers are valid as long as she is behind him.

Key Takeaway
The prayer of a man becomes invalid if a woman aligns with him without a barrier, due to leaving the obligatory positioning (fard al-maqam).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Muhadha: Intra-Hanafi Differences and the Relied-Upon View
Examines the definition of muhadha and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the different definitions of muhadha (alignment) within the Hanafi school and explain the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi definition of alignment is standing side-by-side without a barrier or gap, not a specific limb.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a notable difference of opinion on what exactly constitutes invalidating alignment. Some scholars restrict it to the foot, others to the shin and ankle, and some to any limb. This lesson examines these views and the reconciliation that the criterion is being next to the man without any barrier, as stated in al-Mujtaba.

Guided Path
1
List the different definitions
Three main definitions: (1) the foot only, (2) the shin and ankle (al-ashah), (3) any limb of the woman aligning with any limb of the man. Also, the definition in al-Mujtaba: standing next to the man without a barrier or in front of him.
Each definition has textual support in Hanafi works.
2
Examine the evidence for each
The foot-only view is based on statements from Qadikhan and al-Nihaya. The shin/ankle view is called al-ashah by many. The any-limb view is found in al-Mi'raj and attributed to Abu Ali al-Nasafi.
3
Understand the reconciliation
The definition in al-Mujtaba (side-by-side without barrier) reconciles these by focusing on the spatial relationship rather than a specific limb. This also accounts for cases like a woman in the second row.
4
Apply to problematic cases
If a woman is on a balcony and a man below, or if she is in the second row directly behind a man, does alignment occur? The side-by-side definition explains these cases.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that invalidating alignment occurs when a desirable woman stands next to a non-mahram man without a barrier or gap, regardless of which limb touches.

الصف مكروه عندنا ومفسد عند أحمد ولحديث ابن مسعود أخروهن من حيث أخرهن الله والحنفية يذكرونه مرفوعاً. والمحقق ابن الهمام منع رفعه بل هو موقوف على ابن مسعود، وهو يفيد افتراض تأخرهن عن الرجال لأنه وإن كان أيضاً. قال في السراج عن النهاية : نص في فتاوى قاضيخان أن المراد بقوله أن يحاذي عضواً منها هو قدمها لا غيرها فإن محاذاة غير قدمها لشيء من الرجل لا توجب فساد صلاته اهـ . لكنه لا يناسبه التفريع عليه بقوله حتى لو كانت الخ. بل الظاهر أنه مبني على القول الفساد بمحاذاة أي عضو منها لا بقيد كونه الساق والكعب يدل عليه قوله في المعراج : شرطنا المحاذاة مطلقاً ليتناول كل الأعضاء وبعضها فإنه ذكر أبو علي النسفي المحاذاة أن يحاذي عضواً منها عضو منه حتى لو كانت المرأة على الظلة ورجل بحذائها أسفل منها إن كان يحاذي الرجل شيء منها تفسد صلاة الرجل .اهـ لكن قال في النهاية بعد نقله ذلك : وإنما عين هذه الصورة لتكون قدم المرأة محاذية للرجل لأن المراد بقوله أن يحاذي عضواً منها هو قدم المرأة لا غيرها فإن محاذاة غير قدمها لشيء من الرجل لا يوجب فساد صلاة الرجل. نص على هذا في فتاوى الإمام قاضيخان في أواسط فصل من يصح يصح وقال : المرأة إذا صلت مع زوجها في البيت الخ. به و من فهذا صريح في أن إطلاق العضو غير مراد خلافاً لما فهمه المؤلف ونقل في السراج كلام النهاية وأقره، وبه علم أن ما نقله المؤلف ثانياً عن قاضيخان أيضاً من قوله وحد المحاذاة الخ» محمول على هذا أيضاً بدليل الصورة التي ذكرها فإن تعيين هذه الصورة دليل على أن المراد بعضو المرأة القدم لا غير كما قاله صاحب النهاية والله اعلم قوله : (لأن العبرة للقدم أي وهي هنا غير محاذية بسبب الاقتداء لا
Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. The row is disliked (makruh) according to us and invalidating according to Ahmad, and due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Delay them from where Allah delayed them.' The Hanafis mention it as marfu'. The investigator Ibn al-Humam denied its raising; rather it is mawquf on Ibn Mas'ud. It indicates the obligation of women being behind men because, although it is ahad, it is an explanation (bayan) of the mujmal of the Book, which is His saying, 'And for men is a degree over them' [2:228]. So if he does not gesture to her to delay after entering the prayer and intends to lead her, he has left the fard of position, so his prayer is invalid. If he gestures to her to delay and she does not delay, then she leaves the fard of position, so her prayer is invalid but not his, and he cannot step forward one or two steps because it is makruh, so he is not commanded to do so. This is the distinction between her and him. This is regarding alignment (muhadha) with someone other than the imam. As for alignment with her imam, the prayer of both is invalid because if the imam's prayer is invalid, the prayer of the follower is invalid. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a woman prays with her husband in the house, if her foot is parallel to her husband's foot, their congregational prayer is valid. In al-Muhit: If she aligns with her imam, the prayer of all is invalid. As for alignment with an amrad (beardless youth), in Fath al-Qadir: They all explicitly state there is no invalidation except from an anomalous opinion, and there is no support for it in riwaya or diraya because they explicitly state that invalidation in a woman is not caused by arousal of desire but by leaving the fard of position, and this is not the case for a boy. Whoever is lenient and causal about it, he explicitly negates it for the boy, claiming he does not desire [women]. End quote. Therefore, what is in Mi'raj al-Diraya from al-Multaqat that from the amrad his head to his foot is 'awra is based on the anomalous opinion that joins him to a woman. The commentator and others mentioned that the valid consideration in alignment is the shin and ankle in the most correct view, and some considered the foot. End quote. And it is deficient in benefit, as it is according to themselves even if they have privation [59:9] unless evidence for specification exists. His statement: (And the Hanafis mention it as marfu' etc.) Al-Bulbani said in Sharh Talkhis al-Jami': This hadith is mentioned in Jami' al-Usul and attributed to the book of Razin ibn Mu'awiya al-Abdari who compiled the six books. Ibn al-Athir attributed it to him because he indicated in his book that he did not find it in his fundamentals which he heard; this hadith is famous and mentioned in most of our companions' books composed in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir. Al-Kiya al-Harasi mentioned it in some things unique to Imam Ahmad, and al-Muwaffaq ibn Qudama in al-Mughni. Although it is disconnected (munqati') according to hadith scholars, the deduction of the general giants of our scholars and the just among our companions and jurists, despite the abundant motives of opponents to reject the likes of it, removes the suspicion of those who suspect its weakness. How can it be that their absolute statement of its fame is apparent evidence of its authenticity in reality even if after that the path of its chain is disconnected, as in the basis of ijma from texts. End quote. His statement: (and it is deficient) meaning considering the shin and ankle or foot. In al-Nahr: I say: we do not concede that it is deficient because the one behind her only has his prayer invalid if he is aligned with her as the commentator restricted, and mentioned it in al-Siraj, and al-Hakim al-Shahid explicitly stated it in al-Kafiya, meaning by shin and ankle. Yes, this specification needs evidence, and the implication of their evidence is absolute. End quote. I say: The summary is that alignment can occur with the one behind her also by being in the second row, and they explicitly stated that a single woman invalidates the prayer of three: the one on her right, the one on her left, and the one behind her. There is no doubt that alignment by shin and ankle is not realized for the one behind her. So the correct interpretation of alignment is what is in al-Mujtaba: invalidating alignment is that she stands next to the man without a barrier or in front of him. End quote. The bottom line is that body contact with his body is not a condition, but rather that she be by his side without a barrier or gap. The interpretation of barrier and gap will come. So if one of them is on a platform less than a cubit and the other on the ground, his prayer is invalid due to the existence of alignment of some of her body because she is by his side, and here there is no alignment by shin and ankle nor by foot. In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya: A woman if she prays in her house with her husband, if her feet are behind her husband's feet, but she is tall so her head falls in prostration before the imam's head, their prayer is valid because the criterion is the foot. End quote. And Qadikhan said in the chapter on what invalidates prayer: The limit of alignment is that any limb of hers aligns with any limb of the man, even if the woman is on a balcony and the man is parallel to her below her or behind her, if any part of her aligns with the man, his prayer is invalid. And he restricted it to a desirable woman, because a non-desirable woman does not invalidate his prayer. And this, this, the other, and it is aligned with her by shin and ankle, i.e., not deviating right or left. So if he is behind her but deviating right or left, he is not aligned with her by shin and ankle, so his prayer is not invalid in the more correct view due to the existence of a gap by that deviation. This meaning will be mentioned by the author reconciling between their statements as we will point out. His statement: (In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya etc.) is based on the meaning that the intended meaning of alignment is only the foot, as explicitly stated in the end of the expression. What he mentioned after that from Qadikhan is also interpreted accordingly. He said in al-Siraj from al-Nihaya: The text in Fatawa Qadikhan states that the meaning of his statement 'any limb of hers aligns' is her foot, not other, because alignment of other than her foot with something of the man does not necessitate invalidation of his prayer. End quote. But the derivation based on his statement 'even if...' does not suit it. Rather, apparently it is based on the opinion of invalidation by alignment of any limb of hers without the restriction of shin and ankle, as indicated by his statement in al-Mi'raj: We made the condition of alignment absolute to include all limbs and some of them. Abu Ali al-Nasafi mentioned alignment: that any limb of hers aligns with a limb of his, so if the woman is on a balcony and a man is parallel to her below her, if any part of her aligns with the man, the man's prayer is invalid. End quote. But he said in al-Nihaya after quoting that: He only specified this image so that the woman's foot is aligned with the man, because the meaning of his statement 'any limb of hers' is the woman's foot, nothing else, because alignment of other than her foot with something of the man does not necessitate invalidation of the man's prayer. This is textually stated in Fatawa of Imam Qadikhan in the middle of the chapter on who is valid to lead, and he said: The woman if she prays with her husband in the house etc. with it and from it. So this is explicit that the absolute limb is not intended, contrary to what the author understood. And he quoted in al-Siraj the statement of al-Nihaya and approved it. By this it is known that what the author quoted secondly from Qadikhan also, from his statement 'the limit of alignment etc.' is also interpreted in this way, as evidence of the image he mentioned, because specifying this image is evidence that the intended part of the woman is the foot only, as the author of al-Nihaya said. And Allah knows best. His statement: (because the criterion is the foot) meaning here it is not aligned due to the act of iqtida, not.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the ruling on a woman aligning (muhadha) with a man in congregational prayer. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining textual evidence and legal reasoning. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi position: a woman standing in the same row as men is makruh (disliked) according to the Hanafis, but invalidates the prayer according to Imam Ahmad. The Hanafis cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, 'Delay them from where Allah delayed them.' While the hadith is often considered marfu' (raised to the Prophet) by Hanafis, Ibn al-Humam argued it is mawquf (a saying of Ibn Mas'ud). Nevertheless, it serves as a bayan (explanation) of the Qur'anic verse 'For men is a degree over them,' indicating that women must be behind men. The ruling: if the imam intends to lead a woman and does not gesture for her to step back, his prayer becomes invalid because he has left the fard of position (fard al-maqam). If he gestures and she does not comply, her prayer is invalid but his remains valid. This applies when the woman aligns with a man other than the imam. If she aligns with the imam himself, both prayers are invalid because when the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's is as well. The passage then contrasts this with a scenario from Fatawa Qadikhan: if a woman's foot is parallel to her husband's foot in a home prayer, their congregation is valid. Later, the author discusses the definition of muhadha. The most correct view is that alignment occurs when the woman's shin and ankle are aligned with the man's, though some say only the foot. This is challenged by citing that a woman in the second row can invalidate the prayers of three men (right, left, behind), even though alignment by shin and ankle is not present. Thus, the correct definition, as in al-Mujtaba, is that invalidating alignment occurs when the woman stands side by side with a man without a barrier or in front of him. The condition of physical contact is not required; simply being next to him without a gap suffices. The passage then addresses the amrad (beardless youth): the majority rule no invalidation if he aligns with a woman, because the invalidation for a woman is due to leaving fard al-maqam, not desire. A stray opinion that treats him as a woman is rejected. Finally, the discussion reconciles different definitions of alignment, noting that the foot is the criterion in some works, but the more reliable position is that any limb can cause invalidation if it leads to desire, though the text emphasizes that the primary cause is the duty of positioning. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that alignment with a non-mahram woman invalidates the prayer, with the condition that the woman is desirable (mashuta).

Key Terms
محاذاة (muḥādha): Alignment: a woman standing beside or in front of a man in prayer without a barrier, causing invalidation.
حائل (hā'il): Barrier: something that prevents direct physical line-of-sight or presence, e.g., a wall, curtain, or gap.
فرجة (furja): Gap: a space between the woman and man that prevents alignment, e.g., an empty seat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view (al-Mujtaba), what constitutes invalidating alignment?
A) The woman's foot aligns with the man's foot.
B) The woman stands next to the man without barrier or in front of him.
C) The woman's shin and ankle touch the man's shin and ankle.
D) The woman's any limb aligns with the man's any limb.

Key Takeaway
The correct definition of invalidating alignment is standing next to a non-mahram man without a barrier or in front of him, regardless of specific limb.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Special Cases: Amrad, Desirable Woman, and Multi-Row Scenarios
Covers special cases: amrad, desirable woman, and second row

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on alignment to special cases including the amrad (beardless youth), non-desirable women, and the scenario of a woman in the second row.

Core Idea
Invalidation is not caused by desire but by leaving fard al-maqam; hence an amrad does not cause invalidation.

The Hanafi ruling on alignment includes refinements: it applies only to desirable women (mushtāhā), and an amrad (beardless youth) does not cause invalidation because the cause is not desire. Additionally, a woman in the second row can invalidate the prayers of three men. This lesson covers these nuanced cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of desirability
The text restricts invalidation to a desirable woman. Why? Because the invalidation is due to leaving fard al-maqam, not desire. Non-desirable women are excluded because the ruling is tied to typical cases.
Some texts do not make this restriction.
2
Apply to amrad
A beardless youth does not cause invalidation because he is not a woman. The anomalous opinion to the contrary is rejected because the cause is not desire.
3
Analyze the second row scenario
A woman in the second row can invalidate the prayers of three men: the one on her right, left, and behind. This shows that alignment is not limited to being side-by-side in the same row.
This supports the side-by-side definition.
4
Determine the ruling for the woman behind the imam
If she aligns with the imam, both prayers are invalid. If she is in the second row behind a non-imam, only the man behind her may be affected if alignment is considered.
5
Synthesize the overall mufta bihi
State the complete ruling: a desirable woman's alignment with a non-mahram man without barrier invalidates his prayer. For an amrad, no invalidation.

Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. The row is disliked (makruh) according to us and invalidating according to Ahmad, and due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Delay them from where Allah delayed them.' The Hanafis mention it as marfu'. The investigator Ibn al-Humam denied its raising; rather it is mawquf on Ibn Mas'ud. It indicates the obligation of women being behind men because, although it is ahad, it is an explanation (bayan) of the mujmal of the Book, which is His saying, 'And for men is a degree over them' [2:228]. So if he does not gesture to her to delay after entering the prayer and intends to lead her, he has left the fard of position, so his prayer is invalid. If he gestures to her to delay and she does not delay, then she leaves the fard of position, so her prayer is invalid but not his, and he cannot step forward one or two steps because it is makruh, so he is not commanded to do so. This is the distinction between her and him. This is regarding alignment (muhadha) with someone other than the imam. As for alignment with her imam, the prayer of both is invalid because if the imam's prayer is invalid, the prayer of the follower is invalid. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a woman prays with her husband in the house, if her foot is parallel to her husband's foot, their congregational prayer is valid. In al-Muhit: If she aligns with her imam, the prayer of all is invalid. As for alignment with an amrad (beardless youth), in Fath al-Qadir: They all explicitly state there is no invalidation except from an anomalous opinion, and there is no support for it in riwaya or diraya because they explicitly state that invalidation in a woman is not caused by arousal of desire but by leaving the fard of position, and this is not the case for a boy. Whoever is lenient and causal about it, he explicitly negates it for the boy, claiming he does not desire [women]. End quote. Therefore, what is in Mi'raj al-Diraya from al-Multaqat that from the amrad his head to his foot is 'awra is based on the anomalous opinion that joins him to a woman. The commentator and others mentioned that the valid consideration in alignment is the shin and ankle in the most correct view, and some considered the foot. End quote. And it is deficient in benefit, as it is according to themselves even if they have privation [59:9] unless evidence for specification exists. His statement: (And the Hanafis mention it as marfu' etc.) Al-Bulbani said in Sharh Talkhis al-Jami': This hadith is mentioned in Jami' al-Usul and attributed to the book of Razin ibn Mu'awiya al-Abdari who compiled the six books. Ibn al-Athir attributed it to him because he indicated in his book that he did not find it in his fundamentals which he heard; this hadith is famous and mentioned in most of our companions' books composed in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir. Al-Kiya al-Harasi mentioned it in some things unique to Imam Ahmad, and al-Muwaffaq ibn Qudama in al-Mughni. Although it is disconnected (munqati') according to hadith scholars, the deduction of the general giants of our scholars and the just among our companions and jurists, despite the abundant motives of opponents to reject the likes of it, removes the suspicion of those who suspect its weakness. How can it be that their absolute statement of its fame is apparent evidence of its authenticity in reality even if after that the path of its chain is disconnected, as in the basis of ijma from texts. End quote. His statement: (and it is deficient) meaning considering the shin and ankle or foot. In al-Nahr: I say: we do not concede that it is deficient because the one behind her only has his prayer invalid if he is aligned with her as the commentator restricted, and mentioned it in al-Siraj, and al-Hakim al-Shahid explicitly stated it in al-Kafiya, meaning by shin and ankle. Yes, this specification needs evidence, and the implication of their evidence is absolute. End quote. I say: The summary is that alignment can occur with the one behind her also by being in the second row, and they explicitly stated that a single woman invalidates the prayer of three: the one on her right, the one on her left, and the one behind her. There is no doubt that alignment by shin and ankle is not realized for the one behind her. So the correct interpretation of alignment is what is in al-Mujtaba: invalidating alignment is that she stands next to the man without a barrier or in front of him. End quote. The bottom line is that body contact with his body is not a condition, but rather that she be by his side without a barrier or gap. The interpretation of barrier and gap will come. So if one of them is on a platform less than a cubit and the other on the ground, his prayer is invalid due to the existence of alignment of some of her body because she is by his side, and here there is no alignment by shin and ankle nor by foot. In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya: A woman if she prays in her house with her husband, if her feet are behind her husband's feet, but she is tall so her head falls in prostration before the imam's head, their prayer is valid because the criterion is the foot. End quote. And Qadikhan said in the chapter on what invalidates prayer: The limit of alignment is that any limb of hers aligns with any limb of the man, even if the woman is on a balcony and the man is parallel to her below her or behind her, if any part of her aligns with the man, his prayer is invalid. And he restricted it to a desirable woman, because a non-desirable woman does not invalidate his prayer. And this, this, the other, and it is aligned with her by shin and ankle, i.e., not deviating right or left. So if he is behind her but deviating right or left, he is not aligned with her by shin and ankle, so his prayer is not invalid in the more correct view due to the existence of a gap by that deviation. This meaning will be mentioned by the author reconciling between their statements as we will point out. His statement: (In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya etc.) is based on the meaning that the intended meaning of alignment is only the foot, as explicitly stated in the end of the expression. What he mentioned after that from Qadikhan is also interpreted accordingly. He said in al-Siraj from al-Nihaya: The text in Fatawa Qadikhan states that the meaning of his statement 'any limb of hers aligns' is her foot, not other, because alignment of other than her foot with something of the man does not necessitate invalidation of his prayer. End quote. But the derivation based on his statement 'even if...' does not suit it. Rather, apparently it is based on the opinion of invalidation by alignment of any limb of hers without the restriction of shin and ankle, as indicated by his statement in al-Mi'raj: We made the condition of alignment absolute to include all limbs and some of them. Abu Ali al-Nasafi mentioned alignment: that any limb of hers aligns with a limb of his, so if the woman is on a balcony and a man is parallel to her below her, if any part of her aligns with the man, the man's prayer is invalid. End quote. But he said in al-Nihaya after quoting that: He only specified this image so that the woman's foot is aligned with the man, because the meaning of his statement 'any limb of hers' is the woman's foot, nothing else, because alignment of other than her foot with something of the man does not necessitate invalidation of the man's prayer. This is textually stated in Fatawa of Imam Qadikhan in the middle of the chapter on who is valid to lead, and he said: The woman if she prays with her husband in the house etc. with it and from it. So this is explicit that the absolute limb is not intended, contrary to what the author understood. And he quoted in al-Siraj the statement of al-Nihaya and approved it. By this it is known that what the author quoted secondly from Qadikhan also, from his statement 'the limit of alignment etc.' is also interpreted in this way, as evidence of the image he mentioned, because specifying this image is evidence that the intended part of the woman is the foot only, as the author of al-Nihaya said. And Allah knows best. His statement: (because the criterion is the foot) meaning here it is not aligned due to the act of iqtida, not.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the ruling on a woman aligning (muhadha) with a man in congregational prayer. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining textual evidence and legal reasoning. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi position: a woman standing in the same row as men is makruh (disliked) according to the Hanafis, but invalidates the prayer according to Imam Ahmad. The Hanafis cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, 'Delay them from where Allah delayed them.' While the hadith is often considered marfu' (raised to the Prophet) by Hanafis, Ibn al-Humam argued it is mawquf (a saying of Ibn Mas'ud). Nevertheless, it serves as a bayan (explanation) of the Qur'anic verse 'For men is a degree over them,' indicating that women must be behind men. The ruling: if the imam intends to lead a woman and does not gesture for her to step back, his prayer becomes invalid because he has left the fard of position (fard al-maqam). If he gestures and she does not comply, her prayer is invalid but his remains valid. This applies when the woman aligns with a man other than the imam. If she aligns with the imam himself, both prayers are invalid because when the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's is as well. The passage then contrasts this with a scenario from Fatawa Qadikhan: if a woman's foot is parallel to her husband's foot in a home prayer, their congregation is valid. Later, the author discusses the definition of muhadha. The most correct view is that alignment occurs when the woman's shin and ankle are aligned with the man's, though some say only the foot. This is challenged by citing that a woman in the second row can invalidate the prayers of three men (right, left, behind), even though alignment by shin and ankle is not present. Thus, the correct definition, as in al-Mujtaba, is that invalidating alignment occurs when the woman stands side by side with a man without a barrier or in front of him. The condition of physical contact is not required; simply being next to him without a gap suffices. The passage then addresses the amrad (beardless youth): the majority rule no invalidation if he aligns with a woman, because the invalidation for a woman is due to leaving fard al-maqam, not desire. A stray opinion that treats him as a woman is rejected. Finally, the discussion reconciles different definitions of alignment, noting that the foot is the criterion in some works, but the more reliable position is that any limb can cause invalidation if it leads to desire, though the text emphasizes that the primary cause is the duty of positioning. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that alignment with a non-mahram woman invalidates the prayer, with the condition that the woman is desirable (mashuta).

Key Terms
أمرد (amrad): Beardless youth, typically a male who has not yet grown a beard, often considered an object of desire in some contexts.
مشتهاة (mushtāhā): Desirable woman: one whom men normally desire, as opposed to an old or unattractive woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does a woman aligning with an amrad (beardless youth) invalidate the prayer?
A) Yes, because he is desired.
B) No, because invalidation is specific to women.
C) Yes, if he is above the age of puberty.
D) No, unless she is desirable.

Key Takeaway
Invalidation due to alignment applies only to desirable women, not to amrad, because the cause is leaving fard al-maqam, not desire.

Ruling on Woman's Adjacency in Prayer: Invalidates Three Men
Defines invalidating adjacency and states it affects three men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a woman's adjacency invalidating a man's prayer, identify the three men affected, and apply the Hanafi definition of muḥādhāh (adjacency without barrier or gap).

Core Idea
One woman standing beside a man without barrier or gap invalidates the prayer of three men.

This lesson examines a precise ruling in the chapter of congregational prayer conditions. The Hanafi school holds that if a woman stands in the same row as men without a physical barrier or sufficient gap, she invalidates the prayer of the three men directly adjacent to her: the one to her right, the one to her left, and the one behind. Understanding this requires a clear definition of muḥādhāh and the role of barriers and gaps.

Guided Path
1
Recall the basic ruling
The passage states that one woman invalidates the prayer of three specific men: the one to her right, the one to her left, and the one directly behind her.
Note that this applies when she is in the same row as the men.
2
Define muḥādhāh (invalidating adjacency)
Muḥādhāh is defined as the woman standing beside the man without a physical barrier (ḥā’il) and without a gap (furjah). Physical contact is not required; mere parallelism suffices.
The text explicitly states that touching (mumāssah) is not a condition.
3
Apply the definition to the height difference case
If one is on a low platform (less than a cubit high) and the other on the ground, adjacency still occurs because some part of her body is parallel to him, even if not specifically the shin or foot.
Thus, vertical displacement does not automatically prevent invalidation.
4
Identify the conditions and exceptions
The invalidating condition is met only when the woman is at his side without barrier and without gap. The presence of a barrier or a sufficient gap prevents invalidation.
Further details on what constitutes a barrier or gap are promised later in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صرحوا به المرأة الواحدة تفسد صلاة ثلاثة إذا وقفت في الصف من عن يمينها ومن عن يسارها ومن خلفها ولا شك إن المحاذاة بالساق والكعب لم تتحقق فيمن خلفها فالتفسير الصحيح للمحاذاة ما في المجتبى والمحاذاة المفسدة أن تقوم بجنب الرجل من غير حائل أو قدامه اهـ. فالحاصل أن مماسة بدنها لبدنه ليست بشرط بل أن تكون عن جنبه بلا حائل ولا فرجة، وسيأتي تفسير الحائل والفرجة ولهذا لو كان أحدهما على الدكان دون القامة والآخر على الأرض فسدت صلاته لوجود المحاذاة لبعض بدنها لكونها عن جنبه، وليس هنا محاذاة بالساق والكعب ولا بالقدم
They explicitly stated: One woman invalidates the prayer of three if she stands in the row: the one to her right, the one to her left, and the one behind her. There is no doubt that adjacency by the shin and ankle does not occur for the one behind her. So the correct interpretation of adjacency is what is in Al-Mujtaba: the invalidating adjacency is that she stands beside the man without a barrier or in front of him. The upshot is that touching of her body to his body is not a condition; rather, she should be at his side without barrier or gap. The interpretation of barrier and gap will follow. For this reason, if one of them is on a platform less than a cubit high and the other on the ground, his prayer is invalidated because adjacency of some of her body exists due to her being at his side, and here there is no adjacency by shin and ankle nor by foot.
Source pages p. 621

Commentary
This passage presents a core ruling in the chapter of imamate regarding the invalidation of a man's prayer by a woman's proximity. The author states that when a single woman stands in the same row as men, she invalidates the prayer of three specific men: the one to her immediate right, her immediate left, and the one directly behind her. The reasoning is that the invalidating adjacency (محاذاة) is defined as standing beside a man without any physical barrier (حائل) or gap (فرجة) between them. Importantly, actual bodily contact is not required; it suffices that she is parallel to him at his side. The passage clarifies that if they are at different heights — for example, one on a low platform and the other on the ground — the prayer is still invalidated because some part of her body is adjacent to him, even if not specifically the shin or foot. This ruling underscores the Hanafi emphasis on physical proximity during prayer as a factor that can nullify the validity of the man's salah.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muḥādhāh): Adjacency in prayer: a woman standing directly beside a man without a physical barrier or gap, such that some part of her body is parallel to him.
حائل (ḥā'il): A physical barrier that prevents direct adjacency, such as a wall, curtain, or partition.
فرجة (furjah): A gap or space between the woman and the man that prevents adjacency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman stands beside a man in prayer with a small gap but no physical barrier, does the man's prayer become invalid according to this passage?
A) Yes, because any adjacency without barrier invalidates even if there is a gap.
B) No, because a gap exempts from invalidation.
C) Only if the gap is less than the width of a hand.
D) Only if she touches him.

Key Takeaway
One woman invalidates the prayer of three men when she stands beside them in the same row without a barrier or gap.

Intra-Hanafi Views on Limb Adjacency and Conditions for Invalidation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on limb adjacency and conditions for invalidation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on limb adjacency for invalidation and explain the conditions of sharing (ishtirak) required for invalidation.

Core Idea
Invalidation by adjacency requires sharing in both the opening takbir and performance; the relied-upon view limits adjacency to the foot.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an internal Hanafi disagreement: does any limb adjacency cause invalidation, or only the foot? The author reconciles these views and elaborates on the essential conditions of sharing in the prayer, clarifying when adjacency truly nullifies the man's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on limb adjacency
The first view, from al-Khaniya and al-Zaheriyya, states that the criterion is the foot (العبرة للقدم). The second, from Qadikhan, holds that any limb adjacency suffices. Note the key Arabic phrases for each.
The passage later suggests the foot-only view is stronger, as Qadikhan's statement is interpreted restrictively.
2
Define the 'desirable woman' (مشتهاة)
The condition that the woman be desirable (fit for intercourse) is emphasized. The commentator clarifies it is not based on age but physical suitability (ضخمة عبلة).
This excludes the insane woman (her prayer invalid) and very old unattractive women.
3
Extract the general conditions for invalidation
Both man and woman must be in prayer (excluding funeral prayer), and there must be sharing (اشتراك) in both the opening takbir (تحريمة) and the actual performance (أداء).
Adjacency without sharing (e.g., one is not praying) or without concurrent performance does not invalidate.
4
Analyze the scenarios of latecomers and followers
The text discusses cases of the latecomer (لاحق) and follower (مسبوق) to illustrate when sharing in performance is absent despite sharing in the opening takbir.
The ruling depends on whether both are actively performing the same prayer at the same time.
5
Synthesize the reconciliation
The author indicates that sharing in performance necessarily implies sharing in the opening takbir, but both are mentioned explicitly for clarity. The mufta bihi position leans toward foot-only adjacency and strict sharing conditions.
This reflects the Hanafi method of harmonizing positions by interpreting broader statements in light of more precise ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية والظهيرية : المرأة إذا صلت في بيتها مع زوجها إن كانت قدماها خلف قدم الزوج إلا أنها طويلة يقع رأسها في السجود قبل رأس الإمام جازت صلاتهما لأن العبرة للقدم اهـ . وقال قاضيخان في باب ما يفسد الصلاة وحد المحاذاة أن يحاذي عضو منها عضواً من الرجل حتى لو كانت المرأة على الظلة والرجل بحذائها أسفل منها أو خلفها إن كان يحاذي الرجل شيئاً منها تفسد صلاته وقيد بالمشتهاة لأن غير المشتهاة لا تفسد صلاته وإن كانت مميزة. واختلفوا في حد المشتهاة وصحح الشارح وغيره أنه لا اعتبار بالسن من السبع على ما قيل، أو التسع على ما قيل، وإنما المعتبر أن تصلح للجماع بأن تكون ضخمة عبلة، والعبلة المرأة التامة الخلق وأطلقها فشملت الأجنبية والزوجة والمحرم والمشتهاة حالاً أو ماضياً، مراهقة أو بالغة فدخلت العجوز الشوهاء. ولم يقيدها بالعاقلة كما فعل غيره لأن المجنونة لم تصح صلاتها فلم يوجد الاشتراك . وقيد بالصلاة لأنها لو لم تكن في الصلاة فلا فساد. وقيد الصلاة بالإطلاق وهي ما عهد مناجاة للرب سبحانه وتعالى وهي ذات الركوع أو السجود أو الإيماء للعذر للاحتراز عن المحاذاة في صلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تفسد. وقيد بالاشتراك لأن محاذاة المصلية لمصل ليس في صلاتها لا تفسد صلاته لكنه مكروه كما في فتح القدير. وقيد الاشتراك بالتحريمة والأداء لأن اللاحق إذا حاذته اللاحقة عند الذهاب إلى الوضوء أو عند المجيء قبل الاشتغال بعمل الصلاة فلا فساد وإن وجد الاشتراك حالة المحاذاة تحريمة لعدم الاشتراك أداء حالة المحاذاة لأن هذه الحالة ليست حالة الأداء، وكذا المسبوق إذا حاذته المسبوقة بعد سلام الإمام عند قضاء ما سبقا به لعدم الاشتراك في الأداء لأن المسوق منفرد فيما يقضي إلا في مسائل سنذكرها، وإن وجد الاشتراك في التحريمة وليس من شرط الاشتراك في التحريمة تحصيل الركعة الأولى مع الإمام، ولهذا قال في السراج الوهاج ولا يشترط أن تدرك أول الصلاة في الصحيح بل لو سبقها بركعة أو بركعتين فحاذته فيما أدركت تفسد عليه .اهـ. فالمشاركة في التحريمة بناء صلاتها على على من حاذته أو على صلاة إمام في حاذته فحينئذ لا تمكن المشاركة في الأداء بدون المشاركة في التحريمة حاصله أن بينهما العموم المطلق والمشاركة في التحريمة أعم لانفرادها في المسبوقين وعدم انفراد المشاركة في الأداء بناء على ما فسروها به من أن يكون لهما إمام فيما يؤديانه إما حقيقة كالمقتديين، وإما حكماً كاللاحقين وفيه نظر، لأن الإمام إذا سبقه الحديث فاستخلف آخر فاقتدى واحد بالخليفة فالشركة في الأداء ثابتة بين الذي اقتدى بالخليفة وبين الإمام الأول وكل من اقتدى به باعتبار أن لهم إماماً فيما يؤدونه وهو الخليفة ولا شركة بينهم في التحريمة لأن المقتدي بالخليفة بنى تحريمته على تحريمة الخليفة والإمام الأول، ومن اقتدى به لم يبنوا تحريمتهم على تحريمة الخليفة فلم توجد بينهم الشركة ذلك لو كانت المرأة من إحدى الطائفتين فحاذت الطائفة الأخرى تفسد باعتبار الشركة في الأداء لا التحريمة، وقد يقال الشركة فيها أيضاً ثابتة تقديراً فلم تنفرد المشاركة أداء، وعلى هذا يثبت أنه لا تمكن المشاركة في الأداء بدون المشاركة في التحريمة وكان مقتضاه أن لا يذكروا الثانية، ولكن لما كان ذلك بطريق اللزوم لم يكتفوا به في مقام تعليم الأحكام فكان التصريح أولى تقريباً على الأفهام، وهذا ما أشار إليه المؤلف بقوله فلهذا ذكروا الخ فافهم تغنم والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
And in Al-Khaniya and Al-Zaheriyya: If a woman prays in her house with her husband and her feet are behind the husband's feet, except that she is tall so her head prostrates before the imam's head, her prayer and his are valid because the criterion is the foot. Qadikhan said in the chapter on what invalidates prayer: The definition of adjacency is that any limb of hers is parallel to a limb of the man, such that if the woman is on a canopy and the man is parallel to her below or behind, if any part of her is parallel to the man, it invalidates his prayer. And he restricted it to the desirable woman, because an undesirable one does not invalidate even if she is discerning. They differed on the definition of 'desirable'; the commentator and others corrected that age (seven or nine) is not considered; rather, the criterion is that she is fit for intercourse, i.e., robust and fully formed. He did not restrict it to the sane, as others did, because the insane woman's prayer is invalid so there is no sharing. He restricted by prayer: if she is not in prayer, there is no invalidation. He restricted prayer to the absolute meaning, which is the familiar communion with the Lord, involving bowing, prostration, or gesture due to excuse, to exclude prayer over the deceased, for adjacency there does not invalidate. He restricted by sharing: adjacency of a praying woman to a man not in prayer does not invalidate his prayer, but it is disliked. He restricted sharing by the opening takbir and the performance: because if a latecomer is paralleled by a latecoming woman while going to perform ablution or coming before engaging in the prayer, there is no invalidation even if there is sharing in the opening takbir at the time of adjacency because there is no sharing in performance at that time. Similarly, if a follower is paralleled by a female follower after the imam's salam while making up what was missed, there is no invalidation due to lack of sharing in performance, because the follower is alone in what he makes up, except in cases we will mention. Sharing in the opening takbir is present because her prayer is built on the prayer of the one she parallels or on the prayer of the imam he parallels. At that point, sharing in performance cannot occur without sharing in the opening takbir. The gist is that there is absolute generality: sharing in the opening takbir is more general because it occurs alone in latecomers, while sharing in performance does not occur alone, based on their interpretation that each has an imam in what they perform—either literally as followers, or legally as latecomers. There is a consideration: if the imam had an event that invalidated his prayer and appointed a successor, and one person followed the successor, then sharing in performance exists between the one who followed the successor and the first imam and everyone who followed him, considering that they have an imam in what they perform (the successor), but there is no sharing among them in the opening takbir because the follower of the successor built his takbir on the successor's and the first imam's, but those who followed him did not build their takbir on the successor's, so there is no sharing among them. So if a woman is from one of the two groups and she parallels the other group, she invalidates due to sharing in performance, not the opening takbir. It could be said that sharing in it also exists implicitly, so sharing in performance is not exclusive. Based on this, it is established that sharing in performance is not possible without sharing in the opening takbir. This would imply that they should not mention the second, but since it is by necessity, they did not suffice with it in teaching rulings, so stating it explicitly is better for bringing closer to understanding. This is what the author indicated by his saying 'for this reason they mentioned...' So understand, you will gain, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 621

Commentary
This passage delves into the internal Hanafi debate regarding the precise nature of invalidating adjacency between a man and a woman in prayer. The first view, from Al-Khaniya and Al-Zaheriyya, holds that the criterion is the foot: as long as the woman's feet are behind the man's, even if she is tall and prostrates earlier, the prayer remains valid. 'The criterion is the foot' (العبرة للقدم) is a key principle here. The second view, attributed to Qadikhan, is broader: adjacency of any limb of hers to any limb of the man invalidates his prayer. Qadikhan also adds that the woman must be 'desirable' (مشتهاة); an undesirable woman, even if discerning, does not invalidate. The commentator then explores the definition of 'desirable', concluding it refers to a woman fit for intercourse, regardless of whether she is a stranger, wife, or relative, and regardless of age or beauty, as long as she is fully grown and robust. The passage then outlines essential conditions for invalidation: both must be in prayer (excluding funeral prayer), and there must be sharing (اشتراك) in both the opening takbir (تحريمة) and the actual performance (أداء) of the prayer. This sharing means that the male must be part of the same congregation or prayer group. The text explains complex scenarios involving latecomers and followers, emphasizing that mere historical connection in the opening takbir is insufficient without concurrent performance. The author reconciles these views by showing that while sharing in performance is the operative factor, it necessarily depends on sharing in the opening takbir, but the explicit mention of both is pedagogically useful.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muḥādhāh): The parallel positioning of a woman's body part to a man's body part during prayer, which can invalidate the man's prayer under certain conditions.
مشتهاة (mushtahāh): A woman who is desirable, i.e., fit for intercourse by being of age and physically mature (عبلة). Not defined by specific age but by physical suitability.
العبرة للقدم (al-'ibrah li-l-qadam): The legal criterion for adjacency is the foot: only if the woman's foot is parallel to the man's foot does invalidation occur.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer; also refers to the state of being in prayer from that moment.
أداء (adā'): The actual performance of the prayer (actions and recitations) after the opening takbir.
اشتراك (ishtirāk): Participation in the same prayer: both individuals must be performing the same prayer (same imam or same congregation) at the same time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, which limb adjacency invalidates a man's prayer?
A) The foot only.
B) Any limb.
C) The head only.
D) The hand only.

Key Takeaway
Invalidation by adjacency requires foot-only parallel alignment, a desirable woman, and sharing in both the opening takbir and performance.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Definition of a Desirable Woman and Conditions for Invalidating Prayer by Adjacency
Intra-Hanafi dispute on definition and conditions for invalidation by adjacency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which women invalidate a man's prayer when adjacent and explain the conditions of participation in the opening takbir and performance.

Core Idea
A woman invalidates a man's prayer if she is physically suitable for intercourse and both participate in the opening takbir and the performance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute: is the definition of 'desirable woman' based on age or physical suitability? The commentator clarifies that only physical suitability matters, and invalidation requires that both the man and woman are in prayer and share both the initial takbir and the actual performance. Understanding these precise conditions prevents incorrect invalidation and ensures correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed definition
Recognize that the passage addresses a difference among Hanafi scholars: some define a 'desirable woman' (al-mushtahāh) by age (seven or nine), while the corrected view uses physical suitability for intercourse.
The commentator sides with the physical definition.
2
Understand the corrected view
The condition for invalidation is that the woman be 'dakhma 'abla' — bulky and full-fleshed, meaning capable of intercourse. This includes all women of marriageable age, regardless of age, and excludes pre-pubescent girls.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the likelihood of distraction.
3
List the conditions for invalidation
The woman must be in prayer; the prayer must be one with bowing/prostration (not funeral); the man must also be in prayer; both must participate in the opening takbir (tahrima) and the performance (ada'); there must be no barrier or gap between them.
If any condition is missing, the prayer is not invalidated.
4
Differentiate follower categories
The passage categorizes followers into mudrik (catches all), lahiq (catches first rak'ah, misses later due to excuse), and masbuq (misses first rak'ah). Each has specific implications for participation in tahrima and ada'.
A lahiq is considered a follower constructively in what he makes up.
5
Apply the rule to scenarios
Given a scenario with a specific woman and adjacency situation, determine whether the man's prayer is invalidated by checking all conditions.
Practice with the tasks below.
