Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. She (the woman) was discerning. And they differed about the definition of a desirable woman, and the commentator and others corrected that age is not considered—not seven as is said, nor nine as is said—rather what is considered is that she is suitable for intercourse, that she be bulky and full-grown, and 'bulky' is a woman of complete physique. And he made it unrestricted so it includes the foreign woman, the wife, the relative, and one who is desirable now or in the past, adolescent or adult, thus including the ugly old woman. And he did not condition it with sanity as others did, because the insane woman's prayer is invalid, so no participation exists. And he conditioned it with prayer because if she were not in prayer, there is no invalidation. And he conditioned prayer with absolute [definition], which is the known confidential communication with the Lord Almighty, and it includes bowing, prostration, or gesture due to excuse, to exclude adjacency in the funeral prayer, for it does not invalidate. And he conditioned it with participation because the adjacency of a woman praying to a man not in his prayer does not invalidate his prayer, but it is disliked as in Fath al-Qadir. And he conditioned participation with the opening takbir and performance because if a latecomer (lahiq) is adjacently met by a latecomer woman when going to ablution or when coming before engaging in the action of prayer, there is no invalidation even if participation exists in the state of adjacency in the opening takbir, due to lack of participation in performance in the state of adjacency, because this state is not the state of performance. Similarly, a person who has missed part (masbuq) if adjacently met by a masbuq woman after the imam's salutation while making up what she missed, due to lack of participation in performance because the masbuq is alone in what he makes up, except in issues we will mention, even though participation exists in the opening takbir. And it is not a condition of participation in the opening takbir to achieve the first rak'ah with the imam; thus he said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'It is not required that she catches the first prayer in the sound view; rather, if he preceded her by a rak'ah or two, and she adjacently meets him in what she caught, it invalidates upon him.' End quote. So participation in the opening takbir is building her prayer on the one she adjacently meets or on the prayer of an imam regarding him, so then participation in performance is impossible without prayer and specification—her foot being behind him. But if she stood beside him adjacent to him, his prayer is invalidated unless there is a gap or barrier. His saying: (Then participation in performance is not possible without participation in the opening takbir) its summary is that between them is absolute generality and participation in the opening takbir is more general because it is unique in the masbuqs and participation in performance is not unique based on what they explained it as that both have an imam in what they perform, either literally like followers, or constructively like latecomers, and there is objection, because if the imam had a hadath and appointed another, and someone followed the caliph, then there is participation in performance between the one who followed the caliph and the first imam and everyone who followed him, considering that they have an imam in what they perform, which is the caliph, but there is no participation between them in the opening takbir because the follower of the caliph built his opening takbir on the opening takbir of the caliph and the first imam, and those who followed him did not build their opening takbir on the opening takbir of the caliph, so no participation exists between them. That is, if a woman were from one of the two groups and adjacently met the other group, it invalidates based on participation in performance, not in the opening takbir. And it could be said that participation in it is also established hypothetically, so participation in performance is not unique, and on this it is established that participation in performance is not possible without participation in the opening takbir, and its implication would be that they should not mention the second, but because that is by necessity, they did not suffice with it in the context of teaching rulings, so explicit mention is better for bringing close to understanding. And this is what the author indicated by his saying: 'So for this they mentioned...' etc., so grasp it, you will profit, and Allah Almighty knows best. Opening takbir. And with participation in the opening takbir, therefore they mentioned participation in opening takbir and performance and did not suffice with participation in performance. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'Then if one said instead of 'joint in opening takbir and performance' 'joint in performance,' and interprets it as both having an imam in what they perform in the state of adjacency or one of them is imam for the other, it would cover both participations.' End quote. We say: Yes, it covers, but participation in performance necessitates participation in opening takbir, so for this they mentioned both. And the summary is that the follower is either one who catches up (mudrik), or a latecomer not having missed (lahiq ghayr masbuq), or a true masbuq, or a masbuq not latecomer. The mudrik is one who catches all the rak'ahs with the imam; if a woman adjacently meets him, his prayer is invalidated due to existence of participation in opening takbir and performance. The latecomer not having missed is one who catches the first rak'ah but misses one or more due to an excuse like sleep, hadath, heedlessness, crowding, or because he is from the first group in the fear prayer. Its ruling is that when his excuse is removed, he begins making up what he missed due to the excuse, then follows the imam if he has not finished; this is obligatory, not a condition, so if he reverses, it is valid. So if he slept in the third and woke in the fourth, he performs the third without recitation because he is a latecomer in it; if he finishes before the imam prays the fourth, he prays the fourth with him; if after the imam finishes, he prays the fourth alone without recitation also because he is a latecomer. If he follows the imam then makes up the third after the imam finishes, it is valid and he completes. And from its rulings is that he is constructively a follower in what he makes up, therefore he does not recite nor is prostration of forgetfulness required on him. And if his ijtihad regarding the qibla changes, his prayer is invalidated. And if an event overtakes him while he is a traveler, and he enters his town for ablution after the imam finishes, it does not become four. Similarly, if she intends permanent residence after the imam finishes. And they made his action in principles similar to making up, so his duty does not change by intention of permanent residence because it does not affect making up. And among those attached to the latecomer is a resident who follows a traveler, for after his imam's salutation he is like a latecomer; therefore he does not recite nor prostrate for forgetfulness nor is he followed as in al-Khaniyyah. As for the latecomer who is masbuq, it is one who does not catch the first rak'ah with the imam and misses one or more after beginning due to an excuse. Therefore the verifier in Fath al-Qadir chose that the latecomer is one who misses after entering with the imam some of the prayer. His saying: (We say: Yes, but etc.) the summary of the answer is that it is an explicit statement of what is known implicitly, and the difference between stating a thing and it being necessary for another thing is apparent. And what occurred here in al-Nahr of objection that this answer is of no benefit is not apparent. Then he mentioned contradictory speech after it, whose deletion is better. Though he later retracted to what he objected to, so consult it with reflection. And Ibn Kamal Pasha answered, as in al-Shurunbulaliyya, that they mentioned each separately in detail for the place of disagreement versus the place of agreement, as is their habit. That is, participation in opening takbir is a condition by agreement, and participation in performance is a condition according to the most correct. Mentioned in Sharh al-Talkhis. End quote. His saying: (Therefore the verifier chose etc.) He said in al-Nahr: 'And he did not restrict the missing to sleep or crowding as some did, because it is not restricted to that, since the first group in the fear prayer are latecomers. Hence some said 'due to an excuse,' except that what is in al-Khulasa refutes it: if he precedes his imam in bowing and prostration, he makes up a rak'ah without recitation except that...'
Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the chapter of imamate in the prayer book. It addresses the conditions under which a woman's adjacency to a man in prayer invalidates his prayer. The primary issue is the definition of a 'desirable woman' (al-mushtaha). The commentator resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say age seven or nine, but the corrected view (mu'tamad) is that what matters is physical suitability for intercourse—being bulky and full-fleshed (dakhma 'abla). This includes any woman who is sexually desirable, whether currently or in the past, adolescent or adult, even an ugly old woman. Insanity is excluded because the insane woman's prayer is invalid, so no participation occurs. The ruling is conditioned on the woman being in prayer (since adjacency outside prayer does not invalidate), and on the prayer being one with bowing and prostration (excluding funeral prayer). Further, the invalidation requires both 'participation in the opening takbir' (ishtirak fi al-tahrima) and 'participation in performance' (ishtirak fi al-ada'). The text explains why both are necessary: e.g., a latecomer (lahiq) who is adjacent only during takbir but not during actual prayer does not cause invalidation. The passage then categorizes followers (muqtadi) into four types: mudrik (catches all), lahiq ghayr masbuq (caught first rak'ah but missed later ones due to excuse), masbuq haqq (true masbuq), and masbuq ghayr lahiq. Each has specific rulings regarding recitation and following. The commentary also addresses a possible objection: why mention both participations if one implies the other? The answer is that for clarity in teaching, explicit mention is preferred over implicit necessity. The passage ends with a citation from Fath al-Qadir and an answer by Ibn Kamal Pasha emphasizing that participation in tahrima is agreed upon, while participation in ada' is the relied-upon condition (al-ashah).

Key Terms
المشتهاة (al-mushtahāh): A woman who is desirable for sexual intercourse, defined by being bulky and full-fleshed ('abla) rather than by age.
الاشتراك في التحريمة والأداء (al-ishtirāk fī al-taḥrīma wa al-adā'): Participation in both the initial takbir (tahrima) and the performance of prayer (ada'). Both are required for a woman's adjacency to invalidate a man's prayer.
اللاحق (al-lāḥiq): A latecomer who catches the first rak'ah with the imam but misses one or more due to an excuse, and later makes them up without recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected view in this passage, what is the definition of a 'desirable woman' (al-mushtahāh) that invalidates a man's prayer when she stands adjacent to him?
A) Any woman above the age of seven
B) Any woman above the age of nine
C) A woman who is physically suitable for intercourse, described as bulky and full-fleshed ('abla)
D) A woman who is sane and adult

Key Takeaway
The invalidation of a man's prayer by adjacency requires a woman who is physically suitable for intercourse and both must participate in the opening takbir and the actual performance of prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Categories of Followers and Ruling of the Lāḥiq Ghayr Masbūq
Classifying followers and detailing the ruling for the latecomer without precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the four categories of followers in congregational prayer and explain the wājib order of actions for a lāḥiq ghayr masbūq.

Core Idea
The lāḥiq ghayr masbūq must make up missed rak'ahs without recitation before rejoining the imam; order is wājib not a condition.

In this passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq, the author classifies followers (muqtadīn) into four types. The most nuanced is the lāḥiq ghayr masbūq: one who began with the imam but missed later rak'ahs due to a valid excuse. Understanding his ruling is essential for correctly managing common prayer disruptions like sleep, forgetfulness, or crowd pressure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four types of followers mentioned: mudrik, lāḥiq ghayr masbūq, masbūq ḥaqq, masbūq ghayr lāḥiq. Define each briefly.
2
Focus on the lāḥiq ghayr masbūq
Define who qualifies as lāḥiq ghayr masbūq: caught the first rak'ah but missed one or more later rak'ahs due to a valid excuse (sleep, breaking wuḍūʾ, forgetfulness, crowding, being in the first group of ṣalāt al-khawf).
3
Analyze the ruling on order
Understand that when the excuse ceases, the lāḥiq must first make up the missed rak'ahs (without recitation) and then follow the imam. This order is wājib, not a condition; reversing is valid but sinful.
4
Apply scenarios from the text
Work through the example of sleeping in the third rak'ah: he makes up the third without recitation, then prays the fourth with the imam if possible, or alone. Also consider cases when the imam has already finished.
5
Note special rulings
The lāḥiq is considered a follower in ruling during his qaḍāʾ, so no recitation, no sajdat al-sahw. Changes in qibla invalidate his prayer. Traveler's prayer does not become four if he enters his city for wuḍūʾ after imam finishes.

Source Text

المشاركة في التحريمة، فلذا ذكروا المشاركة تحريمة وأداء ولم يكتفوا بالمشاركة في الأداء. وفي فتح القدير : ثم لو قيل بدل مشتركة تحريمة وأداء مشتركة أداء ، ويفسرها بأن يكون لهما إمام فيما يؤديانه حالة المحاذاة أو أحدهما إمام للآخر لعم الاشتراكين .اهـ. قلنا: نعم يعم لكن يلزم من الاشتراك أداء الاشتراك تحريمة، فلهذا ذكروهما . والحاصل أن المقتدي إما مدرك أو لاحق غير مسبوق، أو مسبوق حق أو مسبوق غير لاحق. فالمدرك من أدرك الركعات كلها مع الإمام، فإذا حاذته أبطلت صلاته لوجود الاشتراك تحريمة وأداء. واللاحق الغير المسبوق هو الذي أدرك الركعة الأولى وفاتته ركعة أو أكثر منها بعذر كنوم أو حدث أو غفلة أو زحمة أو لأنه من الطائفة الأولى في صلاة الخوف، وحكمه أنه إذا زال عذره فإنه يبدأ بقضاء ما فاته بالعذر ثم يتابع الإمام إن لم يفرغ، وهذا واجب لا شرط حتى لو عكس فإنه يصح، فلو نام في الثالثة واستيقظ في الرابعة فإنه يأتي بالثالثة بلا قراءة لأنه لاحق فيها، فإذا فرغ منها قبل أن يصلي الإمام الرابعة صلى معه الرابعة ، وإن بعد فراغ الإمام صلى الرابعة وحدها بلا قراءة أيضاً لأنه لاحق، فلو تابع الإمام ثم قضى الثالث بعد فراغ الإمام صح وأتم . ومن حكمه أنه مقتد حكماً فيما يقضي ولهذا لا يقرأ ولا يلزمه سجود بسهوه، وإذا تبدل اجتهاده في القبلة تبطل صلاته ولو سبقه الحدث وهو مسافر فدخل مصره للوضوء بعد فراغ الإمام لا ينقلب أربعاً، وكذا لو نوت الإقامة بعد فراغ الإمام وقد جعلوا فعله في الأصول أداء شبيهاً بالقضاء فلهذا لا يتغير فرضه بنية الإقامة لأنها لا تؤثر في القضاء. ومما الحق باللاحق المقيم إذ اقتدى بمسافر فإنه بعد سلام إمامه كاللاحق، ولهذا لا يقرأ ولا يسجد لسهوه ولا يقتدى به كما في الخانية.
Participation in the opening takbir (taḥrīmah), therefore they mentioned participation in taḥrīmah and performance (adāʾ) and did not suffice with participation in performance alone. In Fatḥ al-Qadīr: Then if it were said instead of 'common in taḥrīmah and adāʾ' it would be 'common in adāʾ', and it is interpreted as both having an imam while they are performing in the state of alignment, or one of them being imam for the other, due to the generality of the two types of participation. We say: Yes, it is general, but participation in adāʾ necessarily entails participation in taḥrīmah, therefore they mentioned both. The summary is that the follower is either a mudrik (one who catches all rak'ahs), or a lāḥiq ghayr masbūq (latecomer not preceded), or a masbūq ḥaqq (true preceded) or a masbūq ghayr lāḥiq (preceded not latecomer). The mudrik is one who catches all rak'ahs with the imam; if a woman aligns with him, his prayer is invalidated due to the existence of participation in taḥrīmah and adāʾ. The lāḥiq ghayr masbūq is one who caught the first rak'ah but missed one or more rak'ahs due to an excuse such as sleep, breaking wudu, forgetfulness, crowding, or being from the first group in the prayer of fear. His ruling is that when his excuse ceases, he begins by making up what he missed due to the excuse, then follows the imam if he has not finished. This is obligatory (wājib), not a condition, so if he reverses it, it is valid. For example, if he slept in the third rak'ah and woke up in the fourth, he performs the third without recitation because he is a lāḥiq in it. If he finishes it before the imam prays the fourth, he prays the fourth with him; if after the imam finishes, he prays the fourth alone also without recitation because he is a lāḥiq. If he follows the imam and then makes up the third after the imam finishes, it is valid and he completes. Among his rulings: he is considered a follower in ruling in what he makes up, therefore he does not recite nor is sajda al-sahw required upon him. If his ijtihād regarding the qibla changes, his prayer is invalidated. If he is overtaken by breaking wudu while traveling and enters his city to perform wudu after the imam finishes, his prayer does not become four (i.e., he does not complete as a resident). Similarly, if his wife intends to stay (residence) after the imam finishes, for they have made his action in the foundational texts 'adāʾ similar to qadāʾ, so his obligatory prayer does not change by the intention of residency because it has no effect on qadāʾ. Included with the lāḥiq is the resident who follows a traveler, for after the imam's salām he is like a lāḥiq; therefore he does not recite, does not perform sajda for his own forgetfulness, and no one follows him, as in al-Khāniyya.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq. It begins by addressing an issue regarding the definition of participation (ishitrāk) in prayer. The author clarifies that participation in the opening takbīr (taḥrīmah) is mentioned alongside participation in performance (adāʾ) because the latter necessarily implies the former, though they are distinct. Then he presents the well-known classification of followers (muqtadīn) into four categories: mudrik (one who catches all rakʿahs with the imam), lāḥiq ghayr masbūq (a latecomer who caught the first rakʿah but missed later ones due to an excuse), masbūq ḥaqq (one who missed the first rakʿah, i.e., a true masbūq), and masbūq ghayr lāḥiq (one who missed the first rakʿah but is not a lāḥiq? Actually the text says 'masbūq ghayr lāḥiq' which is equivalent to a normal masbūq). The focus then turns to the second category: the lāḥiq ghayr masbūq. This is a person who began prayer with the imam from the first rakʿah but then missed one or more rakʿahs due to a valid excuse such as sleep, loss of wuḍūʾ, forgetfulness, crowd pressure, or being in the first group in ṣalāt al-khawf (fear prayer). When the excuse is removed, the lāḥiq must (wājib) first make up the missed rakʿahs—without recitation of Qurʾān because he remains in the ruling of a follower—and then rejoin the imam if he is still praying. If he reverses the order and follows the imam first, the prayer is still valid but he is sinful for missing the wājib. Various scenarios illustrate this: if he slept during the third rakʿah and woke up in the fourth, he prays the third rakʿah alone without recitation; if he finishes before the imam begins the fourth, he prays the fourth with the imam; if the imam already finished, he prays the fourth alone also without recitation. The passage also notes that if his ijtihād regarding qibla changes, his prayer becomes invalid. Special rules apply when a traveler lāḥiq goes to his city for wuḍūʾ: his prayer does not become four rakʿahs because it is like qadāʾ. Similarly, if his wife (accompanying him) intends to stay (i.e., become a resident) after the imam finishes, his prayer remains four (traveler's prayer). Finally, a resident who follows a traveling imam is like a lāḥiq after the imam's salām: he does not recite Qurʾān nor perform sajda al-sahw for his own mistakes, and no one can follow him because his prayer is considered complete? This highlights the Ḥanafī precision in defining follower categories.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): A follower who catches all rak'ahs with the imam from the beginning to the end.
لاحق غير مسبوق (lāḥiq ghayr masbūq): A follower who caught the first rak'ah but missed one or more later rak'ahs due to a valid excuse.
الاشتراك في التحريمة (al-ishtirāk fī al-taḥrīmah): Participation in the opening takbīr, meaning both follower and imam begin the prayer together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person begins prayer with the imam, catches the first rak'ah, but falls asleep during the third rak'ah and wakes up in the fourth. What should he do according to this passage?
A) Immediately follow the imam in the fourth rak'ah, then make up the third rak'ah after the imam finishes.
B) Make up the third rak'ah first without recitation, then follow the imam in the fourth rak'ah if he is still praying, or pray the fourth alone if the imam has finished.
C) Make up the third rak'ah with recitation because it is a missed rak'ah.
D) Start his prayer anew because his sleep invalidated his following.

Key Takeaway
The lāḥiq ghayr masbūq must first make up missed rak'ahs without recitation before rejoining the imam; this order is wājib, not a condition of validity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
The Lāḥiq Masbūq: Definition and Order of Qaḍāʾ
Definition and rulings of the lāḥiq masbūq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the lāḥiq masbūq and state the Hanafi ruling on the order of making up missed rak'ahs, including the position of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
The lāḥiq masbūq must first make up the rak'ahs he was late in; reversing is valid but sinful.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between a follower who misses the beginning and later misses more due to an excuse. This lesson unpacks the unique category of lāḥiq masbūq, focusing on the obligatory order of qaḍāʾ and a critical case where two followers break wuḍūʾ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Look at the opening lines: what is a lāḥiq masbūq? Note the critique of the definition in Fatḥ al-Qadīr.
The definition includes both missing the first rak'ah and later missing due to excuse.
2
Understand the order of qaḍāʾ
From al-Majmaʿ: the lāḥiq masbūq first makes up what he was late in (due to excuse), then what he was preceded in.
3
Work through the case of two followers
They start in the third rak'ah, break wuḍūʾ, then align in qaḍāʾ. Determine which rak'ahs invalidate and why.
Focus on the concept of participation (ishtirāk) in the late rak'ahs.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Zufar
Zufar says the order is apparent and reversal invalid; the majority holds reversal valid but sinful.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the invalidity of prayer depends on which rak'ahs they align in, based on the order.
This is crucial for fatwa.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما اللاحق المسبوق فهو من لم يدرك الركعة الأولى مع الإمام وفاته بعد الشروع ركعة أو أكثر بعذر، ولهذا اختار المحقق في فتح القدير أن اللاحق هو من فاته بعد ما دخل مع الإمام بعض صلاة ثم الإمام ليشمل اللاحق المسبوق، وتعريفهم اللاحق بأنه من أدرك أوّل صلاة الإمام وفاته شيء منها بعذر تساهل اهـ . لكن يرد عليه المقيم إذا اقتدى بمسافر فإنه لاحق ولم يشمله تعريفه إلا أن يقال : إنه ملحق به وليس هو حقيقة وحكمه إذا زال عذره ما قال في المجمع : أن يصلي فيما أدرك ما نام فيه ثم يقضي ما فاته ولو تابع فيما بقي ثم قضى الفائت ثم ما نام فيه أجزناه، وقدمنا أنه يصح مع الإثم لترك الواجب . وأما المسبوق فقط فهو من لم يدرك الركعة الأولى مع الإمام وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى بيان أحكامه عند قوله وصح استخلاف المسبوق». وقالوا : لو اقتديا في الركعة الثالثة أحدثا فذهبا للوضوء ثم حاذته في القضاء ينظر؛ فإن حاذته في الأولى أو الثانية وهي الثالثة والرابعة للإمام تفسد صلاته لوجود الشركة فيهما تقديراً لكونهما لاحقين فيهما، وإن حاذته في الثالثة والرابعة لا تفسد لعدم المشاركة فيهما لكونهما مسبوقين. وهذا بناء على أن اللاحق المسبوق يقضي أولاً ما لحق فيه ثم ما سبق فيه، وهذا عند زفر ظاهر، وعندنا وإن صح عكسه لكن يجب هذا فباعتباره تفسد. وقيد باتحاد المكان لأنه لو اختلف فلا فساد سواء كان هناك حائل أو لا، ولهذا قال في السراج الوهاج : لو كان على الدكان أو الحائط وهو قدر قامة وهي على الأرض لا تفسد لعدم اتحاد المكان، وهكذا في الكافي . قال في النوازل قوم صلوا على ظهر ظلة في المسجد وبحذائهم من تحتهم نساء أجزأتهم صلاتهم لعدم اتحاد المكان بخلاف ما إذا كان قدامهم نساء فإنها فاسدة لأنه تخلل بينهم وبين الإمام . صف من النساء وهو مانع من الاقتداء كما سيأتي، وفي المجتبى : اقتدين على رفة المسجد وتحته صفوف الرجال لا تفسد صلاتهم وقيد بعدم الحائل لأنه لو كان بينها وبينه حائل فلا فساد وأدناه قدر مؤخرة الرجل أو مقدمته لأن أدنى أحوال الصلاة القعود فقدرنا الحائل ،به وهو قدر ذراع كذا في المحيط. وفي المجتبى : لو كان بينهما أسطوانة أو سترة قدر مؤخرة الرحل أو عود أو قصبة منتصبة للسترة أو حائط أو دكان قدر الذراع لا تفسد . وذكر الشارح أن أدناه قدر مؤخرة الرحل وغلظه مثل غلظ الأصبع، ولم يذكر المصنف الفرجة من غير حائل وظاهر كلامه أنه لا عبرة بها وأن المرأة إذا كانت عن يمينه أو عن يساره وبينهما فرجة بلا حائل فإنها تفسد صلاته. وذكر الشارح وغيره أن يقال : إنه يلحق به أيضاً قوله : لكن يرد عليه المقيم الخ) ظاهره أنه لا يرد على تعريفهم وليس كذلك كما لا يخفى قوله : (وهذا بناء على أن اللاحق المسبوق الخ قال في النهر : وينبغي أنه إن نوی قضاء ما سبق به أولاً أن ينعكس حكم المسألة، وهذا أحد المواضع التي خالف فيها اللاحق، المسبوق ومنها: لو نسي القعدة الأولى أتى بها المسبوق لا اللاحق ومنها لو ضحك الإمام أو أحدث عمداً في موضع السلام فسدت صلاة المسبوق وفي اللاحق روايتان، والأصح عدم الفساد. ومنها لو قال الإمام بعد فراغه من الفجر كنت محدثاً في العشاء فسدت صلاة المسبوق وفي اللاحق روايتان.
As for the lāḥiq masbūq (latecomer who is also preceded), he is one who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam and missed one or more rak'ahs after starting due to an excuse. For this reason, the muḥaqqiq (researcher) in Fatḥ al-Qadīr chose that the lāḥiq is one who misses some of the prayer after entering with the imam, then the imam (?) to include the lāḥiq masbūq, and their definition of the lāḥiq as one who caught the first of the imam's prayer and missed some of it due to an excuse is lenient. But the resident (muqīm) who follows a traveler is an objection to it, for he is a lāḥiq yet is not included in this definition, unless it is said that he is annexed to him (mulḥaq bih) and is not a real lāḥiq. His ruling when his excuse ceases is as stated in al-Majmaʿ: he should pray what he caught (i.e., the rak'ahs he was present for) with sleep, then make up what he missed; and if he followed in the remaining then made up the missed ones and then the ones he slept in, we allow it, and we have stated that it is valid with sin for leaving the wājib. As for the masbūq only, he is one who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam, and his rulings will come later. They said: if two followers start in the third rak'ah and then both break wuḍūʾ and go for wuḍūʾ, then align in the qaḍāʾ (make-up prayers), it is considered: if they align in the first or second (of their make-up), which correspond to the third and fourth for the imam, their prayer is invalid due to the presence of participation (ishtirāk) in both, because they are considered lāḥiq in them. If they align in the third and fourth (of their make-up), it is not invalid due to lack of participation because they are masbūq in them. This is based on the fact that the lāḥiq masbūq first makes up what he was late in, then what he was preceded in. This is apparent according to Zufar, and according to us, although its reverse is valid, it is obligatory (wājib), so by considering it (the order) it is invalid. It is conditioned on unity of place (ittiḥād al-makān), because if they differ, there is no invalidity, whether there is a barrier or not. Therefore it is said in al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj: if he is on a platform or wall that is a standing height and she is on the ground, it is not invalid due to lack of unity of place; likewise in al-Kāfī. It is said in al-Nawāzil: people who pray on top of a canopy in the mosque, and women are beneath them alongside them, their prayer is valid due to lack of unity of place, unlike if women are in front of them, then it is invalid because a row of women comes between them and the imam, which prevents following. In al-Mujtabā: women who pray on the roof of the mosque and beneath them are rows of men, their prayer is not invalid, conditioned on no barrier. Because if there is a barrier between them and him, there is no invalidity, and the minimum (height) is the size of the hind part of a saddle or its front part (approx. a cubit). In al-Mujtabā: if between them is a pillar or a screen of that size, a stick, a reed erected as a screen, a wall, or a platform of a cubit, it does not invalidate. The commentator mentioned that the minimum is the size of the hind part of a saddle, and its thickness is the thickness of a finger. The author (al-Kanz) did not mention an open gap without a barrier, and his apparent statement is that it is not considered, and that if a woman is to his right or left and between them is an open gap without a barrier, it invalidates his prayer. The commentator and others mention that... He said: (This is based on that the lāḥiq masbūq...) In al-Nahr: It should be that if he intends to make up what he was preceded in first, the ruling of the case is reversed. This is one of the places where the lāḥiq and masbūq differ. Among them: if he forgets the first sitting (tashahhud), the masbūq performs it, the lāḥiq does not. Among them: if the imam laughs or intentionally breaks wuḍūʾ in the place of salām, the masbūq's prayer is invalid; regarding the lāḥiq there are two narrations, the most correct is no invalidity. Among them: if the imam says after finishing Fajr that he was in a state of major impurity (ḥadath) during ʿIshāʾ, the masbūq's prayer is invalid; regarding the lāḥiq there are two narrations.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq continues the discussion on follower categories, now focusing on the lāḥiq masbūq—a follower who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam but joined later and then missed further rak'ahs due to an excuse. The author critiques the definition in Fatḥ al-Qadīr, which defined lāḥiq as one who caught the first of the imam's prayer and missed something due to an excuse; this excludes the resident who follows a traveler (who is a lāḥiq by annexation). The actual ruling for such a person is given from al-Majmaʿ: he should make up the rak'ahs he missed due to the excuse in a specific order, but reversing is valid though sinful. Then a detailed case is presented: two followers both start in the third rak'ah (i.e., they missed the first two), then both break wuḍūʾ and go to renew it, then come back and align in their make-up prayers. The validity depends on which rak'ahs they align in during their qaḍāʾ. If they align in the first or second of their make-up (which correspond to the imam's third and fourth), their prayer is invalid because they are considered lāḥiq in those rak'ahs (since they were late in them due to the excuse of wuḍūʾ). If they align in the third and fourth of their make-up (i.e., their own sequence), it is valid because they are masbūq (just preceded) in those. This is based on the order of qaḍāʾ for the lāḥiq masbūq: he first makes up what he was late in (i.e., the rak'ahs he missed after joining) and then what he was preceded in (the rak'ahs he missed before joining). According to Zufar, this order is apparent; according to the majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad), the reverse is also valid but the order is obligatory, so considering the obligatory order, the prayer is invalid if they align in the wrong rak'ahs. The discussion then moves to the condition of unity of place (ittiḥād al-makān) when women are present. The presence of a woman in alignment with a man during prayer invalidates his prayer only if they share the same place. If the man is on a higher platform and the woman on the ground, or if there is a barrier of a certain height (minimum: the size of the hind part of a saddle, about a cubit), the prayer is not invalid. The author also addresses the issue of an open gap (farjah) without a barrier: if a woman is to the side with an open gap, it invalidates the prayer according to the apparent meaning of al-Kanz. Finally, a list of differences between the lāḥiq and masbūq is given from al-Nahr, including cases of forgetting the first sitting, the effect of the imam's laughter or intentional ḥadath, and the imam's later confession of impurity. These illustrate that the rulings for the lāḥiq often differ from those for the masbūq.

Key Terms
لاحق مسبوق (lāḥiq masbūq): A follower who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam and then missed one or more later rak'ahs due to an excuse after joining.
اتحاد المكان (ittiḥād al-makān): Unity of place: the condition that a man and a woman must be on the same level of elevation or within the same defined space for the woman's alignment to invalidate the man's prayer.
مؤخرة الرحل (muʾakhkharat al-raḥl): The hind part of a saddle, used as a measure for the minimum barrier height (approx. 1 cubit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two men begin prayer in the third rak'ah behind an imam, both break wuḍūʾ, go to renew it, and then come back. They align in their make-up prayer in the first and second rak'ahs of their own prayer (which correspond to the imam's third and fourth). According to the text, what is the ruling?
A) Their prayer is valid because they are masbūq in those rak'ahs.
B) Their prayer is invalid because they are lāḥiq in those rak'ahs.
C) Their prayer is valid if they intended to make up the preceded rak'ahs first.
D) Their prayer is invalid regardless of intention.

Key Takeaway
The order of qaḍāʾ for the lāḥiq masbūq is wājib: first make up rak'ahs missed due to excuse, then those missed before joining; reversing is valid but sinful.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Unity of Place (Ittiḥād al-Makān) and Prayer Validity
Condition of unity of place for prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition of ittiḥād al-makān and determine when a woman's alignment invalidates a man's prayer, including the minimum barrier height.

Core Idea
A woman's alignment invalidates a man's prayer only if they share the same place; a height difference or barrier prevents invalidity.

The presence of a woman alongside a man during prayer raises questions of validity. The Hanafi school conditions invalidity on unity of place (ittiḥād al-makān). This lesson explores the rulings on height differences, barriers, and the measure used to determine them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition of ittiḥād al-makān
The prayer is invalid only if the man and woman are on the same level and without a barrier.
If they are on different levels (e.g., man on a platform), there is no unity of place.
2
Identify the examples of differing places
Cases from al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj: man on a platform, women on ground; women on a canopy above men.
Also see al-Nawāzil: people on top of a canopy, women beneath alongside.
3
Determine the barrier measure
The minimum barrier height is the size of the hind part of a saddle (qadr muʾakhkharat al-raḥl), about 1 cubit, and thickness of a finger.
This measure is derived from the smallest posture in prayer, which is sitting.
4
Note the ruling on an open gap without a barrier
If a woman is to the side with an open gap (no barrier), the prayer is invalid according to apparent meaning of al-Kanz.
An open gap does not prevent invalidity; only a physical barrier suffices.
5
Apply the condition to real scenarios
E.g., women praying on the roof of the mosque while men are below: no invalidity.
Also, a pillar or screen of sufficient size acts as a barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما اللاحق المسبوق فهو من لم يدرك الركعة الأولى مع الإمام وفاته بعد الشروع ركعة أو أكثر بعذر، ولهذا اختار المحقق في فتح القدير أن اللاحق هو من فاته بعد ما دخل مع الإمام بعض صلاة ثم الإمام ليشمل اللاحق المسبوق، وتعريفهم اللاحق بأنه من أدرك أوّل صلاة الإمام وفاته شيء منها بعذر تساهل اهـ . لكن يرد عليه المقيم إذا اقتدى بمسافر فإنه لاحق ولم يشمله تعريفه إلا أن يقال : إنه ملحق به وليس هو حقيقة وحكمه إذا زال عذره ما قال في المجمع : أن يصلي فيما أدرك ما نام فيه ثم يقضي ما فاته ولو تابع فيما بقي ثم قضى الفائت ثم ما نام فيه أجزناه، وقدمنا أنه يصح مع الإثم لترك الواجب . وأما المسبوق فقط فهو من لم يدرك الركعة الأولى مع الإمام وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى بيان أحكامه عند قوله وصح استخلاف المسبوق». وقالوا : لو اقتديا في الركعة الثالثة أحدثا فذهبا للوضوء ثم حاذته في القضاء ينظر؛ فإن حاذته في الأولى أو الثانية وهي الثالثة والرابعة للإمام تفسد صلاته لوجود الشركة فيهما تقديراً لكونهما لاحقين فيهما، وإن حاذته في الثالثة والرابعة لا تفسد لعدم المشاركة فيهما لكونهما مسبوقين. وهذا بناء على أن اللاحق المسبوق يقضي أولاً ما لحق فيه ثم ما سبق فيه، وهذا عند زفر ظاهر، وعندنا وإن صح عكسه لكن يجب هذا فباعتباره تفسد. وقيد باتحاد المكان لأنه لو اختلف فلا فساد سواء كان هناك حائل أو لا، ولهذا قال في السراج الوهاج : لو كان على الدكان أو الحائط وهو قدر قامة وهي على الأرض لا تفسد لعدم اتحاد المكان، وهكذا في الكافي . قال في النوازل قوم صلوا على ظهر ظلة في المسجد وبحذائهم من تحتهم نساء أجزأتهم صلاتهم لعدم اتحاد المكان بخلاف ما إذا كان قدامهم نساء فإنها فاسدة لأنه تخلل بينهم وبين الإمام . صف من النساء وهو مانع من الاقتداء كما سيأتي، وفي المجتبى : اقتدين على رفة المسجد وتحته صفوف الرجال لا تفسد صلاتهم وقيد بعدم الحائل لأنه لو كان بينها وبينه حائل فلا فساد وأدناه قدر مؤخرة الرجل أو مقدمته لأن أدنى أحوال الصلاة القعود فقدرنا الحائل ،به وهو قدر ذراع كذا في المحيط. وفي المجتبى : لو كان بينهما أسطوانة أو سترة قدر مؤخرة الرحل أو عود أو قصبة منتصبة للسترة أو حائط أو دكان قدر الذراع لا تفسد . وذكر الشارح أن أدناه قدر مؤخرة الرحل وغلظه مثل غلظ الأصبع، ولم يذكر المصنف الفرجة من غير حائل وظاهر كلامه أنه لا عبرة بها وأن المرأة إذا كانت عن يمينه أو عن يساره وبينهما فرجة بلا حائل فإنها تفسد صلاته. وذكر الشارح وغيره أن يقال : إنه يلحق به أيضاً قوله : لكن يرد عليه المقيم الخ) ظاهره أنه لا يرد على تعريفهم وليس كذلك كما لا يخفى قوله : (وهذا بناء على أن اللاحق المسبوق الخ قال في النهر : وينبغي أنه إن نوی قضاء ما سبق به أولاً أن ينعكس حكم المسألة، وهذا أحد المواضع التي خالف فيها اللاحق، المسبوق ومنها: لو نسي القعدة الأولى أتى بها المسبوق لا اللاحق ومنها لو ضحك الإمام أو أحدث عمداً في موضع السلام فسدت صلاة المسبوق وفي اللاحق روايتان، والأصح عدم الفساد. ومنها لو قال الإمام بعد فراغه من الفجر كنت محدثاً في العشاء فسدت صلاة المسبوق وفي اللاحق روايتان.
As for the lāḥiq masbūq (latecomer who is also preceded), he is one who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam and missed one or more rak'ahs after starting due to an excuse. For this reason, the muḥaqqiq (researcher) in Fatḥ al-Qadīr chose that the lāḥiq is one who misses some of the prayer after entering with the imam, then the imam (?) to include the lāḥiq masbūq, and their definition of the lāḥiq as one who caught the first of the imam's prayer and missed some of it due to an excuse is lenient. But the resident (muqīm) who follows a traveler is an objection to it, for he is a lāḥiq yet is not included in this definition, unless it is said that he is annexed to him (mulḥaq bih) and is not a real lāḥiq. His ruling when his excuse ceases is as stated in al-Majmaʿ: he should pray what he caught (i.e., the rak'ahs he was present for) with sleep, then make up what he missed; and if he followed in the remaining then made up the missed ones and then the ones he slept in, we allow it, and we have stated that it is valid with sin for leaving the wājib. As for the masbūq only, he is one who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam, and his rulings will come later. They said: if two followers start in the third rak'ah and then both break wuḍūʾ and go for wuḍūʾ, then align in the qaḍāʾ (make-up prayers), it is considered: if they align in the first or second (of their make-up), which correspond to the third and fourth for the imam, their prayer is invalid due to the presence of participation (ishtirāk) in both, because they are considered lāḥiq in them. If they align in the third and fourth (of their make-up), it is not invalid due to lack of participation because they are masbūq in them. This is based on the fact that the lāḥiq masbūq first makes up what he was late in, then what he was preceded in. This is apparent according to Zufar, and according to us, although its reverse is valid, it is obligatory (wājib), so by considering it (the order) it is invalid. It is conditioned on unity of place (ittiḥād al-makān), because if they differ, there is no invalidity, whether there is a barrier or not. Therefore it is said in al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj: if he is on a platform or wall that is a standing height and she is on the ground, it is not invalid due to lack of unity of place; likewise in al-Kāfī. It is said in al-Nawāzil: people who pray on top of a canopy in the mosque, and women are beneath them alongside them, their prayer is valid due to lack of unity of place, unlike if women are in front of them, then it is invalid because a row of women comes between them and the imam, which prevents following. In al-Mujtabā: women who pray on the roof of the mosque and beneath them are rows of men, their prayer is not invalid, conditioned on no barrier. Because if there is a barrier between them and him, there is no invalidity, and the minimum (height) is the size of the hind part of a saddle or its front part (approx. a cubit). In al-Mujtabā: if between them is a pillar or a screen of that size, a stick, a reed erected as a screen, a wall, or a platform of a cubit, it does not invalidate. The commentator mentioned that the minimum is the size of the hind part of a saddle, and its thickness is the thickness of a finger. The author (al-Kanz) did not mention an open gap without a barrier, and his apparent statement is that it is not considered, and that if a woman is to his right or left and between them is an open gap without a barrier, it invalidates his prayer. The commentator and others mention that... He said: (This is based on that the lāḥiq masbūq...) In al-Nahr: It should be that if he intends to make up what he was preceded in first, the ruling of the case is reversed. This is one of the places where the lāḥiq and masbūq differ. Among them: if he forgets the first sitting (tashahhud), the masbūq performs it, the lāḥiq does not. Among them: if the imam laughs or intentionally breaks wuḍūʾ in the place of salām, the masbūq's prayer is invalid; regarding the lāḥiq there are two narrations, the most correct is no invalidity. Among them: if the imam says after finishing Fajr that he was in a state of major impurity (ḥadath) during ʿIshāʾ, the masbūq's prayer is invalid; regarding the lāḥiq there are two narrations.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq continues the discussion on follower categories, now focusing on the lāḥiq masbūq—a follower who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam but joined later and then missed further rak'ahs due to an excuse. The author critiques the definition in Fatḥ al-Qadīr, which defined lāḥiq as one who caught the first of the imam's prayer and missed something due to an excuse; this excludes the resident who follows a traveler (who is a lāḥiq by annexation). The actual ruling for such a person is given from al-Majmaʿ: he should make up the rak'ahs he missed due to the excuse in a specific order, but reversing is valid though sinful. Then a detailed case is presented: two followers both start in the third rak'ah (i.e., they missed the first two), then both break wuḍūʾ and go to renew it, then come back and align in their make-up prayers. The validity depends on which rak'ahs they align in during their qaḍāʾ. If they align in the first or second of their make-up (which correspond to the imam's third and fourth), their prayer is invalid because they are considered lāḥiq in those rak'ahs (since they were late in them due to the excuse of wuḍūʾ). If they align in the third and fourth of their make-up (i.e., their own sequence), it is valid because they are masbūq (just preceded) in those. This is based on the order of qaḍāʾ for the lāḥiq masbūq: he first makes up what he was late in (i.e., the rak'ahs he missed after joining) and then what he was preceded in (the rak'ahs he missed before joining). According to Zufar, this order is apparent; according to the majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad), the reverse is also valid but the order is obligatory, so considering the obligatory order, the prayer is invalid if they align in the wrong rak'ahs. The discussion then moves to the condition of unity of place (ittiḥād al-makān) when women are present. The presence of a woman in alignment with a man during prayer invalidates his prayer only if they share the same place. If the man is on a higher platform and the woman on the ground, or if there is a barrier of a certain height (minimum: the size of the hind part of a saddle, about a cubit), the prayer is not invalid. The author also addresses the issue of an open gap (farjah) without a barrier: if a woman is to the side with an open gap, it invalidates the prayer according to the apparent meaning of al-Kanz. Finally, a list of differences between the lāḥiq and masbūq is given from al-Nahr, including cases of forgetting the first sitting, the effect of the imam's laughter or intentional ḥadath, and the imam's later confession of impurity. These illustrate that the rulings for the lāḥiq often differ from those for the masbūq.

Key Terms
اتحاد المكان (ittiḥād al-makān): Unity of place: the condition that a man and a woman must be on the same level of elevation or within the same defined space for the woman's alignment to invalidate the man's prayer.
مؤخرة الرحل (muʾakhkharat al-raḥl): The hind part of a saddle, used as a measure for the minimum barrier height (approx. 1 cubit).
فرجة (farjah): An open gap without a barrier between a man and a woman during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum height of a barrier to prevent invalidity due to a woman's alignment?
A) The size of a finger
B) The height of a sitting person
C) The size of the hind part of a saddle (approx. 1 cubit)
D) Any height suffices

Key Takeaway
Unity of place is required for a woman's alignment to invalidate a man's prayer; a height difference or barrier of at least 1 cubit prevents invalidity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Definitions of Lāḥiq and Masbūq and the Order of Qaḍā'
Defines lāḥiq and masbūq and states their qada' order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-lāḥiq and al-masbūq according to the Hanafi school and state the mufta bihi order of qada' for a lāḥiq.

Core Idea
A lāḥiq prays what he caught first, then what he missed; a masbūq prays what he missed first.

In Hanafi fiqh, the terms lāḥiq and masbūq classify followers in congregational prayer who miss parts due to different reasons. Their rulings differ, especially regarding the order in which they complete missed rak'ahs. This lesson clarifies these definitions and the relied-upon order of qada'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the definitions of lāḥiq and masbūq in the source. A lāḥiq catches the beginning of the imam's prayer but misses part due to an excuse. A masbūq misses the first rak'ah entirely.
The text also mentions that a resident following a traveler is considered a lāḥiq by extension.
2
Understand the difference
Note that the key difference is whether the first rak'ah was caught. A lāḥiq has caught the first rak'ah; a masbūq has not.
3
Learn the qada' order for a lāḥiq
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that a lāḥiq first prays what he caught (the part he joined), then prays what he missed (the part he was preceded in). This is the opposite of Imam Zufar's view.
According to the text, if a lāḥiq followed the imam in the remaining part and then completed the missed part, his prayer is valid but sinful for leaving the wajib order.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar holds that a lāḥiq prays what he was preceded in first, then what he caught. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold the opposite order, which is mufta bihi.
This ikhtilaf affects the validity scenario described later in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وليس هو حقيقة وحكمه إذا زال عذره ما قال في المجمع : أن يصلي فيما أدرك ما نام فيه ثم يقضي ما فاته ولو تابع فيما بقي ثم قضى الفائت ثم ما نام فيه أجزناه، وقدمنا أنه يصح مع الإثم لترك الواجب . وأما المسبوق فقط فهو من لم يدرك الركعة الأولى مع الإمام وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى بيان أحكامه عند قوله وصح استخلاف المسبوق». وقالوا : لو اقتديا في الركعة الثالثة أحدثا فذهبا للوضوء ثم حاذته في القضاء ينظر؛ فإن حاذته في الأولى أو الثانية وهي الثالثة والرابعة للإمام تفسد صلاته لوجود الشركة فيهما تقديراً لكونهما لاحقين فيهما، وإن حاذته في الثالثة والرابعة لا تفسد لعدم المشاركة فيهما لكونهما مسبوقين. وهذا بناء على أن اللاحق المسبوق يقضي أولاً ما لحق فيه ثم ما سبق فيه، وهذا عند زفر ظاهر، وعندنا وإن صح عكسه لكن يجب هذا فباعتباره تفسد. وقيد باتحاد المكان لأنه لو اختلف فلا فساد سواء كان هناك حائل أو لا، ولهذا قال في السراج الوهاج : لو كان على الدكان أو الحائط وهو قدر قامة وهي على الأرض لا تفسد لعدم اتحاد المكان، وهكذا في الكافي . قال في النوازل قوم صلوا على ظهر ظلة في المسجد وبحذائهم من تحتهم نساء أجزأتهم صلاتهم لعدم اتحاد المكان بخلاف ما إذا كان قدامهم نساء فإنها فاسدة لأنه تخلل بينهم وبين الإمام . صف من النساء وهو مانع من الاقتداء كما سيأتي، وفي المجتبى : اقتدين على رفة المسجد وتحته صفوف الرجال لا تفسد صلاتهم وقيد بعدم الحائل لأنه لو كان بينها وبينه حائل فلا فساد وأدناه قدر مؤخرة الرجل أو مقدمته لأن أدنى أحوال الصلاة القعود فقدرنا الحائل به وهو قدر ذراع كذا في المحيط. وفي المجتبى : لو كان بينهما أسطوانة أو سترة قدر مؤخرة الرحل أو عود أو قصبة منتصبة للسترة أو حائط أو دكان قدر الذراع لا تفسد . وذكر الشارح أن أدناه قدر مؤخرة الرحل وغلظه مثل غلظ الأصبع، ولم يذكر المصنف الفرجة من غير حائل وظاهر كلامه أنه لا عبرة بها وأن المرأة إذا كانت عن يمينه أو عن يساره وبينهما فرجة بلا حائل فإنها تفسد صلاته. وذكر الشارح وغيره أن الفرجة كالحائل وأدناها قدر ما يقوم فيها الرجل، ولو كان أحدهما على المجتبى عن صلاة البقالي.
Then the imam is general to include the latecomer and the one preceded. Their definition of the latecomer: one who catches the first part of the imam's prayer but misses some of it due to an excuse, leniently. But the resident who follows a traveler is a latecomer, and this definition does not include him unless it is said: he is attached to him but not in reality. His ruling when his excuse ends is as stated in al-Majma': he should pray what he caught first (the part he slept through) then complete what he missed. Even if he followed in the remaining part and then completed the missed part and then what he slept through, we deem it permissible. We have stated that it is valid but with sin for leaving an obligatory act. As for the one who is preceded only: he is one who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam, and his rulings will come later, God willing, at his statement: 'It is valid to appoint the one preceded as substitute.' They said: If two people catch the third rak'ah, then both have an event (ritual impurity) and go for wudu, then they line up with him (the imam) in the remaining prayer, it is considered: if they line up in the first or second (of his remaining rak'ahs), which are the third and fourth for the imam, their prayer is invalid because of shared participation in them, since they are considered latecomers in them. If they line up in the third and fourth (of his remaining), which are the first and second for the imam, it is not invalid due to lack of participation in them since they are preceded in them. This is based on the principle that the latecomer who is preceded first prays what he caught (the part he joined) and then what he missed (the part he was preceded in). This is apparent according to Zufar, and according to us, although the opposite is valid, this is obligatory, so by considering it, it is invalid. It is conditioned by unity of place, because if it differs, then no invalidity, whether there is a barrier or not. For this reason, it is stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if one is on a platform or wall of normal height and the other is on the ground, it is not invalid due to lack of unity of place. Similarly in al-Kafi. It is stated in al-Nawazil: people prayed on the roof of an arcade in the mosque, and below them were women in line with them; their prayer is valid due to lack of unity of place, unlike if the women were in front of them, then it is invalid because there is an intervening row of women between them and the imam, which prevents valid following, as will come. In al-Mujtaba: Women prayed on a ledge of the mosque with rows of men below; their prayer is not invalid. It is conditioned by the absence of a barrier, because if there is a barrier between them and him, there is no invalidity. The minimum barrier is the size of the back of a saddle or its front, because the minimum state of prayer is sitting, so we estimate the barrier by that, which is a cubit's length, as in al-Muhit. In al-Mujtaba: If between them is a pillar or a screen the size of the back of a saddle, or a stick or reed erected as a screen, or a wall or platform of a cubit, it does not invalidate. The explainer mentioned that the minimum is the size of the back of a saddle and its thickness like a finger. The author did not mention the gap without a barrier, and apparently, he gives it no consideration, and that if a woman is to his right or left with a gap between them without a barrier, it invalidates his prayer. The explainer and others mentioned that the gap is like a barrier, and its minimum is the space a man can stand in. If one is on a platform of normal height and the other below, it does not invalidate due to lack of actual alignment. It is clearly stated in Miraj al-Diraya: if there is a gap wide enough for a man or a pillar, it is said it does not invalidate, and similarly if she stands in front of him with this gap between them, and it is clearly stated in al-Mujtaba concerning the prayer of Bazzazi.
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines two important terms in Hanafi congregational prayer: al-lāḥiq (the latecomer) and al-masbūq (the one preceded). The latecomer is one who catches the beginning of the imam's prayer but misses a part due to an excuse, such as sleeping and waking late. The one preceded (masbūq) is one who misses the first rak'ah entirely. The text then presents a scenario: two people join the imam in the third rak'ah, then both have ritual impurity and leave for wudu. Upon returning, they line up with the imam during the remaining prayer (qadā'). The ruling depends on whether they line up during the imam's first two remaining rak'ahs (which are the third and fourth for the imam) or during the imam's last two remaining rak'ahs (which are the first and second for the imam). If they line up in the first category, their prayer is invalid because they are considered latecomers in those rak'ahs and thus have a participatory connection that is broken by their interruption. If in the second category, it is valid because they are considered preceded in those rak'ahs and have no such connection. This is based on the principle that a latecomer (lāḥiq) prays first what he caught (the part he joined) and then what he missed (the part he was preceded in), differing from the order for a simply preceded person (masbūq). The text then discusses the condition of unity of place: if the followers are at different vertical levels (e.g., on a platform vs. ground), the prayer is not invalid. It also mentions that a row of women between the imam and male followers invalidates the prayer, but if there is a barrier like a pillar or screen of a certain minimum size, it can prevent invalidity. The author also notes that a gap (furjah) without a physical barrier is treated like a barrier if it is at least the width of a man standing, and this affects the validity of the prayer when a woman is aligned without a barrier. The passage is a detailed expansion (sharḥ) on the rulings of congregational prayer, specifically the conditions for valid following and exceptions for latecomers and those preceded.

Key Terms
لاحق (lāḥiq): One who catches the beginning of the imam's prayer but misses a part due to an excuse (e.g., sleep).
مسبوق (masbūq): One who misses the first rak'ah of the imam's prayer.

The mufta bihi order for a lāḥiq is to first pray the part he caught, then the part he missed.

Rulings on Unity of Place, Barriers, and Gaps in Congregational Prayer
Discusses conditions for valid following: unity of place, barriers, and gaps.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of unity of place and presence of a barrier or gap to determine the validity of congregational prayer in various scenarios.

Core Idea
Unity of place and absence of a barrier or wide gap are essential for valid following; differences in vertical level or a sufficient barrier prevent invalidity.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of following the imam depends on physical proximity and the absence of obstacles. The source discusses scenarios where followers are at different heights, where a barrier exists, or where a gap without a barrier is present. This lesson explains these rulings and their application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition of unity of place (ittihad al-makan)
If the follower is not on the same level as the imam (e.g., on a platform), the prayer is not invalid due to lack of unity of place.
This applies even if there is no barrier.
2
Identify the effect of a barrier (ha'il)
A barrier such as a pillar, screen, or wall of a minimum size prevents invalidity when there is a misalignment (e.g., women behind men).
Minimum barrier: size of the back of a saddle (approx. a cubit).
3
Learn the ruling on a gap (furjah) without a barrier
A gap wide enough for a man to stand is treated like a barrier; narrower gaps are ignored and may invalidate prayer.
The author (al-Haskafi) does not give it consideration, but the commentator (al-Shurunbulali) and others do.
4
Apply to the scenario of women in the congregation
A row of women between the imam and men invalidates the men's prayer, unless there is a barrier or the women are not in line (e.g., above or below).
Unity of place is negated by different levels.
5
Apply to the scenario of two people returning after wudu
The earlier lesson's scenario also depends on unity of place; if they line up on a different level, prayer is not invalid even if they are in the 'wrong' rak'ah.
The condition of unity of place overrides the qada' order issue.

Then the imam is general to include the latecomer and the one preceded. Their definition of the latecomer: one who catches the first part of the imam's prayer but misses some of it due to an excuse, leniently. But the resident who follows a traveler is a latecomer, and this definition does not include him unless it is said: he is attached to him but not in reality. His ruling when his excuse ends is as stated in al-Majma': he should pray what he caught first (the part he slept through) then complete what he missed. Even if he followed in the remaining part and then completed the missed part and then what he slept through, we deem it permissible. We have stated that it is valid but with sin for leaving an obligatory act. As for the one who is preceded only: he is one who did not catch the first rak'ah with the imam, and his rulings will come later, God willing, at his statement: 'It is valid to appoint the one preceded as substitute.' They said: If two people catch the third rak'ah, then both have an event (ritual impurity) and go for wudu, then they line up with him (the imam) in the remaining prayer, it is considered: if they line up in the first or second (of his remaining rak'ahs), which are the third and fourth for the imam, their prayer is invalid because of shared participation in them, since they are considered latecomers in them. If they line up in the third and fourth (of his remaining), which are the first and second for the imam, it is not invalid due to lack of participation in them since they are preceded in them. This is based on the principle that the latecomer who is preceded first prays what he caught (the part he joined) and then what he missed (the part he was preceded in). This is apparent according to Zufar, and according to us, although the opposite is valid, this is obligatory, so by considering it, it is invalid. It is conditioned by unity of place, because if it differs, then no invalidity, whether there is a barrier or not. For this reason, it is stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if one is on a platform or wall of normal height and the other is on the ground, it is not invalid due to lack of unity of place. Similarly in al-Kafi. It is stated in al-Nawazil: people prayed on the roof of an arcade in the mosque, and below them were women in line with them; their prayer is valid due to lack of unity of place, unlike if the women were in front of them, then it is invalid because there is an intervening row of women between them and the imam, which prevents valid following, as will come. In al-Mujtaba: Women prayed on a ledge of the mosque with rows of men below; their prayer is not invalid. It is conditioned by the absence of a barrier, because if there is a barrier between them and him, there is no invalidity. The minimum barrier is the size of the back of a saddle or its front, because the minimum state of prayer is sitting, so we estimate the barrier by that, which is a cubit's length, as in al-Muhit. In al-Mujtaba: If between them is a pillar or a screen the size of the back of a saddle, or a stick or reed erected as a screen, or a wall or platform of a cubit, it does not invalidate. The explainer mentioned that the minimum is the size of the back of a saddle and its thickness like a finger. The author did not mention the gap without a barrier, and apparently, he gives it no consideration, and that if a woman is to his right or left with a gap between them without a barrier, it invalidates his prayer. Key Terms

فرجة (furjah): An open gap between imam and follower without a physical barrier, which can be treated as a barrier if wide enough for a man to stand.

Women, Barriers, and Gaps in Congregational Prayer
Resolves a seeming contradiction in rulings on women and gaps

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's presence in prayer invalidates the congregation's prayer, and explain the role of alignment (muhadhat) and gaps in determining validity.

Core Idea
A woman's prayer only invalidates the congregation when directly aligned without a gap; a barrier or large gap preserves validity.

This lesson unpacks a problematic case in Hanafi fiqh: according to transmitted rulings, a woman standing opposite the imam invalidates the prayer for everyone, but what if there is a gap? The text resolves the apparent contradiction by clarifying that invalidity requires direct alignment without a gap. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly applying the rules of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problematic case
Read the agreed-upon rulings from Ghayat al-Bayan: a woman opposite the imam invalidates all; a woman in the row invalidates two men on sides and one behind; a woman ahead of imam only invalidates her own prayer. Note the apparent conflict with the later statements about gaps acting as barriers.
The conflict arises because a gap is supposed to act like a barrier, yet the rulings seem to assume no gap.
2
Understand the concept of alignment (muhadhat)
The author explains that invalidity only occurs when there is direct alignment between the woman and the man, with no gap of a man's height. If there is a gap of that size, it is treated as a barrier and prevents invalidity.
Muhadhat means being directly opposite without any separation.
3
Apply the resolution to the problematic case
Apply the condition of alignment: the rulings from Ghayat al-Bayan apply only when the woman stands directly opposite the imam or the men without a gap. If a gap exists, the prayer remains valid for those behind her.
The resolution is taken from al-Fath and al-Nahr, emphasizing that the gap must be the size of a man's height.
4
Distinguish between barrier (ha'il) and gap (furjah)
A physical barrier (e.g., wall of specific dimensions) and a gap of a man's height both prevent invalidity. However, a small gap does not.
This distinction is key: not all gaps are equal; only a gap wide enough for a man to stand suffices.

And it is problematic what they agreed to transmit from our associates, as in Ghayat al-Bayan: If a woman stands opposite the imam while he intends her imamate, it invalidates the prayer of the imam and the congregation. If she stands in the row, it invalidates the prayer of two men on her sides and one man behind her. If she goes ahead of the imam, it does not invalidate the prayer of the imam and the congregation but it invalidates her own prayer. If there is a row of men (not women) between the imam and the men, the men's following of the imam is valid and it is considered a barrier. If there are two women in the row of men, it invalidates the prayer of one man to their right, one to their left, and two men behind them only. If they are three, it invalidates the prayer of three three behind them to the end of the rows and one to their right and one to their left, because three is a valid group (jamm) and thus becomes like a row preventing valid following for those whom they have become intervening between him and his imam. In al-Muhit from al-Jurjani: If she says takbir in the first row, bows in the second, and prostrates in the third, it invalidates the prayer of those to her right, left, and behind in each row because she performed a pillar in each row, so she becomes like one pushed to the row of women. The face of its problem is that the man or the row that is behind her has a gap between them and her the size of a man's height, and they have made the gap like a barrier for those on her side or behind her as we presented from al-Mujtaba and others. Therefore, it must be interpreted as when behind her there is no gap, being aligned with her such that there is not between them a man's height. For this reason he said: And from them: If after completion he knows that their tahrima (opening takbir) differed from the imam's tahrima, the prayer of the masbuq is invalid, and for the lahiq there are two narrations. Similarly if the time of Friday prayer exits. And from them: If the masbuq remembers a missed prayer on him, his prayer is invalid, and for the lahiq there are two narrations. Similarly if both are tayammum and see water or the period of their wiping ends, both their prayers are invalid by agreement. Similarly if Fajr or Eid exits. And from them: If the sun rises during Fajr, it invalidates for the masbuq, not for the lahiq according to the correct view. And from them: If he changes his opinion after the imam finishes, it invalidates for the lahiq, and the masbuq builds upon. And from them: If the imam remembers a missed prayer after finishing, it does not invalidate the masbuq's prayer; the more apparent view for the lahiq is invalidation as in al-Qunyah. His saying: 'And it is problematic what they agreed...' The origin of the problem is taken from al-Fath because he said after quoting the previous expression from al-Diraya, 'And it is not far-fetched to consider the validity of this saying because its implication is that the row of women does not invalidate the row behind it of men.' He said in al-Nahr after it: I say: If the invalidation in the row is interpreted as when the men are opposite them, it becomes straight. And the explainer has conditioned the invalidation of the two behind them as when there is alignment, and no difference appears, so ponder it: meaning there is no difference between two and a row in the condition of alignment. And this is a leaning towards what his brother the author collected in his subsequent saying: 'Therefore it is determined...' His saying: (the size of a man's height) has interpreted the gap earlier as being the size of what a man can stand in.

Commentary
This passage addresses a problematic case in Hanafi fiqh regarding the effect of women's rows on the validity of congregational prayer. The text begins by stating a problem: according to transmitted rulings from the Hanafi school, if a woman stands opposite the imam while he intends her imamate, it invalidates the prayer for everyone. If she stands in the row, it invalidates the prayer of two men on her sides and one behind. However, if there is a row of women between the imam and male followers, but with a gap large enough for a man to stand, the earlier ruling that a gap is like a barrier seems to contradict the agreed-upon practice. The author resolves this by specifying that the invalidation occurs only when the men are directly aligned (muhadhat) without a gap. The text then lists several additional differences between the rulings for the masbuq (preceded) and lahiq (latecomer) in various scenarios, such as when the opening takbir differs, when the time for Friday prayer expires, when a missed prayer is remembered, when tayammum conditions end, when the sun rises during Fajr, when the follower changes intention after the imam finishes, and when the imam remembers a missed prayer after completion. In many of these cases, the ruling differs between masbuq and lahiq, with some having two narrations or a correct view. This passage is from a sharh (expansion) on the rulings of imamate, showing the detailed legal reasoning and resolution of apparent contradictions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muhādāh): Direct alignment or being opposite each other without a gap.
فرجة (furjah): An open gap between the imam and follower that is treated like a barrier if wide enough for a man to stand.
حائل (ḥā'il): A physical barrier of specific minimum dimensions (e.g., a pillar, wall, or screen of a cubit) that separates imam and follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The man's prayer is invalid.
B) The man's prayer is valid because the gap acts as a barrier.
C) The man's prayer is invalid only if he is directly aligned.
D) The woman's prayer becomes valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a woman's presence in prayer invalidates others only when directly aligned without a gap of a man's height; a large gap or barrier preserves validity.

Differing Rulings for Lāḥiq and Masbūq
Lists differences between masbuq and lahiq rulings in various scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the rulings for masbuq and lahiq in various situations, and apply the correct mufta bihi for each.

Core Idea
The masbuq (preceded) and lahiq (latecomer) have different rulings in many scenarios; the lahiq often has two narrations while the masbuq has a clear ruling.

This lesson presents a list of scenarios from the Hanafi school where the rulings for the masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer with the imam) and the lahiq (one who joined late but caught the whole prayer) diverge. Understanding these differences is essential for correctly determining the validity of prayers and the need for repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories: masbuq and lahiq
Masbuq is one who missed at least one rak'ah with the imam and later completes the prayer alone. Lahiq is one who joined from the beginning but was absent for some part (e.g., due to sleep or unconsciousness). The passage lists instances where their rulings differ.
The key distinction: masbuq follows the imam initially, lahiq prays most of the prayer with the imam but misses some due to excuse.
2
List the specific scenarios given
Go through each scenario: (1) differing opening takbir, (2) Friday time exit, (3) remembering missed prayer, (4) tayammum ending, (5) sunrise during Fajr, (6) changing intention, (7) imam remembering missed prayer. For each, note the ruling for masbuq and lahiq.
Some scenarios have 'two narrations' for lahiq, meaning ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Apply the tarjih (preferred ruling) for lahiq
The passage provides the mufta bihi for some cases: e.g., for sunrise, lahiq is not invalidated on the correct view. For others, the text refers to al-Qunyah for the apparent view.
The tarjih authority includes al-Qunyah and the author's asahh.
4
Understand the reason for differences
The differences stem from the nature of the two positions: masbuq's prayer is contingent on the imam's completion, while lahiq's prayer is more independent but affected by his absence. The school has two narrations for lahiq in some cases due to differing analogies.
This ikhtilaf is internal to Hanafi and not between schools.

وكذا لو خرج وقت الجمعة ومنها لو تذكر المسبوق فائتة عليه فسدت صلاته وفي اللاحق روايتان وكذا لو كانا متيممين فرأيا ماء أو انقضت مدة مسحهما فسدت صلاتهما اتفاقاً، وكذا لو خرج الفجر أو العيد ومنها لو طلعت الأثنين وبين الصف في التقييد بالمحاذاة وهذا ميل إلى ما جمع به أخوه المؤلف بقوله الآتي فتعين الخ». قوله : (قدر قامة (الرجل) قد فسر الفرجة فيما مر بأن تكون قدر ما يقوم به
And it is problematic what they agreed to transmit from our associates, as in Ghayat al-Bayan: If a woman stands opposite the imam while he intends her imamate, it invalidates the prayer of the imam and the congregation. If she stands in the row, it invalidates the prayer of two men on her sides and one man behind her. If she goes ahead of the imam, it does not invalidate the prayer of the imam and the congregation but it invalidates her own prayer. If there is a row of men (not women) between the imam and the men, the men's following of the imam is valid and it is considered a barrier. If there are two women in the row of men, it invalidates the prayer of one man to their right, one to their left, and two men behind them only. If they are three, it invalidates the prayer of three three behind them to the end of the rows and one to their right and one to their left, because three is a valid group (jamm) and thus becomes like a row preventing valid following for those whom they have become intervening between him and his imam. In al-Muhit from al-Jurjani: If she says takbir in the first row, bows in the second, and prostrates in the third, it invalidates the prayer of those to her right, left, and behind in each row because she performed a pillar in each row, so she becomes like one pushed to the row of women. The face of its problem is that the man or the row that is behind her has a gap between them and her the size of a man's height, and they have made the gap like a barrier for those on her side or behind her as we presented from al-Mujtaba and others. Therefore, it must be interpreted as when behind her there is no gap, being aligned with her such that there is not between them a man's height. For this reason he said: And from them: If after completion he knows that their tahrima (opening takbir) differed from the imam's tahrima, the prayer of the masbuq is invalid, and for the lahiq there are two narrations. Similarly if the time of Friday prayer exits. And from them: If the masbuq remembers a missed prayer on him, his prayer is invalid, and for the lahiq there are two narrations. Similarly if both are tayammum and see water or the period of their wiping ends, both their prayers are invalid by agreement. Similarly if Fajr or Eid exits. And from them: If the sun rises during Fajr, it invalidates for the masbuq, not for the lahiq according to the correct view. And from them: If he changes his opinion after the imam finishes, it invalidates for the lahiq, and the masbuq builds upon. And from them: If the imam remembers a missed prayer after finishing, it does not invalidate the masbuq's prayer; the more apparent view for the lahiq is invalidation as in al-Qunyah. His saying: 'And it is problematic what they agreed...' The origin of the problem is taken from al-Fath because he said after quoting the previous expression from al-Diraya, 'And it is not far-fetched to consider the validity of this saying because its implication is that the row of women does not invalidate the row behind it of men.' He said in al-Nahr after it: I say: If the invalidation in the row is interpreted as when the men are opposite them, it becomes straight. And the explainer has conditioned the invalidation of the two behind them as when there is alignment, and no difference appears, so ponder it: meaning there is no difference between two and a row in the condition of alignment. And this is a leaning towards what his brother the author collected in his subsequent saying: 'Therefore it is determined...' His saying: (the size of a man's height) has interpreted the gap earlier as being the size of what a man can stand in.
