Ruling on an Adult Praying Behind a Minor
Explains the impermissibility with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on an adult following a child in prayer, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and evaluate the qiyas argument used by the opposing scholars.

Core Idea
A child's prayer is training, not valid prayer, so an adult cannot follow a child in any prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical question: can an adult pray behind a minor (mumayyiz) as imam? The Hanafi school's relied-upon ruling is that it is not permissible in any prayer, but some later Hanafi scholars allowed it in non-obligatory prayers by analogy to a different case. We will unpack the reasoning, the dispute, and the distinguishing factors that led to the chosen position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is an adult standing behind a minor imam. The chosen ruling (mufta bihi) is that it is not permissible (la yajuz) in any prayer, including tarawih and sunnah prayers.
This is a strong prohibition (makruh tahrimi).
2
Understand the core reasoning
The author states 'the stronger cannot follow the weaker.' The minor's nafl prayer is of a lesser status; it is not considered valid prayer but merely training (takhalluq). Therefore the adult's prayer behind him is invalid.
This reasoning applies regardless of the prayer type (fard or nafl).
3
Distinguish from the case of al-ẓān
The objector argues by analogy to a person who assumes a prayer is obligatory (al-ẓān) and then finds it is not; following such an imam is valid as nafl. The author responds that the assumption is incidental, whereas a child's deficiency is inherent. Hence the analogy fails.
The key distinction: one defect is temporary and incidental, the other is permanent and essential.
4
Examine the Balkh scholars' qiyas and the Hanafi rebuttal
Scholars of Balkh (and Imam Muhammad in one narration) permitted an adult following a child in non-obligatory prayers by qiyas to al-ẓān. The Hanafi response in the text is that the qiyas is invalid because the child's prayer is not actually prayer, while the al-ẓān's prayer is valid for iqtida due to his ijtihad.
This qiyas is a clear case of tanqih al-manat: the effective cause is not present in the far'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its implications
The chosen position, supported by al-Marghinani and the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, is absolute impermissibility. The practical consequence: an adult must not follow a minor imam in any prayer; if he does, his prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This is the fatwa that a mufti should give in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى لا يبني يجب القضاء عليه بالإفساد فيكون نفل الصبي دون نفل البالغ فلا يجوز أن القوي على الضعيف، ولا يرد عليه الاقتداء بالظان أي بمن ظن أن عليه فرضاً ثم تبين خلافه فإن الاقتداء به صحيح نفلاً مع أن نفل المقتدي مضمون عليه بالإفساد حتى يلزمه القضاء، ونفل الإمام ليس بمضمون عليه حتى لا يلزمه القضاء لأنه مجتهد في وجوب قضائه على الظان، فإن زفر يقول بوجوبه فاعتبر الظن العارض عدماً في حق المقتدي بخلاف الصبي، ومشايخ بلخ جوزوا اقتداء البالغ بالصبي في غير الفرض قياساً على المظنون وقد علمت جوابه. وفي النهاية والاختلاف راجع إلى أن صلاة الصبي هل هي صلاة أم لا؛ قيل ليست بصلاة وإنما يؤمر بها تخلقاً ولهذا لو صلت المراهقة بغير قناع فإنه يجوز، وقيل هي صلاة ولهذا لو قهقه المراهق في الصلاة يؤمر بالوضوء فظاهره ترجيح أنها ليست بصلاة ولهذا كان المختار عدم جواز الاقتداء به في كل صلاة.
So that he does not build upon it. The compensation is obligatory upon him due to invalidating. Thus the nafl of a child is lesser than the nafl of an adult, so it is not permissible for the stronger to follow the weaker. And the case of following one who assumes does not contradict this, meaning one who assumed that a prayer was obligatory upon him then it became clear otherwise, for following him is valid as nafl, even though the nafl of the follower is guaranteed with respect to invalidation such that compensation becomes obligatory upon him, while the nafl of the imam is not guaranteed such that compensation is not obligatory upon him because he is a mujtahid regarding the obligation of its compensation for the assumer. For Zufar says it is obligatory. So the incidental assumption was considered non-existent regarding the follower, unlike the child. And the scholars of Balkh permitted an adult following a child in non-obligatory prayers by analogy to the case of the assumer, and you have known its answer. And in al-Nihaya: the difference refers back to whether the child's prayer is prayer or not. It is said it is not prayer but rather he is commanded to it for character formation, and therefore if a girl near puberty prays without a headcover it is permissible. And it is said it is prayer, and therefore if a boy near puberty laughs aloud in prayer he is commanded to perform ablution. So its apparent implication is the preponderance that it is not prayer, and thus the chosen position is the impermissibility of following him in every prayer.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of a sane adult praying behind a minor in the Hanafi school. The author explains that the child's nafl prayer is of a lower status than the adult's nafl, so it is not permissible for the stronger to follow the weaker. An exception is made for the case of a person who assumed a prayer was obligatory upon him, but that is distinguished because the assumption was incidental. The scholars of Balkh allowed an adult following a child in non-obligatory prayers by analogy to the case of the assumer, but the relied-upon position is that it is not allowed. The underlying dispute is whether a child's prayer is actually considered valid prayer or merely a practice for discipline. The preponderant view is that it is not prayer, hence following him is invalid in all prayers.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-ṣabī): A minor child who has not reached puberty but is old enough to pray (mumayyiz).
الظان (al-ẓān): One who assumes a particular prayer is obligatory upon him and then finds out it is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, can an adult pray behind a child in taraweeh prayer?
A) Yes, it is permissible
B) No, it is not permissible
C) It is permissible only if the child is baligh
D) It is permissible with a condition

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an adult cannot follow a minor as imam in any prayer because the child's prayer is not considered valid prayer for iqtida; the mufta bihi is absolute impermissibility.

Ruling on a Pure Person Praying Behind an Excused Person
Explains the impermissibility with conditions and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a pure person (tahir) praying behind an excused person (ma'dhur) and apply the conditions that determine validity.

Core Idea
A pure person cannot follow an excused imam because the weaker cannot lead the stronger.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in congregational prayer: can a person who has performed proper wudu (tahir) pray behind an imam who has a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) that prevents him from maintaining purity? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling backed by reasoning. We will explore the base ruling, its rationale, and important exceptions, such as when the ma'dhur performs wudu after the excuse stops or when the follower shares the same excuse.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate between tahir and ma'dhur
Define both terms: a tahir has valid wudu and no ongoing impurity; a ma'dhur has a chronic condition that breaks wudu continuously. Understand why the ma'dhur is considered lower in purity.
The key distinction is the continuous nature of the excuse.
2
Identify the base ruling of iqtida
State that a tahir following a ma'dhur renders the prayer fasid (invalid). The text says 'it is invalid'.
This is the default ruling.
3
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
Understand the proofs: the imam has both hadath and najasa; the tahir is stronger in state; a thing cannot encompass what is above it, and the imam's prayer is supposed to encompass the follower's.
This reasoning is foundational to Hanafi iqtida rulings.
4
Recognize the exceptions
Note that if the ma'dhur performs wudu after his excuse momentarily stops and prays without new hadath, he is considered tahir and can be followed. Also, if a ma'dhur follows another ma'dhur with the identical excuse, it is valid.
5
Apply the ruling to specific examples
Work through cases: pure behind urinary incontinence (invalid), flatulence behind urinary (invalid due to different excuses), mustahada behind mustahada (invalid due to possibility of menstruation), etc.
Practice with examples solidifies the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطاهر بمعذور أي وفسد اقتداء طاهر بصاحب العذر المفوت للطهارة لأن معه حدث ونجاسة ولأن الصحيح أقوى حالاً من المعذور والشيء لا يتضمن ما هو فوقه والإمام ضامن بمعنى تضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي وقيد المعذور في المجتبى بأن يقارن الوضوء الحدث أو يطرأ عليه للاحتراز عما إذا توضأ على الانقطاع وصلى كذلك فإنه يصح الاقتداء به لأنه في حكم الطاهر. وقيد بالطاهر لأن اقتداء المعذور بالمعذور صحيح إن اتحد عذرهما، وأما إن اختلف فلا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات من به سلس البول لأن الإمام ريح ونجاسة فكان الإمام صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر، وكذا لا يصلي من به سلس البول خلف من به انفلات ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وظاهره أن سلس البول والجرح من قبيل المتحد، وكذا سلس البول واستطلاق البطن. وفي المجتبى واقتداء المستحاضة بالمستحاضة والضالة بالضالة لا يجوز كالخنثى المشكل بالمشكل اهـ لعله لجواز أن يكون الإمام حائضاً أما إذا انتفى الاحتمال فينبغي الجواز لأنه من قبيل المتحد وفي الخلاصة وإمامة المفتصد لغيره من الأصحاء صحيحة إذا كان يأمن خروج الدم.
And a pure person following an excused person: i.e., the iqtida of a pure person behind one who has an excuse that prevents purity is invalid, because with the imam there are hadath and najasa, and because the sound person is stronger in state than the excused one, and a thing does not encompass what is above it, and the imam is a guarantor in the sense that his prayer encompasses the prayer of the follower. And the excused person is restricted in al-Mujtaba to the one whose wudu is accompanied by hadath or hadath occurs after it, to exclude the case where he performs wudu after the cessation of the excuse and prays like that; then it is valid to follow him because he is in the ruling of pure. And it is restricted to the pure because the iqtida of an excused person behind an excused person is valid if their excuses are the same, but if they differ it is not permissible. For example, one who has flatulence cannot pray behind one who has urinary incontinence, because the imam has wind and impurity, so the imam has two excuses and the follower has one. Similarly, one with urinary incontinence cannot pray behind one with flatulence and a wound that does not stop bleeding, because the imam has two excuses. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Its apparent meaning is that urinary incontinence and a wound are of the same type, and similarly urinary incontinence and stomach looseness. And in al-Mujtaba: the iqtida of a mustahada behind a mustahada and a dahla behind a dahla is not permissible, like the ambiguous hermaphrodite behind another, perhaps due to the possibility that the imam might be menstruating. But if the possibility is removed, then permissibility is expected because it is of the same type. And in al-Khulasa: the imama of one who is cupped for other healthy persons is valid if he is secure from blood coming out.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of a person who has valid wudu (tahir) praying behind someone who has a chronic excuse that invalidates his purity, such as continuous wind or bleeding (ma'dhur). The Hanafi school rules this invalid because the imam's state is weaker than that of the follower: the imam has both hadath and najasa, while the follower is pure. The principle is that the stronger cannot follow the weaker. However, if the ma'dhur performs wudu after the excuse stops momentarily and prays without any new hadath, he is considered in the ruling of tahir and can be followed. If an excused person follows another excused person, it is valid only if their excuses are identical; if different, it is invalid because the imam may have two excuses while the follower has one, creating an imbalance. Special cases: a mustahada (woman with chronic uterine bleeding) following another mustahada is invalid due to possibility of menstruation, but if that possibility is eliminated, it becomes valid. Similarly, a person with a fresh cupping wound can lead if he is certain no blood will come out.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): A person with a chronic excuse (e.g., continuous wind, incontinence) that prevents maintaining purity.
الطاهر (al-ṭāhir): A person who has performed wudu properly and has no hadath or najasa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person with urinary incontinence leads a person with flatulence, is the prayer valid?
A) Yes, because both are excused
B) No, because their excuses differ
C) Yes, because the imam has only one excuse
D) No, because the follower is stronger

Key Takeaway
A pure person cannot follow an excused imam; excused persons can only follow those with identical excuses.

Ruling on a Qari Praying Behind an Ummi
Ruling statement on imamat hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a qari prays behind an ummi and identify the condition that makes the iqtida invalid.

Core Idea
A qari cannot follow an ummi: the imam must be at least equal in Quranic knowledge.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from the matn of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: if a person has memorized at least one verse of the Quran (a qari), he cannot pray behind an imam who knows no Quran (an ummi). The prayer is invalid and must be repeated. This ruling is based on the hierarchy of recitation ability and is a fundamental principle of Hanafi fiqh regarding imamat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of persons
A qari is one who has memorized at least one verse of the Quran. An ummi is one who cannot recite any portion of the Quran.
2
State the ruling
The iqtida (following) of a qari behind an ummi is fasid (invalid).
3
Understand the condition
For valid iqtida, the imam must not be ummi when the follower is a qari. The imam must be at least equal in recitation ability.
4
Note the consequence
Since the iqtida is invalid, the prayer must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقارئ بأمي أي وفسد اقتداء حافظ الآية من القرآن بمن لا يحسن شيئاً
And a qari behind an ummi: i.e., the iqtida of one who has memorized a verse of the Quran behind one who does not know anything is invalid.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This is a direct ruling from the matn: if a person has memorized at least one verse of the Quran, he cannot pray behind an imam who knows no Quran. The reason is that the qari is more qualified, and the weaker cannot lead the stronger. This is a clear, unquestioned ruling in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الأمي (al-ummī): One who cannot recite any portion of the Quran.
القارئ (al-qāri’): One who has memorized at least one verse of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zaid knows Surah al-Fatiha, while imam Amr knows no Quran. Can Zaid pray behind Amr?
A) Yes, because Zaid can correct him
B) No, it is invalid because Zaid is a qari and Amr is ummi
C) Yes, if Amr follows Zaid's recitation
D) No, unless Zaid is also ummi

Key Takeaway
A qari cannot validly pray behind an imam who knows nothing of the Quran; the iqtida is fasid and must be repeated.

Pure Person Following an Excused Imam
Ruling on pure following an excused imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pure person following an excused imam and explain the condition of unity of excuses for valid following.

Core Idea
A pure person cannot follow an excused imam because the follower's state is stronger, but two excused persons with the same excuse may follow each other.

In this lesson, we examine the first case from the passage: the invalidity of a pure person praying behind an excused imam. The commentator explains the underlying principle and an important exception when both imam and follower share the same excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The following of a pure person (طاهر) by an excused imam (معذور) is invalid (فاسد). The imam has continuous impurity, and the follower is in a stronger state of purity.
The excused person (maʿdhūr) is one with a continuous excuse like urinary incontinence or flatulence that prevents maintaining purity.
2
Understand the rationale
The pure person is stronger (أقوى حالاً) than the excused imam. A thing cannot encompass what is above it, so the imam's prayer cannot encompass the follower's.
3
Note the exception for temporary purity
If the excused imam performs ablution at a time when the impurity has ceased (e.g., after urination stops) and prays before the next occurrence, he is considered like a pure person, and following him becomes valid.
This is from al-Mujtaba's restriction: المقارنة الحدث للوضوء أو الطرآن
4
Explore equality of excuses
If both imam and follower have the same excuse (e.g., both have urinary incontinence), the following is valid. If the excuses differ (e.g., one has urinary incontinence, the other flatulence), it is invalid because the imam may have two excuses.
The example: one with flatulence (انفلات ريح) behind one with urinary incontinence (سلس البول) is invalid because the imam has wind and impurity – two excuses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المعذور في المجتبى بأن يقارن الوضوء الحدث أو يطرأ عليه للاحتراز عما إذا توضأ على الانقطاع وصلى كذلك فإنه يصح الاقتداء به لأنه في حكم الطاهر. وقيد بالطاهر لأن اقتداء المعذور بالمعذور صحيح إن اتحد عذرهما، وأما إن اختلف فلا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات من به سلس البول لأن الإمام ريح ونجاسة فكان الإمام صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر، وكذا لا يصلي من به سلس البول خلف من به انفلات ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وظاهره أن سلس البول والجرح من قبيل المتحد، وكذا سلس البول واستطلاق البطن. وفي المجتبى واقتداء المستحاضة بالمستحاضة والضالة بالضالة لا يجوز كالخنثى المشكل بالمشكل اهـ لعله لجواز أن يكون الإمام حائضاً أما إذا انتفى الاحتمال فينبغي الجواز لأنه من قبيل المتحد وفي الخلاصة وإمامة المفتصد لغيره من الأصحاء صحيحة إذا كان يأمن خروج الدم .اهـ. قوله : ( وقارئ بأمي أي وفسد اقتداء حافظ الآية من القرآن بمن لا يحفظها وهو المسمى بالأمي، فهو عندنا من لا يحسن القراءة المفروضة، وعند الشافعي من لا يحسن الفاتحة وإنما فسد لأن القارئ أقوى حالاً منه لأنه يصلي مع عدم ركنها للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة. وعلم منه أنه لا يجوز اقتداء القارئ بالأخرس بالأولى، وأشار إلى أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الأمي بالأخرس لأن الأمي أقوى حالاً منه لقدرته على التحريمة وإلى جواز اقتداء الأخرس بالأمي. قوله: (ومكتس بعار لأن صلاة العاري جائزة مع فقد الشرط للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي. وفي السراج الوهاج لو قال ولا مستور العورة خلف العاري لكان أولى لأن ستر عورته بالسروال أو نحوه لا يسمى مكتسياً في العرف، وتصح صلاة المكتسي خلفه لأنه مستور العورة .اهـ لكن اختلفوا في السراويل هل يكون كسوة شرعاً في كفارة اليمين، وصحح صاحب الخلاصة أنه لا يجوز للرجل ولا للمرأة أي لا يكون كسوة قيد بالمكتسي لأنه لو أم العاري عراة ولابسين فصلاة الإمام ومن هو مثله جائزة بلا خلاف، وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح بخلاف الأمي إذا أم أمياً وقارئاً فإن صلاة الكل فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأمي يمكن أن يجعل صلاته بقراءة إذا اقتدى بقارئ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة وليست طهارة الإمام وسترته طهارة وسترة للمأموم حكماً فافترقا . قوله: (وغير موم بموم) أي فسد اقتداء من يقدر على الركوع والسجود بمن لا يقدر عليهما للعذر لقوة حال المقتدي، قيد به لأن اقتداء المومي بالمومي صحيح للماثلة كما سيأتي . قوله : ( ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر) أي وفسد اقتداء المفترض بإمام متنفل أو بإمام يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي لأن الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم في حق الإمام في الأولى وهو مشاركة وموافقة فلا بد من الاتحاد وهو معدوم في الثانية، والذي صح وترجح أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نفلاً وبقومه فرضاً لقوله حين شكوا تطویله بهم یا معاذ إما أن تصلي معي وإما أن تخفف على قومك كما رواه الإمام أحمد. فشرع له أحد الأمرين الصلاة معه ولا يصلي بقومه أو الصلاة بقومه على وجه التخفيف ولا هذا حقيقة اللفظ أفاد منعه من الإمامة إذا صلى معه عليه السلام ولا تمتنع إمامته مطلقاً بالاتفاق فعلم الفرض والحاصل أن اتحاد الصلاتين شرط لصحة الاقتداء وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنية صلاة الإمام فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي . وذكر روايتين في اقتداء الخنثى المشكل بمثله قوله : ( وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح) أي وكذا ائتمام صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح والأولى حذف الباء من الموضعين. قوله : (يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي إشارة إلى أن قول المصنف «آخر» ليس صفة المفترض لفساد المعنى وإنما هو صفة لمحذوف أي فرضاً آخر.
His statement: (And a pure person by an excused person) meaning: the following of a pure person by a person with an excuse that removes purity is invalid because the imam has impurity and filth, and the healthy person is in a stronger state than the excused person, and a thing does not encompass what is above it, and the imam is a guarantor in the sense that his prayer includes the prayer of the follower. The excused person in al-Mujtaba is restricted to where the impurity accompanies the ablution or occurs after it, to exclude the case where he performs ablution at the time of cessation and prays accordingly, for then following him is valid because he is in the ruling of a pure person. He restricted it to the pure person because following of an excused person by an excused person is valid if their excuses are the same; but if they differ, it is not permissible for one with flatulence to pray behind one with urinary incontinence because the imam has wind and impurity, so the imam has two excuses and the follower has one excuse. Likewise, one with urinary incontinence should not pray behind one with flatulence and a wound that does not stop bleeding because the imam has two excuses. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Its apparent meaning is that urinary incontinence and wound are of a single type, and likewise urinary incontinence and diarrhea. In al-Mujtaba: the following of a mustahada by a mustahada and a women in istihada [َ؟] by a women in istihada is not permissible, just as the ambiguous hermaphrodite by the ambiguous hermaphrodite. End. Perhaps it is because of the possibility that the imam is menstruating; but if the possibility is negated, then permissibility is appropriate, because it is of a single type. In al-Khulasa: the imamah of one who is cupped for others among the healthy is valid if he is secure from blood coming out. End. His statement: (And a reciter by an illiterate) meaning: the following of one who memorizes a verse of the Quran by one who does not memorize it, who is called illiterate. According to us, the illiterate is one who does not know the obligatory recitation; according to al-Shafi'i, one who does not know al-Fatiha. It is invalid because the reciter is in a stronger state than him, because he prays despite the lack of its pillar due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. It will come that the prayer of an illiterate imam is also invalid according to Abu Hanifa. From this it is known that following of a reciter by a mute is even more invalid, and it is indicated that following of an illiterate by a mute is invalid because the illiterate is in a stronger state than him due to his ability to make the takbir, and that following of an illiterate by a mute is permissible. His statement: (And a clothed person by a naked person) because the prayer of a naked person is valid despite the missing condition due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if he said 'and one whose private parts are covered behind a naked person' it would be more appropriate, because covering his private parts with trousers or the like is not called being clothed in custom, and the prayer of a clothed person behind him is valid because his private parts are covered. End, but they differed regarding trousers: are they considered clothing legally in the expiation of an oath? The author of al-Khulasa deemed that it is not permissible for a man nor a woman, i.e., it is not clothing. He restricted it to the clothed person because if a naked person leads both naked and clothed persons, then the prayer of the imam and those like him is valid without disagreement. Likewise, one with a flowing wound behind his like and behind a healthy person, contrary to the illiterate when he leads an illiterate and a reciter, for the prayer of all is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, because the illiterate can make his prayer by recitation if he follows a reciter, because the imam's recitation is recitation for him, whereas the imam's purification and covering are not purification and covering for the follower in a legal sense, so they differ. His statement: (And a non-signaler by a signaler) i.e., the following of one who is able to bow and prostrate by one who is not able due to an excuse is invalid due to the stronger state of the follower. He restricted it because following of a signaler by a signaler is valid due to similarity, as will come. His statement: (And one praying farḍ by one praying nafl and by another farḍ) i.e., the following of one praying farḍ by an imam praying nafl or by an imam praying a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ is invalid, because following is a structure, and the description of farḍiness is absent in the imam in the first case, and it is participation and agreement, so unity is necessary, and it is absent in the second case. What is deemed correct and preferred is that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray nafl with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and farḍ with his people, because of his statement when they complained about his prolonging: 'O Mu'adh, either pray with me or lighten for your people,' as narrated by Imam Ahmad. So he was given one of two commands: to pray with him and not pray with his people, or to pray with his people with lightening. This does not give the literal meaning, but it indicates his prohibition from leading while praying with him (peace be upon him) and his leadership is not absolutely prohibited by consensus. Thus it is understood that unity of the two prayers is a condition for the validity of following, meaning that he can enter into his prayer with the intention of the imam's prayer, so that the imam's prayer includes the follower's prayer. He mentioned two narrations regarding the following of an ambiguous hermaphrodite by the like. His statement: (And likewise one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person) i.e., likewise the following of one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person, and it is better to omit the 'ba' from both places. His statement: (He prays a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ) indicates that the author's word 'other' is not an adjective of 'muftarid' because that would corrupt the meaning, but rather it is an adjective for an omitted word, i.e., another farḍ.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the rulings of valid and invalid imamah in the Hanafi school. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains a series of cases where a follower's prayer is invalid due to being in a stronger state than the imam. The principle is that the follower must not be superior in purity, recitation, clothing, ability to bow/prostrate, or farḍ status. The commentary elaborates on each type:

1. Pure (طاهر) behind excused (معذور): Invalid because the pure person is stronger. Exception if the excused person maintains continuous purity. If both are excused with the same excuse, it is valid.

2. Reciter (قارئ) behind illiterate (أمي): Invalid because the reciter is stronger. The Hanafi definition of 'ami' is one who cannot recite the obligatory portion. At Abu Hanifa, an illiterate imam also invalidates the prayers of both other illiterate and reciter followers.

3. Clothed (مكتس) behind naked (عاري): Invalid; covering is better. There is a discussion about trousers as covering.

4. One who can bow/prostrate (غير موم) behind one who cannot (موم): Invalid due to the follower's superior ability.

5. One praying farḍ behind an imam praying nafl or a different farḍ: Invalid because unity of prayer type is necessary. The story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is used to derive the ruling.

Throughout, the commentary uses rational proofs (talil) based on the concept of 'قوة الحال' (strength of state) and hadith references (e.g., Mu'adh story). The authority weight is from the established Hanafi school, particularly Abu Hanifa and the sahih riwayah from the companions.

Key Terms
معذور (maʿdhūr): A person with a continuous excuse that prevents maintaining purity, such as urinary incontinence or continuous wind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the prayer of an excused person behind another excused person valid?
A) Always, regardless of the excuse.
B) Only when both have exactly the same continuous excuse.
C) Only when the imam's excuse is stronger.
D) Never, because any excuse invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A pure person cannot follow an excused imam; two excused persons may follow each other only if their excuses are identical.

Reciter Following an Illiterate Imam
Ruling on reciter following an illiterate imam with inter-madhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a reciter following an illiterate imam and explain the inter-madhab dispute on the definition of 'ami'.

Core Idea
A reciter cannot follow an illiterate imam because the reciter is stronger, but the definition of 'illiteracy' differs between Hanafis and Shafi'is.

This lesson covers the second case from the passage: the invalidity of a reciter (one who can recite the obligatory portion) praying behind an illiterate imam. The commentator explains the Hanafi definition of 'ami' and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The following of a reciter (قارئ) by an illiterate imam (أمي) is invalid. The reciter knows the obligatory recitation; the illiterate does not.
The term 'ami' in the Hanafi school means one who cannot recite the obligatory portion of the Quran in prayer.
2
Understand the rationale
The reciter is stronger because he prays with a complete pillar (recitation), while the illiterate prays without it due to necessity. The follower has no such necessity.
3
Define 'ami' according to Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
In the Hanafi school, the obligatory recitation includes at least three short verses or one long verse after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs. In the Shafi'i school, only al-Fatiha is obligatory. Thus, a person who can recite al-Fatiha but not more is 'ami' in Hanafi but not in Shafi'i.
The text says: 'عندنا من لا يحسن القراءة المفروضة، وعند الشافعي من لا يحسن الفاتحة'
4
Note additional ruling on illiterate imam
According to Abu Hanifa, an illiterate imam invalidates the prayer of all followers (including other illiterate and reciters). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad may have a different view (mentioned later).
The passage says 'وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة'.

Source Text

قوله: (وطاهر بمعذور) أي وفسد اقتداء طاهر بصاحب العذر المفوت للطهارة لأن الإمام معه حدث ونجاسة والصحيح أقوى حالاً من المعذور والشيء لا يتضمن ما هو فوقه والإمام ضامن بمعنى تضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي وقيد المعذور في المجتبى بأن يقارن الوضوء الحدث أو يطرأ عليه للاحتراز عما إذا توضأ على الانقطاع وصلى كذلك فإنه يصح الاقتداء به لأنه في حكم الطاهر. وقيد بالطاهر لأن اقتداء المعذور بالمعذور صحيح إن اتحد عذرهما، وأما إن اختلف فلا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات من به سلس البول لأن الإمام ريح ونجاسة فكان الإمام صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر، وكذا لا يصلي من به سلس البول خلف من به انفلات ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وظاهره أن سلس البول والجرح من قبيل المتحد، وكذا سلس البول واستطلاق البطن. وفي المجتبى واقتداء المستحاضة بالمستحاضة والضالة بالضالة لا يجوز كالخنثى المشكل بالمشكل اهـ لعله لجواز أن يكون الإمام حائضاً أما إذا انتفى الاحتمال فينبغي الجواز لأنه من قبيل المتحد وفي الخلاصة وإمامة المفتصد لغيره من الأصحاء صحيحة إذا كان يأمن خروج الدم .اهـ. قوله : ( وقارئ بأمي أي وفسد اقتداء حافظ الآية من القرآن بمن لا يحفظها وهو المسمى بالأمي، فهو عندنا من لا يحسن القراءة المفروضة، وعند الشافعي من لا يحسن الفاتحة وإنما فسد لأن القارئ أقوى حالاً منه لأنه يصلي مع عدم ركنها للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة. وعلم منه أنه لا يجوز اقتداء القارئ بالأخرس بالأولى، وأشار إلى أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الأمي بالأخرس لأن الأمي أقوى حالاً منه لقدرته على التحريمة وإلى جواز اقتداء الأخرس بالأمي. قوله: (ومكتس بعار لأن صلاة العاري جائزة مع فقد الشرط للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي. وفي السراج الوهاج لو قال ولا مستور العورة خلف العاري لكان أولى لأن ستر عورته بالسروال أو نحوه لا يسمى مكتسياً في العرف، وتصح صلاة المكتسي خلفه لأنه مستور العورة .اهـ لكن اختلفوا في السراويل هل يكون كسوة شرعاً في كفارة اليمين، وصحح صاحب الخلاصة أنه لا يجوز للرجل ولا للمرأة أي لا يكون كسوة قيد بالمكتسي لأنه لو أم العاري عراة ولابسين فصلاة الإمام ومن هو مثله جائزة بلا خلاف، وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح بخلاف الأمي إذا أم أمياً وقارئاً فإن صلاة الكل فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأمي يمكن أن يجعل صلاته بقراءة إذا اقتدى بقارئ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة وليست طهارة الإمام وسترته طهارة وسترة للمأموم حكماً فافترقا . قوله: (وغير موم بموم) أي فسد اقتداء من يقدر على الركوع والسجود بمن لا يقدر عليهما للعذر لقوة حال المقتدي، قيد به لأن اقتداء المومي بالمومي صحيح للماثلة كما سيأتي . قوله : ( ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر) أي وفسد اقتداء المفترض بإمام متنفل أو بإمام يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي لأن الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم في حق الإمام في الأولى وهو مشاركة وموافقة فلا بد من الاتحاد وهو معدوم في الثانية، والذي صح وترجح أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نفلاً وبقومه فرضاً لقوله حين شكوا تطویله بهم یا معاذ إما أن تصلي معي وإما أن تخفف على قومك كما رواه الإمام أحمد. فشرع له أحد الأمرين الصلاة معه ولا يصلي بقومه أو الصلاة بقومه على وجه التخفيف ولا هذا حقيقة اللفظ أفاد منعه من الإمامة إذا صلى معه عليه السلام ولا تمتنع إمامته مطلقاً بالاتفاق فعلم الفرض والحاصل أن اتحاد الصلاتين شرط لصحة الاقتداء وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنية صلاة الإمام فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي . وذكر روايتين في اقتداء الخنثى المشكل بمثله قوله : ( وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح) أي وكذا ائتمام صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح والأولى حذف الباء من الموضعين. قوله : (يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي إشارة إلى أن قول المصنف «آخر» ليس صفة المفترض لفساد المعنى وإنما هو صفة لمحذوف أي فرضاً آخر.
His statement: (And a pure person by an excused person) meaning: the following of a pure person by a person with an excuse that removes purity is invalid because the imam has impurity and filth, and the healthy person is in a stronger state than the excused person, and a thing does not encompass what is above it, and the imam is a guarantor in the sense that his prayer includes the prayer of the follower. The excused person in al-Mujtaba is restricted to where the impurity accompanies the ablution or occurs after it, to exclude the case where he performs ablution at the time of cessation and prays accordingly, for then following him is valid because he is in the ruling of a pure person. He restricted it to the pure person because following of an excused person by an excused person is valid if their excuses are the same; but if they differ, it is not permissible for one with flatulence to pray behind one with urinary incontinence because the imam has wind and impurity, so the imam has two excuses and the follower has one excuse. Likewise, one with urinary incontinence should not pray behind one with flatulence and a wound that does not stop bleeding because the imam has two excuses. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Its apparent meaning is that urinary incontinence and wound are of a single type, and likewise urinary incontinence and diarrhea. In al-Mujtaba: the following of a mustahada by a mustahada and a women in istihada [َ؟] by a women in istihada is not permissible, just as the ambiguous hermaphrodite by the ambiguous hermaphrodite. End. Perhaps it is because of the possibility that the imam is menstruating; but if the possibility is negated, then permissibility is appropriate, because it is of a single type. In al-Khulasa: the imamah of one who is cupped for others among the healthy is valid if he is secure from blood coming out. End. His statement: (And a reciter by an illiterate) meaning: the following of one who memorizes a verse of the Quran by one who does not memorize it, who is called illiterate. According to us, the illiterate is one who does not know the obligatory recitation; according to al-Shafi'i, one who does not know al-Fatiha. It is invalid because the reciter is in a stronger state than him, because he prays despite the lack of its pillar due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. It will come that the prayer of an illiterate imam is also invalid according to Abu Hanifa. From this it is known that following of a reciter by a mute is even more invalid, and it is indicated that following of an illiterate by a mute is invalid because the illiterate is in a stronger state than him due to his ability to make the takbir, and that following of an illiterate by a mute is permissible. His statement: (And a clothed person by a naked person) because the prayer of a naked person is valid despite the missing condition due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if he said 'and one whose private parts are covered behind a naked person' it would be more appropriate, because covering his private parts with trousers or the like is not called being clothed in custom, and the prayer of a clothed person behind him is valid because his private parts are covered. End, but they differed regarding trousers: are they considered clothing legally in the expiation of an oath? The author of al-Khulasa deemed that it is not permissible for a man nor a woman, i.e., it is not clothing. He restricted it to the clothed person because if a naked person leads both naked and clothed persons, then the prayer of the imam and those like him is valid without disagreement. Likewise, one with a flowing wound behind his like and behind a healthy person, contrary to the illiterate when he leads an illiterate and a reciter, for the prayer of all is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, because the illiterate can make his prayer by recitation if he follows a reciter, because the imam's recitation is recitation for him, whereas the imam's purification and covering are not purification and covering for the follower in a legal sense, so they differ. His statement: (And a non-signaler by a signaler) i.e., the following of one who is able to bow and prostrate by one who is not able due to an excuse is invalid due to the stronger state of the follower. He restricted it because following of a signaler by a signaler is valid due to similarity, as will come. His statement: (And one praying farḍ by one praying nafl and by another farḍ) i.e., the following of one praying farḍ by an imam praying nafl or by an imam praying a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ is invalid, because following is a structure, and the description of farḍiness is absent in the imam in the first case, and it is participation and agreement, so unity is necessary, and it is absent in the second case. What is deemed correct and preferred is that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray nafl with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and farḍ with his people, because of his statement when they complained about his prolonging: 'O Mu'adh, either pray with me or lighten for your people,' as narrated by Imam Ahmad. So he was given one of two commands: to pray with him and not pray with his people, or to pray with his people with lightening. This does not give the literal meaning, but it indicates his prohibition from leading while praying with him (peace be upon him) and his leadership is not absolutely prohibited by consensus. Thus it is understood that unity of the two prayers is a condition for the validity of following, meaning that he can enter into his prayer with the intention of the imam's prayer, so that the imam's prayer includes the follower's prayer. He mentioned two narrations regarding the following of an ambiguous hermaphrodite by the like. His statement: (And likewise one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person) i.e., likewise the following of one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person, and it is better to omit the 'ba' from both places. His statement: (He prays a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ) indicates that the author's word 'other' is not an adjective of 'muftarid' because that would corrupt the meaning, but rather it is an adjective for an omitted word, i.e., another farḍ.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the rulings of valid and invalid imamah in the Hanafi school. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains a series of cases where a follower's prayer is invalid due to being in a stronger state than the imam. The principle is that the follower must not be superior in purity, recitation, clothing, ability to bow/prostrate, or farḍ status. The commentary elaborates on each type:

1. Pure (طاهر) behind excused (معذور): Invalid because the pure person is stronger. Exception if the excused person maintains continuous purity. If both are excused with the same excuse, it is valid.

2. Reciter (قارئ) behind illiterate (أمي): Invalid because the reciter is stronger. The Hanafi definition of 'ami' is one who cannot recite the obligatory portion. At Abu Hanifa, an illiterate imam also invalidates the prayers of both other illiterate and reciter followers.

3. Clothed (مكتس) behind naked (عاري): Invalid; covering is better. There is a discussion about trousers as covering.

4. One who can bow/prostrate (غير موم) behind one who cannot (موم): Invalid due to the follower's superior ability.

5. One praying farḍ behind an imam praying nafl or a different farḍ: Invalid because unity of prayer type is necessary. The story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is used to derive the ruling.

Throughout, the commentary uses rational proofs (talil) based on the concept of 'قوة الحال' (strength of state) and hadith references (e.g., Mu'adh story). The authority weight is from the established Hanafi school, particularly Abu Hanifa and the sahih riwayah from the companions.

Key Terms
أمي (ummī): One who cannot recite the obligatory portion of the Quran in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is considered an 'ami' (illiterate) in the context of imamah?
A) One who cannot read Arabic.
B) One who cannot recite al-Fatiha correctly.
C) One who cannot recite the obligatory portion of the Quran (al-Fatiha and an additional surah or verses in the first two rak'ahs).
D) One who cannot recite any Quran at all.

Key Takeaway
A reciter cannot follow an illiterate imam; the Hanafi definition of 'ami' is stricter than the Shafi'i.

Clothed Person Following a Naked Imam
Ruling on clothed following a naked imam with discussion on trousers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a clothed person following a naked imam and explain the discussion on trousers as covering.

Core Idea
A clothed person cannot follow a naked imam because the follower is stronger in covering, but trousers may not count as proper clothing in some contexts.

This lesson addresses the third case: the invalidity of a clothed person praying behind a naked imam. The commentator explains the rationale and adds a discussion on whether trousers count as covering for legal purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The following of a clothed person (مكتس) by a naked imam (عاري) is invalid. The clothed person is stronger in terms of covering the private parts.
The naked person prays without covering due to necessity (e.g., no cloth available).
2
Understand the rationale
The naked imam prays without a condition (covering) due to necessity, but the follower has no such necessity, so his state is stronger.
3
Note the better phrasing
The commentator from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj suggests that it would be more appropriate to say 'one whose private parts are covered' (مستور العورة) instead of 'clothed' (مكتس), because wearing trousers is not considered being fully clothed in custom.
4
Discuss trousers as covering
There is a difference of opinion on whether trousers (سراويل) count as clothing (كسوة) in legal contexts like expiation of an oath. The author of al-Khulasa holds that trousers are not clothing for men or women in that context.

قوله: (وطاهر بمعذور) أي وفسد اقتداء طاهر بصاحب العذر المفوت للطهارة لأن الإمام معه حدث ونجاسة والصحيح أقوى حالاً من المعذور والشيء لا يتضمن ما هو فوقه والإمام ضامن بمعنى تضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي وقيد المعذور في المجتبى بأن يقارن الوضوء الحدث أو يطرأ عليه للاحتراز عما إذا توضأ على الانقطاع وصلى كذلك فإنه يصح الاقتداء به لأنه في حكم الطاهر. وقيد بالطاهر لأن اقتداء المعذور بالمعذور صحيح إن اتحد عذرهما، وأما إن اختلف فلا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات من به سلس البول لأن الإمام ريح ونجاسة فكان الإمام صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر، وكذا لا يصلي من به سلس البول خلف من به انفلات ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وظاهره أن سلس البول والجرح من قبيل المتحد، وكذا سلس البول واستطلاق البطن. وفي المجتبى واقتداء المستحاضة بالمستحاضة والضالة بالضالة لا يجوز كالخنثى المشكل بالمشكل اهـ لعله لجواز أن يكون الإمام حائضاً أما إذا انتفى الاحتمال فينبغي الجواز لأنه من قبيل المتحد وفي الخلاصة وإمامة المفتصد لغيره من الأصحاء صحيحة إذا كان يأمن خروج الدم .اهـ. قوله : ( وقارئ بأمي أي وفسد اقتداء حافظ الآية من القرآن بمن لا يحفظها وهو المسمى بالأمي، فهو عندنا من لا يحسن القراءة المفروضة، وعند الشافعي من لا يحسن الفاتحة وإنما فسد لأن القارئ أقوى حالاً منه لأنه يصلي مع عدم ركنها للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة. وعلم منه أنه لا يجوز اقتداء القارئ بالأخرس بالأولى، وأشار إلى أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الأمي بالأخرس لأن الأمي أقوى حالاً منه لقدرته على التحريمة وإلى جواز اقتداء الأخرس بالأمي. قوله: (ومكتس بعار لأن صلاة العاري جائزة مع فقد الشرط للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي. وفي السراج الوهاج لو قال ولا مستور العورة خلف العاري لكان أولى لأن ستر عورته بالسروال أو نحوه لا يسمى مكتسياً في العرف، وتصح صلاة المكتسي خلفه لأنه مستور العورة .اهـ لكن اختلفوا في السراويل هل يكون كسوة شرعاً في كفارة اليمين، وصحح صاحب الخلاصة أنه لا يجوز للرجل ولا للمرأة أي لا يكون كسوة قيد بالمكتسي لأنه لو أم العاري عراة ولابسين فصلاة الإمام ومن هو مثله جائزة بلا خلاف، وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح بخلاف الأمي إذا أم أمياً وقارئاً فإن صلاة الكل فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأمي يمكن أن يجعل صلاته بقراءة إذا اقتدى بقارئ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة وليست طهارة الإمام وسترته طهارة وسترة للمأموم حكماً فافترقا . قوله: (وغير موم بموم) أي فسد اقتداء من يقدر على الركوع والسجود بمن لا يقدر عليهما للعذر لقوة حال المقتدي، قيد به لأن اقتداء المومي بالمومي صحيح للماثلة كما سيأتي . قوله : ( ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر) أي وفسد اقتداء المفترض بإمام متنفل أو بإمام يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي لأن الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم في حق الإمام في الأولى وهو مشاركة وموافقة فلا بد من الاتحاد وهو معدوم في الثانية، والذي صح وترجح أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نفلاً وبقومه فرضاً لقوله حين شكوا تطویله بهم یا معاذ إما أن تصلي معي وإما أن تخفف على قومك كما رواه الإمام أحمد. فشرع له أحد الأمرين الصلاة معه ولا يصلي بقومه أو الصلاة بقومه على وجه التخفيف ولا هذا حقيقة اللفظ أفاد منعه من الإمامة إذا صلى معه عليه السلام ولا تمتنع إمامته مطلقاً بالاتفاق فعلم الفرض والحاصل أن اتحاد الصلاتين شرط لصحة الاقتداء وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنية صلاة الإمام فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي . وذكر روايتين في اقتداء الخنثى المشكل بمثله قوله : ( وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح) أي وكذا ائتمام صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح والأولى حذف الباء من الموضعين. قوله : (يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي إشارة إلى أن قول المصنف «آخر» ليس صفة المفترض لفساد المعنى وإنما هو صفة لمحذوف أي فرضاً آخر.
His statement: (And a pure person by an excused person) meaning: the following of a pure person by a person with an excuse that removes purity is invalid because the imam has impurity and filth, and the healthy person is in a stronger state than the excused person, and a thing does not encompass what is above it, and the imam is a guarantor in the sense that his prayer includes the prayer of the follower. The excused person in al-Mujtaba is restricted to where the impurity accompanies the ablution or occurs after it, to exclude the case where he performs ablution at the time of cessation and prays accordingly, for then following him is valid because he is in the ruling of a pure person. He restricted it to the pure person because following of an excused person by an excused person is valid if their excuses are the same; but if they differ, it is not permissible for one with flatulence to pray behind one with urinary incontinence because the imam has wind and impurity, so the imam has two excuses and the follower has one excuse. Likewise, one with urinary incontinence should not pray behind one with flatulence and a wound that does not stop bleeding because the imam has two excuses. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Its apparent meaning is that urinary incontinence and wound are of a single type, and likewise urinary incontinence and diarrhea. In al-Mujtaba: the following of a mustahada by a mustahada and a women in istihada [َ؟] by a women in istihada is not permissible, just as the ambiguous hermaphrodite by the ambiguous hermaphrodite. End. Perhaps it is because of the possibility that the imam is menstruating; but if the possibility is negated, then permissibility is appropriate, because it is of a single type. In al-Khulasa: the imamah of one who is cupped for others among the healthy is valid if he is secure from blood coming out. End. His statement: (And a reciter by an illiterate) meaning: the following of one who memorizes a verse of the Quran by one who does not memorize it, who is called illiterate. According to us, the illiterate is one who does not know the obligatory recitation; according to al-Shafi'i, one who does not know al-Fatiha. It is invalid because the reciter is in a stronger state than him, because he prays despite the lack of its pillar due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. It will come that the prayer of an illiterate imam is also invalid according to Abu Hanifa. From this it is known that following of a reciter by a mute is even more invalid, and it is indicated that following of an illiterate by a mute is invalid because the illiterate is in a stronger state than him due to his ability to make the takbir, and that following of an illiterate by a mute is permissible. His statement: (And a clothed person by a naked person) because the prayer of a naked person is valid despite the missing condition due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if he said 'and one whose private parts are covered behind a naked person' it would be more appropriate, because covering his private parts with trousers or the like is not called being clothed in custom, and the prayer of a clothed person behind him is valid because his private parts are covered. End, but they differed regarding trousers: are they considered clothing legally in the expiation of an oath? The author of al-Khulasa deemed that it is not permissible for a man nor a woman, i.e., it is not clothing. He restricted it to the clothed person because if a naked person leads both naked and clothed persons, then the prayer of the imam and those like him is valid without disagreement. Likewise, one with a flowing wound behind his like and behind a healthy person, contrary to the illiterate when he leads an illiterate and a reciter, for the prayer of all is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, because the illiterate can make his prayer by recitation if he follows a reciter, because the imam's recitation is recitation for him, whereas the imam's purification and covering are not purification and covering for the follower in a legal sense, so they differ. His statement: (And a non-signaler by a signaler) i.e., the following of one who is able to bow and prostrate by one who is not able due to an excuse is invalid due to the stronger state of the follower. He restricted it because following of a signaler by a signaler is valid due to similarity, as will come. His statement: (And one praying farḍ by one praying nafl and by another farḍ) i.e., the following of one praying farḍ by an imam praying nafl or by an imam praying a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ is invalid, because following is a structure, and the description of farḍiness is absent in the imam in the first case, and it is participation and agreement, so unity is necessary, and it is absent in the second case. What is deemed correct and preferred is that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray nafl with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and farḍ with his people, because of his statement when they complained about his prolonging: 'O Mu'adh, either pray with me or lighten for your people,' as narrated by Imam Ahmad. So he was given one of two commands: to pray with him and not pray with his people, or to pray with his people with lightening. This does not give the literal meaning, but it indicates his prohibition from leading while praying with him (peace be upon him) and his leadership is not absolutely prohibited by consensus. Thus it is understood that unity of the two prayers is a condition for the validity of following, meaning that he can enter into his prayer with the intention of the imam's prayer, so that the imam's prayer includes the follower's prayer. He mentioned two narrations regarding the following of an ambiguous hermaphrodite by the like. His statement: (And likewise one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person) i.e., likewise the following of one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person, and it is better to omit the 'ba' from both places. His statement: (He prays a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ) indicates that the author's word 'other' is not an adjective of 'muftarid' because that would corrupt the meaning, but rather it is an adjective for an omitted word, i.e., another farḍ.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the rulings of valid and invalid imamah in the Hanafi school. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains a series of cases where a follower's prayer is invalid due to being in a stronger state than the imam. The principle is that the follower must not be superior in purity, recitation, clothing, ability to bow/prostrate, or farḍ status. The commentary elaborates on each type:

1. Pure (طاهر) behind excused (معذور): Invalid because the pure person is stronger. Exception if the excused person maintains continuous purity. If both are excused with the same excuse, it is valid.

2. Reciter (قارئ) behind illiterate (أمي): Invalid because the reciter is stronger. The Hanafi definition of 'ami' is one who cannot recite the obligatory portion. At Abu Hanifa, an illiterate imam also invalidates the prayers of both other illiterate and reciter followers.

3. Clothed (مكتس) behind naked (عاري): Invalid; covering is better. There is a discussion about trousers as covering.

4. One who can bow/prostrate (غير موم) behind one who cannot (موم): Invalid due to the follower's superior ability.

5. One praying farḍ behind an imam praying nafl or a different farḍ: Invalid because unity of prayer type is necessary. The story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is used to derive the ruling.

Throughout, the commentary uses rational proofs (talil) based on the concept of 'قوة الحال' (strength of state) and hadith references (e.g., Mu'adh story). The authority weight is from the established Hanafi school, particularly Abu Hanifa and the sahih riwayah from the companions.

Key Terms
مكتس (muktas): One who is clothed, i.e., wearing sufficient clothing to cover the private parts and more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refinement from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, what is the preferred expression for the ruling?
A) A clothed person cannot follow a naked imam.
B) A person whose private parts are covered cannot follow a naked imam.
C) A person with trousers cannot follow a naked imam.
D) A person with a shirt cannot follow a naked imam.

Key Takeaway
A clothed person cannot follow a naked imam, but the definition of 'clothed' is custom-based and may exclude mere covering of private parts with trousers.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
5 min
Able to Bow/Prostrate Following a Signaler Imam
Ruling on able-bodied following a signaler imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a person who can bow and prostrate following an imam who prays by gestures.

Core Idea
A person who can bow and prostrate cannot follow an imam who signals, because the follower has more physical ability.

This lesson covers the fourth case: the invalidity of a person who is able to perform the physical pillars of prayer (bowing and prostration) following an imam who is physically unable and prays by gestures. The principle of strength of state applies again.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The following of a person who can bow and prostrate (غير مومئ) by an imam who cannot (مومئ) is invalid. The follower is physically stronger.
The imam signals with his head or eyes due to illness or disability.
2
Understand the rationale
The follower can perform the pillars fully while the imam does them by gestures due to necessity. The follower has no such necessity.
3
Note validity when similar
If both imam and follower are unable and pray by gestures, the following is valid due to equality. The text says 'qayyada bihi li-anna iqtida' al-mu'mi bi al-mu'mi sahih li al-mathala'.

للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة. وعلم منه أنه لا يجوز اقتداء القارئ بالأخرس بالأولى، وأشار إلى أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الأمي بالأخرس لأن الأمي أقوى حالاً منه لقدرته على التحريمة وإلى جواز اقتداء الأخرس بالأمي. قوله: (ومكتس بعار لأن صلاة العاري جائزة مع فقد الشرط للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي. وفي السراج الوهاج لو قال ولا مستور العورة خلف العاري لكان أولى لأن ستر عورته بالسروال أو نحوه لا يسمى مكتسياً في العرف، وتصح صلاة المكتسي خلفه لأنه مستور العورة .اهـ لكن اختلفوا في السراويل هل يكون كسوة شرعاً في كفارة اليمين، وصحح صاحب الخلاصة أنه لا يجوز للرجل ولا للمرأة أي لا يكون كسوة قيد بالمكتسي لأنه لو أم العاري عراة ولابسين فصلاة الإمام ومن هو مثله جائزة بلا خلاف، وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح بخلاف الأمي إذا أم أمياً وقارئاً فإن صلاة الكل فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأمي يمكن أن يجعل صلاته بقراءة إذا اقتدى بقارئ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة وليست طهارة الإمام وسترته طهارة وسترة للمأموم حكماً فافترقا . قوله: (وغير موم بموم) أي فسد اقتداء من يقدر على الركوع والسجود بمن لا يقدر عليهما للعذر لقوة حال المقتدي، قيد به لأن اقتداء المومي بالمومي صحيح للماثلة كما سيأتي . قوله : ( ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر) أي وفسد اقتداء المفترض بإمام متنفل أو بإمام يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي لأن الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم في حق الإمام في الأولى وهو مشاركة وموافقة فلا بد من الاتحاد وهو معدوم في الثانية، والذي صح وترجح أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نفلاً وبقومه فرضاً لقوله حين شكوا تطویله بهم یا معاذ إما أن تصلي معي وإما أن تخفف على قومك كما رواه الإمام أحمد. فشرع له أحد الأمرين الصلاة معه ولا يصلي بقومه أو الصلاة بقومه على وجه التخفيف ولا هذا حقيقة اللفظ أفاد منعه من الإمامة إذا صلى معه عليه السلام ولا تمتنع إمامته مطلقاً بالاتفاق فعلم الفرض والحاصل أن اتحاد الصلاتين شرط لصحة الاقتداء وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنية صلاة الإمام فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي . وذكر روايتين في اقتداء الخنثى المشكل بمثله قوله : ( وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح) أي وكذا ائتمام صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح والأولى حذف الباء من الموضعين. قوله : (يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي إشارة إلى أن قول المصنف «آخر» ليس صفة المفترض لفساد المعنى وإنما هو صفة لمحذوف أي فرضاً آخر.

Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the rulings of valid and invalid imamah in the Hanafi school. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains a series of cases where a follower's prayer is invalid due to being in a stronger state than the imam. The principle is that the follower must not be superior in purity, recitation, clothing, ability to bow/prostrate, or farḍ status. The commentary elaborates on each type:

1. Pure (طاهر) behind excused (معذور): Invalid because the pure person is stronger. Exception if the excused person maintains continuous purity. If both are excused with the same excuse, it is valid.

2. Reciter (قارئ) behind illiterate (أمي): Invalid because the reciter is stronger. The Hanafi definition of 'ami' is one who cannot recite the obligatory portion. At Abu Hanifa, an illiterate imam also invalidates the prayers of both other illiterate and reciter followers.

3. Clothed (مكتس) behind naked (عاري): Invalid; covering is better. There is a discussion about trousers as covering.

4. One who can bow/prostrate (غير موم) behind one who cannot (موم): Invalid due to the follower's superior ability.

5. One praying farḍ behind an imam praying nafl or a different farḍ: Invalid because unity of prayer type is necessary. The story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is used to derive the ruling.

Throughout, the commentary uses rational proofs (talil) based on the concept of 'قوة الحال' (strength of state) and hadith references (e.g., Mu'adh story). The authority weight is from the established Hanafi school, particularly Abu Hanifa and the sahih riwayah from the companions.

Key Terms
مومئ (mūmiʾ): One who prays by gestures (signaling) due to inability to bow and prostrate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the following of a signaler by a signaler valid?
A) Never, because signaling is not a valid prayer.
B) Always, regardless of the degree of disability.
C) Only when both have the same degree of disability.
D) Valid because of similarity (الماثلة).

Key Takeaway
A person who can bow and prostrate cannot follow an imam who signals; only those with equal inability can follow each other.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
One Praying Farḍ Following an Imam Praying Nafl or Different Farḍ
Ruling on farḍ behind nafl or different farḍ with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a person performing farḍ following an imam performing nafl or a different farḍ, and explain the hadith evidence from Mu'adh ibn Jabal.

Core Idea
Unity of prayer type (farḍ or nafl) is essential for valid following; one performing farḍ cannot follow an imam praying nafl or a different farḍ.

This lesson addresses the fifth case: the invalidity of a person performing farḍ prayer following an imam who is praying nafl (supererogatory) or a different farḍ prayer. The commentator provides the story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal as proof and explains the principle of unity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The following of a person praying farḍ by an imam praying nafl or by an imam praying a different farḍ (e.g., Zuhr behind Asr) is invalid.
2
Understand the rationale
Following is based on inclusion (tadamman) and agreement (muwafaqa). The imam's prayer must be able to encompass the follower's prayer. If the imam is praying nafl, he lacks the obligation (farḍiyya) that the follower has, so inclusion fails. If the imam is praying a different farḍ, the prayers are different in time and type, so no agreement.
3
Analyze the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal
The Prophet said to Mu'adh: 'Either pray with me or lighten for your people.' This implies that if Mu'adh prayed with the Prophet (nafl for him) and then led his people in farḍ, his imamah would be problematic. The hadith indicates the requirement of unity of prayer type.
The hadith is narrated by Imam Ahmad in his Musnad.
4
Note the exception of equality
If both imam and follower are praying the same farḍ (e.g., both Zuhr), it is valid. If both are praying nafl, it is valid. The issue is only when the types differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وطاهر بمعذور) أي وفسد اقتداء طاهر بصاحب العذر المفوت للطهارة لأن الإمام معه حدث ونجاسة والصحيح أقوى حالاً من المعذور والشيء لا يتضمن ما هو فوقه والإمام ضامن بمعنى تضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي وقيد المعذور في المجتبى بأن يقارن الوضوء الحدث أو يطرأ عليه للاحتراز عما إذا توضأ على الانقطاع وصلى كذلك فإنه يصح الاقتداء به لأنه في حكم الطاهر. وقيد بالطاهر لأن اقتداء المعذور بالمعذور صحيح إن اتحد عذرهما، وأما إن اختلف فلا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات من به سلس البول لأن الإمام ريح ونجاسة فكان الإمام صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر، وكذا لا يصلي من به سلس البول خلف من به انفلات ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وظاهره أن سلس البول والجرح من قبيل المتحد، وكذا سلس البول واستطلاق البطن. وفي المجتبى واقتداء المستحاضة بالمستحاضة والضالة بالضالة لا يجوز كالخنثى المشكل بالمشكل اهـ لعله لجواز أن يكون الإمام حائضاً أما إذا انتفى الاحتمال فينبغي الجواز لأنه من قبيل المتحد وفي الخلاصة وإمامة المفتصد لغيره من الأصحاء صحيحة إذا كان يأمن خروج الدم .اهـ. قوله : ( وقارئ بأمي أي وفسد اقتداء حافظ الآية من القرآن بمن لا يحفظها وهو المسمى بالأمي، فهو عندنا من لا يحسن القراءة المفروضة، وعند الشافعي من لا يحسن الفاتحة وإنما فسد لأن القارئ أقوى حالاً منه لأنه يصلي مع عدم ركنها للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة. وعلم منه أنه لا يجوز اقتداء القارئ بالأخرس بالأولى، وأشار إلى أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الأمي بالأخرس لأن الأمي أقوى حالاً منه لقدرته على التحريمة وإلى جواز اقتداء الأخرس بالأمي. قوله: (ومكتس بعار لأن صلاة العاري جائزة مع فقد الشرط للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي. وفي السراج الوهاج لو قال ولا مستور العورة خلف العاري لكان أولى لأن ستر عورته بالسروال أو نحوه لا يسمى مكتسياً في العرف، وتصح صلاة المكتسي خلفه لأنه مستور العورة .اهـ لكن اختلفوا في السراويل هل يكون كسوة شرعاً في كفارة اليمين، وصحح صاحب الخلاصة أنه لا يجوز للرجل ولا للمرأة أي لا يكون كسوة قيد بالمكتسي لأنه لو أم العاري عراة ولابسين فصلاة الإمام ومن هو مثله جائزة بلا خلاف، وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح بخلاف الأمي إذا أم أمياً وقارئاً فإن صلاة الكل فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأمي يمكن أن يجعل صلاته بقراءة إذا اقتدى بقارئ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة وليست طهارة الإمام وسترته طهارة وسترة للمأموم حكماً فافترقا . قوله: (وغير موم بموم) أي فسد اقتداء من يقدر على الركوع والسجود بمن لا يقدر عليهما للعذر لقوة حال المقتدي، قيد به لأن اقتداء المومي بالمومي صحيح للماثلة كما سيأتي . قوله : ( ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر) أي وفسد اقتداء المفترض بإمام متنفل أو بإمام يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي لأن الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم في حق الإمام في الأولى وهو مشاركة وموافقة فلا بد من الاتحاد وهو معدوم في الثانية، والذي صح وترجح أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نفلاً وبقومه فرضاً لقوله حين شكوا تطویله بهم یا معاذ إما أن تصلي معي وإما أن تخفف على قومك كما رواه الإمام أحمد. فشرع له أحد الأمرين الصلاة معه ولا يصلي بقومه أو الصلاة بقومه على وجه التخفيف ولا هذا حقيقة اللفظ أفاد منعه من الإمامة إذا صلى معه عليه السلام ولا تمتنع إمامته مطلقاً بالاتفاق فعلم الفرض والحاصل أن اتحاد الصلاتين شرط لصحة الاقتداء وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنية صلاة الإمام فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي . وذكر روايتين في اقتداء الخنثى المشكل بمثله قوله : ( وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح) أي وكذا ائتمام صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح والأولى حذف الباء من الموضعين. قوله : (يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي إشارة إلى أن قول المصنف «آخر» ليس صفة المفترض لفساد المعنى وإنما هو صفة لمحذوف أي فرضاً آخر.
His statement: (And a pure person by an excused person) meaning: the following of a pure person by a person with an excuse that removes purity is invalid because the imam has impurity and filth, and the healthy person is in a stronger state than the excused person, and a thing does not encompass what is above it, and the imam is a guarantor in the sense that his prayer includes the prayer of the follower. The excused person in al-Mujtaba is restricted to where the impurity accompanies the ablution or occurs after it, to exclude the case where he performs ablution at the time of cessation and prays accordingly, for then following him is valid because he is in the ruling of a pure person. He restricted it to the pure person because following of an excused person by an excused person is valid if their excuses are the same; but if they differ, it is not permissible for one with flatulence to pray behind one with urinary incontinence because the imam has wind and impurity, so the imam has two excuses and the follower has one excuse. Likewise, one with urinary incontinence should not pray behind one with flatulence and a wound that does not stop bleeding because the imam has two excuses. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Its apparent meaning is that urinary incontinence and wound are of a single type, and likewise urinary incontinence and diarrhea. In al-Mujtaba: the following of a mustahada by a mustahada and a women in istihada [َ؟] by a women in istihada is not permissible, just as the ambiguous hermaphrodite by the ambiguous hermaphrodite. End. Perhaps it is because of the possibility that the imam is menstruating; but if the possibility is negated, then permissibility is appropriate, because it is of a single type. In al-Khulasa: the imamah of one who is cupped for others among the healthy is valid if he is secure from blood coming out. End. His statement: (And a reciter by an illiterate) meaning: the following of one who memorizes a verse of the Quran by one who does not memorize it, who is called illiterate. According to us, the illiterate is one who does not know the obligatory recitation; according to al-Shafi'i, one who does not know al-Fatiha. It is invalid because the reciter is in a stronger state than him, because he prays despite the lack of its pillar due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. It will come that the prayer of an illiterate imam is also invalid according to Abu Hanifa. From this it is known that following of a reciter by a mute is even more invalid, and it is indicated that following of an illiterate by a mute is invalid because the illiterate is in a stronger state than him due to his ability to make the takbir, and that following of an illiterate by a mute is permissible. His statement: (And a clothed person by a naked person) because the prayer of a naked person is valid despite the missing condition due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if he said 'and one whose private parts are covered behind a naked person' it would be more appropriate, because covering his private parts with trousers or the like is not called being clothed in custom, and the prayer of a clothed person behind him is valid because his private parts are covered. End, but they differed regarding trousers: are they considered clothing legally in the expiation of an oath? The author of al-Khulasa deemed that it is not permissible for a man nor a woman, i.e., it is not clothing. He restricted it to the clothed person because if a naked person leads both naked and clothed persons, then the prayer of the imam and those like him is valid without disagreement. Likewise, one with a flowing wound behind his like and behind a healthy person, contrary to the illiterate when he leads an illiterate and a reciter, for the prayer of all is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, because the illiterate can make his prayer by recitation if he follows a reciter, because the imam's recitation is recitation for him, whereas the imam's purification and covering are not purification and covering for the follower in a legal sense, so they differ. His statement: (And a non-signaler by a signaler) i.e., the following of one who is able to bow and prostrate by one who is not able due to an excuse is invalid due to the stronger state of the follower. He restricted it because following of a signaler by a signaler is valid due to similarity, as will come. His statement: (And one praying farḍ by one praying nafl and by another farḍ) i.e., the following of one praying farḍ by an imam praying nafl or by an imam praying a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ is invalid, because following is a structure, and the description of farḍiness is absent in the imam in the first case, and it is participation and agreement, so unity is necessary, and it is absent in the second case. What is deemed correct and preferred is that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray nafl with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and farḍ with his people, because of his statement when they complained about his prolonging: 'O Mu'adh, either pray with me or lighten for your people,' as narrated by Imam Ahmad. So he was given one of two commands: to pray with him and not pray with his people, or to pray with his people with lightening. This does not give the literal meaning, but it indicates his prohibition from leading while praying with him (peace be upon him) and his leadership is not absolutely prohibited by consensus. Thus it is understood that unity of the two prayers is a condition for the validity of following, meaning that he can enter into his prayer with the intention of the imam's prayer, so that the imam's prayer includes the follower's prayer. He mentioned two narrations regarding the following of an ambiguous hermaphrodite by the like. His statement: (And likewise one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person) i.e., likewise the following of one with a flowing wound by his like and by a healthy person, and it is better to omit the 'ba' from both places. His statement: (He prays a farḍ other than the follower's farḍ) indicates that the author's word 'other' is not an adjective of 'muftarid' because that would corrupt the meaning, but rather it is an adjective for an omitted word, i.e., another farḍ.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the rulings of valid and invalid imamah in the Hanafi school. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains a series of cases where a follower's prayer is invalid due to being in a stronger state than the imam. The principle is that the follower must not be superior in purity, recitation, clothing, ability to bow/prostrate, or farḍ status. The commentary elaborates on each type:

1. Pure (طاهر) behind excused (معذور): Invalid because the pure person is stronger. Exception if the excused person maintains continuous purity. If both are excused with the same excuse, it is valid.

2. Reciter (قارئ) behind illiterate (أمي): Invalid because the reciter is stronger. The Hanafi definition of 'ami' is one who cannot recite the obligatory portion. At Abu Hanifa, an illiterate imam also invalidates the prayers of both other illiterate and reciter followers.

3. Clothed (مكتس) behind naked (عاري): Invalid; covering is better. There is a discussion about trousers as covering.

4. One who can bow/prostrate (غير موم) behind one who cannot (موم): Invalid due to the follower's superior ability.

5. One praying farḍ behind an imam praying nafl or a different farḍ: Invalid because unity of prayer type is necessary. The story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is used to derive the ruling.

Throughout, the commentary uses rational proofs (talil) based on the concept of 'قوة الحال' (strength of state) and hadith references (e.g., Mu'adh story). The authority weight is from the established Hanafi school, particularly Abu Hanifa and the sahih riwayah from the companions.

Key Terms
متنفل (mutanawwil): One who is performing a nafl (supererogatory) prayer.
مفترض (muftarid): One who is performing a farḍ (obligatory) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the essential condition for valid following in terms of prayer type according to the Hanafi school?
A) The imam and follower must pray the same number of rak'ahs.
B) There must be unity of the two prayers (i.e., both must be the same specific prayer).
C) The imam must be praying a farḍ prayer.
D) The follower must pray the same prayer that the imam intended.

Key Takeaway
Unity of the specific prayer type is essential; a farḍ follower cannot follow a nafl imam or an imam praying a different farḍ.
