Definition and Ruling of the Illiterate Imam (الأمي)
Definition and ruling on imamah of the illiterate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'al-ummi' according to the Hanafi school, state the ruling on the imamah of an illiterate person, and explain the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i definitions.

Core Idea
An illiterate imam's prayer is valid only for himself due to necessity, but a literate follower's prayer behind him is invalid.

This lesson defines the key term 'al-ummi' (illiterate) as it relates to leading prayer. We will distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i definitions and understand why a literate person cannot follow an illiterate imam. We will also compare the illiterate to the deaf-mute to see the underlying principle at work.

Guided Path
1
Define al-ummi
Identify the Hanafi definition: one who cannot recite the obligatory portion of the Quran (al-Fatiha and a sura) well. Contrast with the Shafi'i definition that limits it to not knowing al-Fatiha.
The Hanafi definition is broader; the Shafi'i view is also noted in the source.
2
Identify the ruling
Determine why the prayer of a literate follower behind an illiterate imam is fasid. The imam's recitation deficiency makes his prayer valid only due to necessity; the follower has no such necessity.
The proof is qiyas: the reciter is stronger, so invalid.
3
Distinguish the imam's vs follower's status
Note that according to Abu Hanifa, the illiterate imam's own prayer is also invalid; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is valid. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.
This intra-Hanafi disagreement is important for determining who can lead.
4
Compare to the deaf-mute
Apply the rule a fortiori: if following an illiterate (who can say takbir) is invalid, then following a deaf-mute (who cannot even say takbir) is even more invalid. However, an illiterate may follow a deaf-mute? Actually the text says illiterate may not follow deaf-mute, but deaf-mute may follow illiterate.
The hierarchy of ability matters in imamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة وقائم من يحفظها وهو المسمى بالأمي، فهو عندنا من لا يحسن القراءة المفروضة، وعند الشافعي من لا يحسن الفاتحة وإنما فسد لأن القارئ أقوى حالاً منه لأنه يصلي مع عدم ركنها للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي وسيأتي أن صلاة الأمي الإمام تفسد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة. وعلم منه أنه لا يجوز اقتداء القارئ بالأخرس بالأولى، وأشار إلى أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الأمي بالأخرس لأن الأمي أقوى حالاً منه لقدرته على التحريمة وإلى جواز اقتداء الأخرس بالأمي.
Book of Prayer - Chapter of Leadership: And one who stands who knows it [the Quran] and is called the illiterate (al-ummi). According to us, he is one who does not know the obligatory recitation well. According to al-Shafi'i, he is one who does not know al-Fatiha. It is invalid because the reciter is stronger in state than him, as he prays without its pillar due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. It will come that the prayer of the illiterate imam is also invalid according to Abu Hanifa. From this it is understood that the follower who is a reciter may not follow a deaf-mute a fortiori. He indicated that an illiterate may not follow a deaf-mute because the illiterate is stronger in state due to his ability to say the takbir, and that it is permissible for a deaf-mute to follow an illiterate.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage defines the illiterate person (al-ummi) in Hanafi fiqh as one who does not know the obligatory recitation in prayer (i.e., al-Fatiha and a sura). It contrasts with the Shafi'i definition that limits it to not knowing al-Fatiha. The ruling is that a literate follower may not pray behind an illiterate imam because the imam's prayer is valid only due to necessity (the inability to recite), but the follower has no such necessity. The same applies to a deaf-mute, who is even weaker. The passage also explains that an illiterate may not follow a deaf-mute because the illiterate can at least say the opening takbir, making him stronger.

Key Terms
الأمي (al-ummi): One who does not recite the obligatory portion of the Quran in prayer (al-Fatiha and a sura) well enough to be valid.
الأخرس (al-akhras): A person who is born mute or unable to speak, thus cannot recite even the takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the criterion for being considered 'ummi' (illiterate) in the context of imamah?
A) Not being able to recite al-Fatiha at all
B) Not being able to recite the obligatory portion of the Quran (al-Fatiha and a sura) well
C) Being unable to read or write Arabic
D) Not having memorized the entire Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of al-ummi is one who cannot recite the obligatory portion of the Quran, and a literate follower's prayer behind such an imam is invalid due to lack of necessity.

Clothed Follower Behind Naked Imam (مكتس بعار)
Ruling that a clothed person may not pray behind a naked imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a clothed person prays behind a naked imam and explain the reasoning based on necessity.

Core Idea
A clothed follower's prayer behind a naked imam is invalid because the follower has no excuse for missing the condition of covering.

This lesson examines the ruling on a clothed person following a naked imam. The naked imam's prayer is valid due to necessity, but the follower lacks that necessity. We will explore the reasoning and contrast with related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a clothed person (muktasi) praying behind a naked imam (ari). The ruling is that the follower's prayer is invalid (fasid).
2
Understand the basis
The naked imam's prayer is valid because he is excused due to necessity (he cannot find covering). The follower has no such excuse, so he must have proper covering.
The follower's obligation to cover is not lifted by the imam's excuse.
3
Distinguish the imam's condition from the follower's
The imam's excuse does not transfer to the follower. The follower must satisfy the conditions of prayer independently.
4
Compare with similar cases
The passage contrasts with the illiterate imam leading a reciter, where the follower can benefit from the imam's recitation. But covering and purity are not transferable.
This shows that some conditions (like recitation) can be fulfilled by the imam on behalf of the follower, while others (like covering) cannot.
5
Apply the principle
The ruling is based on the presence or absence of necessity. If the follower also is naked due to necessity, his prayer behind a naked imam would be valid.
The decisive factor is the follower's own excuse, not the imam's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومكتس بعار لأن صلاة العاري جائزة مع فقد الشرط للضرورة ولا ضرورة في حق المقتدي. وفي السراج الوهاج لو قال ولا مستور العورة خلف العاري لكان أولى لأن ستر عورته بالسروال أو نحوه لا يسمى مكتسياً في العرف، وتصح صلاة المكتسي خلفه لأنه مستور العورة .اهـ لكن اختلفوا في السراويل هل يكون كسوة شرعاً في كفارة اليمين، وصحح صاحب الخلاصة أنه لا يجوز للرجل ولا للمرأة أي لا يكون كسوة قيد بالمكتسي لأنه لو أم العاري عراة ولابسين فصلاة الإمام ومن هو مثله جائزة بلا خلاف، وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح بخلاف الأمي إذا أم أمياً وقارئاً فإن صلاة الكل فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأمي يمكن أن يجعل صلاته بقراءة إذا اقتدى بقارئ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة وليست طهارة الإمام وسترته طهارة وسترة للمأموم حكماً فافترقا.
His saying: (And a clothed person behind a naked person) because the prayer of the naked is permissible when the condition [of covering] is absent due to necessity, and there is no necessity for the follower. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, if he had said 'and one who covers his private parts is not [the same] behind a naked person,' it would be better, because covering his private parts with trousers or the like is not called 'clothed' in custom, and the prayer of the clothed behind him is valid because he is one who covers his private parts. However, they differed regarding trousers: is it considered clothing legally in the expiation of an oath? The author of al-Khulasa corrected that it is not permissible for a man or a woman, i.e., it is not considered clothing. He restricted it to the clothed because if he leads [a congregation] that includes naked and clothed, the prayer of the imam and those like him is valid without dispute, and likewise the person with a leaking wound behind his like and behind a healthy person, unlike the illiterate if he leads an illiterate and a reciter, then the prayer of all is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, because the illiterate can make his prayer have recitation by following a reciter, since the imam's recitation is recitation for the follower, but the imam's purity and covering are not purity and covering for the follower legally, so they differ.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling that a clothed person may not pray behind a naked imam. The naked imam's prayer is valid because he lacks the means to cover, but the follower has no such excuse. The author notes that if the follower wears only trousers, he is not considered 'clothed' in the legal sense regarding imamah, but his own prayer is valid. The ruling contrasts with the case of the illiterate imam, where the follower can benefit from the imam's recitation, but cannot benefit from his purity or covering.

Key Terms
مكتس (muktasi): One who has clothing to cover his private parts, even if minimal.
عار (ari): One who is naked, i.e., has no covering for his private parts.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that excuses the omission of a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the prayer of a clothed follower invalid behind a naked imam?
A) Because the imam's prayer is invalid
B) Because the follower has no necessity to pray without covering
C) Because the imam cannot recite properly
D) Because the follower must also be naked

Key Takeaway
The follower's prayer behind a naked imam is invalid because the follower lacks the necessity that excuses the imam.

Able Follower Behind Gesturing Imam
Ruling on an able follower behind a gesturing imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that an able-bodied person's prayer behind a gesturing imam is invalid and identify the condition that makes it valid (both gesture).

Core Idea
An able follower cannot validly follow a gesturing imam; equality of capacity is required.

When an imam has a valid excuse and performs prayer by gesturing, the question arises whether an able-bodied follower can join him. The Hanafi ruling is clear: if the follower is physically capable of bowing and prostrating, his prayer behind such an imam is invalid because his state is stronger. The only exception is when the follower also has an excuse, making both equal in capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Locate the key phrase 'فسد اقتداء' – the follower's prayer is invalid (fasid).
The ruling is explicitly stated in the text.
2
Identify the Condition
Note that the invalidity depends on the follower being able to bow and prostrate while the imam cannot.
The condition is the follower's stronger state (قوة حال المقتدي).
3
Understand the Exception
Recognize that if both the imam and the follower are gesturing (both excused), the following is valid due to similarity (الماثلة).
The text mentions this exception explicitly.
4
Apply the Principle
In practice, determine the capability of both parties: if the follower is able and the imam is not, the follower must not follow that imam; he should pray separately or find another imam.
The ruling prevents a stronger obligated person from reducing his obligation due to a weaker imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وغير موم بموم) أي فسد اقتداء من يقدر على الركوع والسجود بمن لا يقدر عليهما للعذر لقوة حال المقتدي، قيد به لأن اقتداء المومي بالمومي صحيح للماثلة كما سيأتي.
His saying: (And one who gestures not behind one who gestures) i.e., the following of one who is able to bow and prostrate behind one who is unable to do so due to an excuse is invalid because of the stronger state of the follower. He restricted it thus because the following of a gesturer by a gesturer is valid due to similarity, as will come.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
The passage rules that a person who can physically perform bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) may not pray behind an imam who can only gesture due to illness or old age. The follower's state is stronger, and since there is no excuse for the follower, his prayer is invalid. However, if both the imam and follower are gesturers, it is valid because they are equal.

Key Terms
موم (mumi): One who gestures with head or eyes instead of bowing and prostrating due to inability.
اقتداء (iqtidā’): Following the imam in congregational prayer.
الماثلة (al-mumāthala): Equality or similitude in the state of excuse between imam and follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Never
B) When the follower is unable to bow and prostrate (has an excuse)
C) Only when the follower is literate
D) When the imam is naked

Key Takeaway
An able-bodied follower cannot validly pray behind a gesturing imam; only when both are similarly excused does the following become valid.

Unity of Prayer (Ittihad) as a Condition for Valid Iqtida'
Ruling with proof and expansion to vow/oath cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that ittihad (unity) of prayer type and intention is required for valid iqtida', and apply this rule to distinguish valid from invalid following scenarios including fard/nafl, nazir/halif, and differing faraid.

Core Idea
Ittihad — the imam's prayer must be the same type and intent as the follower's; otherwise the follower's prayer is invalid.

In congregational prayer, the follower's act is built upon the imam's. The Hanafi school holds that for this building to be sound, the two prayers must be identical in type and essential intent. This lesson unpacks that condition, its proof from the hadith of Mu'adh, and its application to a range of scenarios, from fard behind nafl to the complex cases of vows and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the specific scenario: a person performing an obligatory prayer (fard) follows an imam performing a supererogatory prayer (nafl) or a different fard. The ruling is that the follower's prayer is fasid (invalid).
This is the core ruling of the passage, from which all branch cases derive.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, where the Prophet (saw) gave him the choice between praying with him (as nafl) or leading his people lightly (as fard). This implies he cannot combine both.
The hadith is narrated by Imam Ahmad. The Hanafi interpretation uses it to establish prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyse how the hadith proves the condition of ittihad. The Prophet presented two mutually exclusive options, showing that one cannot simultaneously intend fard behind a nafl imam.
Also note the principle 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor), implying his prayer encompasses the follower's, requiring unity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars argue from the same hadith that it is permissible, because Mu'adh prayed with the Prophet as nafl and later led his people as fard. The Hanafi response distinguishes that these were two separate acts, not simultaneous following.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.
5
Apply to branch cases
Apply the condition of ittihad to the cases mentioned: nazir behind nazir, nazir behind halif, two rak'ats of tawaf, and differing sunnah prayers. Determine validity based on whether unity exists.
Pay attention to the nuances: unity is judged by the actual prayer type, not the belief of the follower (e.g., witr).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ومفترض بمتنفل وبمفترض آخر) أي وفسد اقتداء المفترض بإمام متنفل أو بإمام يصلي فرضاً غير فرض المقتدي لأن الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم في حق الإمام في أئمتنا عند الأولى وهو مشاركة وموافقة فلا بد من الاتحاد وهو معدوم في الثانية، والذي صح وترجح أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نفلاً وبقومه فرضاً لقوله حين شكوا تطویله بهم یا معاذ إما أن تصلي معي وإما أن تخفف على قومك كما رواه الإمام أحمد. فشرع له أحد الأمرين الصلاة معه ولا يصلي بقومه أو الصلاة بقومه على وجه التخفيف ولا هذا حقيقة اللفظ أفاد منعه من الإمامة إذا صلى معه عليه السلام ولا تمتنع إمامته أنه مطلقاً بالاتفاق فعلم الفرض والحاصل أن اتحاد الصلاتين شرط لصحة الاقتداء وذلك بأن يمكنه الدخول في صلاته بنية صلاة الإمام فتكون صلاة الإمام متضمنة لصلاة المقتدي وهو المراد بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الإمام «ضامن» أي تتضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي. وأشار بمنع اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل إلى منع اقتداء الناذر بالناذر لأن صلاة الإمام نفل بالنسبة إلى المقتدي لأن التزامه إنما يظهر عليه فقط إلا إذا نذر أحدهما عين ما نذره الآخر فاقتدى أحدهما بالآخر فإنه يجوز للاتحاد وإلى أنه لو أفسد كل منهما التطوع ثم اقتدى أحدهما بالآخر في قضائه فإنه لا يجوز لما ذكرناه للاختلاف كما لو اقتدى من أفسد بمن يصلي منذورة إلا إذا كان اقتدى أحدهما بالآخر تطوعاً ثم أفسداه ثم قضياه بالاقتداء يجوز للاتحاد. ومصلياً ركعتي الطواف كالناذرين لأن طواف هذا غير طواف الآخر وهو السبب فهو اقتداء الواجب بالنفل . وينبغي أن يصح الاقتداء على القول بسنية ركعتي الطواف كما لا يخفى . وأشار بمنع مفترض خلف مفترض آخر إلى منع اقتداء الناذر بالحالف لأن المنذورة أقوى من المحلوف بها لأنها واجبة قصداً ووجوب المحلوف بها عارض لتحقيق البر، ولهذا الحالف بالحالف والحالف بالناذر وصورة الحلف بها كما في الخلاصة أن يقول والله لأصلين ركعتين. وذكر الولوالجي أن اقتداء الحالف بالمتطوع أو المفترض جائز بخلاف اقتداء الناذر بالمتطوع أو المفترض فإنه لا يجوز اهـ. وهذا يدل على أن صلاة الحالف لم تخرج عن كونها نفلاً بالحلف، وقد يقال إنها واجبة لتحقق البر فينبغي أن لا يجوز خلف المتطوع. ولو اقتدى من يرى وجوب الوتر فيه بمن يرى سنيته صح للاتحاد ولا يختلف باختلاف الاعتقاد، ولو اقتدى من يصلي سنة بمن يصلي سنة أخرى فإنه يجوز كسنة العشاء خلف من يصلي التراويح، أو سنة الظهر البعدية خلف من يصلي القبلية كما في الخلاصة والمجتبى. وأطلق في منع ا المفترض بالمتنفل فشمل الاقتداء في جميع الأفعال وفي بعضها وهو قول العامة فلا یرد ذكره محمد من أن الإمام إذا رفع رأسه من الركوع فاقتدى به إنسان فسبق الإمام الحدث قبل السجود فاستخلفه ما يصلي ويأتي بالسجدتين ويكونان نفلاً للخليفة حتى يعيدهما بعد ذلك،
His saying: (And one who performs an obligatory prayer behind one who performs a supererogatory prayer, and behind another who performs an obligatory prayer) i.e., the following of one who performs an obligatory prayer behind an imam who performs a supererogatory prayer, or behind an imam who performs an obligatory prayer different from the follower's obligatory prayer, is invalid because following is based on participation and agreement; unity is necessary and lacking in the second case. What is correct and preponderant is that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray with the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a supererogatory prayer and with his people as an obligatory prayer, because of his statement when they complained about his lengthening: 'O Mu'adh, either pray with me or lighten [the prayer] for your people' as narrated by Imam Ahmad. So he permitted one of two things: praying with him and not praying with his people, or praying with his people in a lightened manner. This indicates his prohibition of leading when he prayed with him (peace be upon him), but his imamah is not absolutely prohibited by consensus. So the ruling is that unity of the two prayers is a condition for the validity of following, such that he can enter his prayer with the intention of the imam's prayer, so that the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer. This is the meaning of his statement (peace be upon him): 'The imam is a guarantor', i.e., his prayer encompasses the follower's prayer. He indicated by the prohibition of a fard follower behind a nafl imam the prohibition of a nazir (one who vowed) behind another nazir, because the imam's prayer is supererogatory relative to the follower since his obligation only appears upon him, unless one vowed the exact same thing as the other, then it is permissible due to unity. Also, if both invalidate their supererogatory prayer and then one follows the other in its make-up, it is not permissible due to the difference, as if one who invalidated follows one who prays a vowed prayer, unless they followed each other as nafl and then invalidated and then made it up by following, it is permissible due to unity. And the one praying the two rak'ats of tawaf are like the nazirs because the tawaf of this one is different from the tawaf of the other, and it is the cause; thus it is following an obligatory prayer behind a nafl. It should be valid according to the opinion that the two rak'ats of tawaf are sunnah, as is not hidden. He indicated by the prohibition of a fard follower behind another fard the prohibition of a nazir behind a swearer (halif), because the vowed prayer is stronger than the one sworn by, because it is obligatory by intention, whereas the obligation of the sworn by is incidental to fulfill the oath. Hence the swearer behind the swearer and the swearer behind the nazir. The form of swearing by it, as in al-Khulasa, is to say, 'By Allah, I will pray two rak'ats.' Al-Walwaliji mentioned that the following of a swearer behind a volunteer or a fard performer is permissible, unlike the following of a nazir behind a volunteer or a fard performer; it is not permissible. This indicates that the prayer of the swearer does not exit the category of nafl by the oath. It could be said that it becomes obligatory to fulfill the oath, so it should not be permissible behind a volunteer. If one who considers witr obligatory follows one who considers it sunnah, it is valid due to unity, and it does not differ due to difference in belief. If one who prays a sunnah follows one who prays another sunnah, it is permissible, such as sunnah of 'isha behind one who prays tarawih, or the sunnah of zuhr after behind one who prays the qabliyyah, as in al-Khulasa and al-Mujtaba. He made the prohibition of the fard behind the nafl absolute, so it includes following in all actions and in some actions, and this is the statement of the majority. So it is not refuted by what Muhammad mentioned that if the imam raises his head from ruku and a person follows him, and then the imam's state of purity is invalidated before prostration, so he appoints him as successor (khalifah), he continues praying and performs the two prostrations, and they become nafl for the successor until he repeats them after that.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This long passage establishes the fundamental principle that for valid following (iqitida'), the prayers of the imam and follower must be of the same type and intention. A person performing a fard prayer cannot follow an imam performing a nafl prayer, nor can he follow an imam performing a different fard. The proof is the hadith of Mu'adh, which indicates that the Prophet prohibited him from leading his people when he intended to pray with him as nafl. The key is 'ittihad' (unity). The passage then expands to related cases: a person who vowed a prayer (nazir) behind another nazir, the two rak'ats of tawaf, the swearer (halif), and rulings on different opinions (like witr). It also addresses partial following and the case of a substitute imam.

Key Terms
ائتدام (iqtida'): The act of following an imam in prayer, with the intention of being led.
اتحاد (ittihad): Unity of the prayers: the imam's prayer must be the same type (fard/nafl) and same specific prayer as the follower's.
ضامن (damin): Imam is a guarantor; his prayer encompasses the follower's prayer.
ناذر (nazir): One who has made a vow (nadhr) to perform a specific prayer.
حالف (halif): One who has sworn an oath (yamin) to perform a prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The imam must be male
B) The prayers must be of the same type and specific prayer (ittihad)
C) The follower must recite al-Fatiha
D) The imam must not have invalidated his wudu

Key Takeaway
Unity of prayer type and specific intent between imam and follower is a fundamental condition for valid congregational following in the Hanafi school; violation renders the follower's prayer invalid.

The Ruling of a Person with a Leaking Wound Following an Imam
Statement of permissibility for a ma'dhur following an imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a person with a leaking wound may validly follow an imam with the same condition or a healthy imam, and identify the basis for this permissibility.

Core Idea
A person with an ongoing excuse may follow both similarly excused and healthy imams.

In the Hanafi school, a person suffering from a continuously leaking wound is considered a ma'dhur (excused). His prayer is valid despite the impurity. This brief passage extends the same permissibility to his following an imam: whether the imam shares the same condition or is completely healthy, the follower's prayer remains valid. The commentary highlights a grammatical correction but the ruling stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the subject is a person with a leaking wound (sahib al-jarh al-sa'il).
This person is considered ma'dhur (excused) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the imam options
The text mentions two types of imam: his like (another with the same condition) and a healthy person.
3
State the ruling
The person may follow either type of imam; it is permissible.
The ruling is clear: 'behind his like and behind a healthy person'.
4
Note the implication
The follower's prayer is valid even if the imam's condition differs from his own.
The validity is due to the follower's own excuse, not the imam's state.
5
Understand the basis
The ma'dhur's prayer is inherently valid; following an imam does not affect that validity.
This is consistent with the principle that the excused person's prayer is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وكذا صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح) أي وكذا ائتمام صاحب الجرح السائل بمثله وبصحيح والأولى حذف الباء من الموضعين.
His saying: (And likewise the person with a leaking wound behind his like and behind a healthy person) i.e., likewise the following of a person with a leaking wound behind his like and behind a healthy person. It is better to omit the 'ba' from both places.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This short passage states that a person suffering from a continuously bleeding wound (sahib al-jarh al-sa'il) may follow an imam who has the same condition or even a healthy imam. This is analogous to the earlier ruling of a clothed person behind a naked imam, where the imam's prayer is valid due to necessity and the follower's prayer is valid because his own excuse is present. The note about omitting the 'ba' is a grammatical point: the matn should read 'bi-mithlihi wa-sahih' without the preposition.

Key Terms
صاحب الجرح السائل (sahib al-jarh al-sa'il): A person with a wound that continuously bleeds or discharges, making wudu difficult.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A person with a continuous leaking wound may validly follow an imam, whether the imam shares his condition or is healthy.

Prohibition of Fard Behind Nafl Imam: Proof and Refutation
States the ruling and refutes an objection about deputy imam's prayer being nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule prohibiting a fard follower behind a nafl imam, explain the evidence from the hadith 'al-imam damin', and refute the objection regarding the deputy imam's sajdahs.

Core Idea
The hadith 'al-imam damin' demands unity of prayer type between imam and follower.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq establishes that a fard prayer cannot be performed behind an imam who is offering a nafl prayer. The key evidence is the Prophetic statement 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor), which implies the imam's prayer must be of the same type as the follower's. The author then extends this principle to similar cases and defends it against a potential objection from Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the deputy imam's sajdahs being considered nafl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
Locate the main ruling: prohibition of a fard follower behind a mutanafifil. Identify the dalil: the hadith 'al-imam damin'.
The ruling is stated at the start: 'صح اقتداء المقتدي... وأشار بمنع اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل'.
2
Understand the extension to analogous cases
The passage applies the same logic to nadhir (vowed prayer) and half (sworn oath) followers. Note the exceptions: same vow, or when the vowed prayer is identical.
Pay attention to the distinction between nadhir and half, and the condition of ittihad (unity).
3
Analyze the objection from Muhammad al-Shaybani
Imam Muhammad’s riwayah suggests that if a follower catches only the sajdahs after the imam’s wudu breaks, those sajdahs are nafl for the deputy. Recognize this as an objection to the absolute prohibition.
The objection is raised through the phrase 'فلا يرد ذكره محمد من أن الإمام إذا رفع رأسه...'.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi refutation
The author, citing al-Fath and al-Nahr, argues that the deputy stands in the imam’s place, so the sajdahs are fard upon him. The recitation argument is also dismissed because the follower’s recitation is prohibited, not fard.
The refutation concludes: 'فالحق أن الإيراد ساقط من أصله'.
5
Synthesize the final position
The mufta bihi opinion is absolute prohibition of fard behind nafl, and the deputy’s sajdahs are fard. This has practical implications for congregation and deputyship.
The Hanafi position is consistent and based on a strong understanding of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صح اقتداء المقتدي وهو المراد بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الإمام «ضامن» أي تتضمن صلاته صلاة المقتدي. وأشار بمنع اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل إلى منع اقتداء الناذر بالناذر لأن صلاة الإمام نفل بالنسبة إلى المقتدي لأن التزامه إنما يظهر عليه فقط إلا إذا نذر أحدهما عين ما نذره الآخر فاقتدى أحدهما بالآخر فإنه يجوز للاتحاد وإلى أنه لو أفسد كل منهما التطوع ثم اقتدى أحدهما بالآخر في قضائه فإنه لا يجوز لما ذكرناه للاختلاف كما لو اقتدى من أفسد بمن يصلي منذورة إلا إذا كان اقتدى أحدهما بالآخر تطوعاً ثم أفسداه ثم قضياه بالاقتداء يجوز للاتحاد. ومصليا ركعتي الطواف كالناذرين لأن طواف هذا غير طواف الآخر وهو السبب فهو اقتداء الواجب بالنفل. وينبغي أن يصح الاقتداء على القول بسنية ركعتي الطواف كما لا يخفى. وأشار بمنع مفترض خلف مفترض آخر إلى منع اقتداء الناذر بالحالف لأن المنذورة أقوى من المحلوف بها لأنها واجبة قصداً ووجوب المحلوف بها عارض لتحقيق البر، ولهذا الحالف بالحالف والحالف بالناذر وصورة الحلف بها كما في الخلاصة أن يقول والله لأصلين ركعتين. وذكر الولوالجي أن اقتداء الحالف بالمتطوع أو المفترض جائز بخلاف اقتداء الناذر بالمتطوع أو المفترض فإنه لا يجوز اهـ. وهذا يدل على أن صلاة الحالف لم تخرج عن كونها نفلاً بالحلف، وقد يقال إنها واجبة لتحقق البر فينبغي أن لا يجوز خلف المتطوع. ولو اقتدى من يرى وجوب الوتر فيه بمن يرى سنيته صح للاتحاد ولا يختلف باختلاف الاعتقاد، ولو اقتدى من يصلي سنة بمن يصلي سنة أخرى فإنه يجوز كسنة العشاء خلف من يصلي التراويح، أو سنة الظهر البعدية خلف من يصلي القبلية كما في الخلاصة والمجتبى. وأطلق في منع اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل فشمل الاقتداء في جميع الأفعال وفي بعضها وهو قول العامة فلا يرد ذكره محمد من أن الإمام إذا رفع رأسه من الركوع فاقتدى به إنسان فسبق الإمام الحدث قبل صح ويأتي بالسجدتين ويكونان نفلاً للخليفة حتى يعيدهما بعد ذلك، السجود فاستخلفه اقتداء ما قوله: (ومصليا) تثنية مصلي مرفوع بالألف لأنه مبتدأ، وسقطت نونه للإضافة كنون المضاف إليه أيضاً وقوله «كالناذرين» خبر. قوله: (فشمل الاقتداء الخ) رد لما قيل إنما لا يجوز اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل في جميع الصلاة لا في بعضها مستدلاً بما ذكره محمد وبالفرع الذي بعده. قوله: المنع النفلية أي نفلية السجدتين وهو تعليل لعدم الورود. قال في الفتح والعامة على المنع مطلقاً أي سواء كان في جميع الصلاة أو في بعضها ومنعوا نفلية السجدتين بل هما فرض على الخليفة الخ. قوله: فالحق أن الإيراد ساقط من أصله أي الإيراد الثاني. قال في النهر: وفيه نظر بل هي عليه وحظرت لتحمل الإمام إياها عنه، ولو صح ما ادعاه لبطل تعليلهم عدم صحة اقتداء المسافر. رواه أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب كذا، الترمذي في كتاب المواقيت باب كذا، ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب كذا، أحمد في مسنده. وفرضاً في حق من أدرك أول الصلاة لمنع النفلية في حق الخليفة بل هما فرض عليه. ولذا لو تركهما فسدت لأنه قام مقام الأول فلزمه ما لزمه وكذا لا يرد المتنفل إذا اقتدى بالمفترض في الشفع الثاني فإنه يجوز مع أنه اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل في حق القراءة لكون صلاة المقتدي أخذت حكم الفرض بسبب الاقتداء، ولذا لزمه قضاء ما لم يدركه مع الإمام من الشفع الأول، ولذا لو أفسد على نفسه يلزمه قضاء الأربع. والتحقيق ما في غاية البيان من أن قراءة المأموم محظورة، فكيف يقال إنها مفروضة؟ فالحق أن الإيراد ساقط من أصله.
Correct is the following of the follower, which is intended by his saying, peace be upon him, 'The imam is a guarantor,' meaning his prayer includes the follower's prayer. And he indicated by the prohibition of a follower performing fard behind a mutanafifil to the prohibition of a follower performing nadhr behind another nadhr, because the imam's prayer is nafl relative to the follower, since his obligation appears only upon him, except if each vowed the same thing as the other, then one follows the other, for it is permitted due to unity. And also that if both invalidated the tatawwu' then one follows the other in its qada', it is not permissible due to the difference, like one who invalidated following one performing a vowed prayer, except if they followed each other as tatawwu' then invalidated it, then performed qada' with following, it is permissible due to unity. And the two performing two rak'ahs of tawaf are like the two nadhir, because the tawaf of one is not the tawaf of the other, and the cause is the same; so it is following of wajib behind nafl. And it should be that the following is valid according to the view that the two rak'ahs of tawaf are sunnah, as is not hidden. And he indicated by the prohibition of a fard follower behind another fard to the prohibition of a nadhir follower behind a half, because the vowed prayer is stronger than the sworn one, since it is wajib intentionally, whereas the obligation of the sworn one is incidental for fulfilling the oath. Therefore, the half following a half and the half following a nadhir — and the form of the oath as in al-Khulasa is to say, 'By Allah, I will pray two rak'ahs.' And al-Walwaliji mentioned that the half following a mutatawwi' or a muftarid is permissible, contrary to the nadhir following a mutatawwi' or muftarid, for it is not permissible. And this indicates that the prayer of the half does not cease to be nafl by the oath; and it may be said it is wajib to fulfill the oath, so it should not be permissible behind a mutatawwi'. And if one who holds witr to be wajib follows one who holds it to be sunnah, it is valid due to unity, and it does not differ with difference of belief. And if one praying a sunnah follows another praying a different sunnah, it is permissible, like sunnah of 'ishaa' behind one praying tarawih, or the sunnah of zuhr al-ba'diyya behind one praying the qabliyya, as in al-Khulasa and al-Mujtaba. And the prohibition of a fard follower behind a mutanafifil is absolute, so it includes following in all actions and in some of them, and that is the statement of the majority. So the mention of Muhammad is not a valid objection: that if the imam raises his head from ruku' and a person follows him, then the imam's wudu' is invalidated before he [the follower] performs sajdah, and he comes with the two sajdahs and they are nafl for the deputy until he repeats them afterwards, sajdah, then he appoints a deputy, following, his saying: (and the two praying) dual of musalli, nominative with alif because it is subject, and its nun is omitted due to idafah, like the nun of the mudaf ilayhi also, and his saying 'like the two nadhir' is predicate. His saying: (so it includes the following etc.) is a refutation of what was said that the prohibition of a fard follower behind a mutanafifil is only in the entire prayer, not in parts, using as evidence what Muhammad mentioned and the branch after it. His saying: 'the prohibition of nafliyya' meaning nafliyya of the two sajdahs, and it is a reason for the non-occurrence [of the objection]. He said in al-Fath: and the majority are of the prohibition absolutely, i.e., whether in the entire prayer or in parts, and they deny the nafliyya of the two sajdahs; rather they are fard upon the deputy etc. His saying: the truth is that the objection is invalid from its origin, i.e., the second objection. He said in al-Nahr: and there is consideration in this; rather they are upon him, and it is prevented because the imam carries them for him; and if his claim were correct, it would invalidate their reasoning of the invalidity of a traveller's following. Narrated by Abu Dawud in the Book of Prayer, chapter such-and-such, al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Times, chapter such-and-such, Ibn Majah in the Book of Iqamah, chapter such-and-such, Ahmad in his Musnad. And it is fard for the one who caught the beginning of the prayer, to prevent nafliyya for the deputy; rather they are fard upon him. So if he leaves them, the prayer becomes invalid because he took the place of the first, so what was binding on the first becomes binding on him. Similarly, the mutanafifil following a muftarid in the second shaf' is not a valid objection, for it is permissible, although it is following of a fard behind a mutanafifil with respect to qira'ah, because the follower's prayer takes the ruling of fard due to following; therefore, he must make up what he missed with the imam from the first shaf', and if he invalidates himself, he must make up four [rak'ahs]. And the verification is what is in Ghayat al-Bayan: that the recitation of the follower is prohibited; so how can it be said that it is fard? The truth is that the objection is invalid from its origin.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor), meaning his prayer encompasses the follower's. The author states the general prohibition of a follower performing fard behind an imam performing nafl. He extends this to analogous cases: a nadhir (vowed prayer) follower behind another nadhir is prohibited unless they vowed the same thing, because then the prayers are identical in obligation. Similarly, one who invalidated his tatawwu' cannot follow another in qada' due to difference. The two rak'ahs of tawaf are treated like nadhir prayers because the tawaf is different, so it is wajib behind nafl, though it would be valid if the two rak'ahs are considered sunnah. The prohibition also applies to a nadhir follower behind a half (one who swore an oath to pray), because the vowed prayer is intentionally wajib, while the sworn one becomes wajib incidentally. Al-Walwaliji holds that a half can follow a mutatawwi' or muftarid, but a nadhir cannot. The author notes that if one believes witr to be wajib and follows someone who considers it sunnah, it is valid due to the unity of the prayer type. Following one sunnah behind another sunnah (e.g., 'ishaa' sunnah behind tarawih) is permissible. The passage then refutes an objection from Muhammad al-Shaybani: that if a follower catches only the sajdahs after the imam's wudu breaks, those sajdahs are nafl for the deputy. The author, citing al-Fath and al-Nahr, argues that the majority hold the sajdahs are fard for the deputy because he stands in the imam's place. The recitation argument is also refuted: the follower's recitation is prohibited, not obligatory, so the analogy fails. Thus the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): The imam guarantees the prayer of the follower, meaning his prayer encompasses and satisfies it.
متنفل (mutanafifil): One performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer.
ناذر (nadhir): One who has vowed (nadhr) to perform a specific prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it invalid for a person performing a fard prayer to follow an imam performing a nafl prayer?
A) Because the follower's intention is different
B) Because the hadith 'al-imam damin' requires unity of prayer type
C) Because the imam must be of higher spiritual status
D) Because the follower's prayer would become nafl

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'al-imam damin' requires unity of prayer type; thus, a fard prayer behind a nafl imam is invalid.

The Follower's Prayer Takes the Hukm of Fard
Ruling with proof: follower's prayer becomes fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a follower's prayer becomes fard in ruling when joining the imam in the second shaf', and explain the proof and the refutation of the objection.

Core Idea
A follower's nafil prayer becomes fard in ruling when joined to an imam's fard.

A person who joins the congregational prayer late, even after the first two rak'ahs, might think his prayer remains nafil. The Hanafi school holds otherwise: his prayer takes the ruling of fard due to his connection to the imam. This has real consequences: if he spoils his prayer, he must make up four rak'ahs. In this lesson, we unpack the proof and address a common objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is the prayer of the follower (muqtadi) who joins the imam in the second shaf' of a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The ruling: it takes the hukm of fard (fard in ruling), not nafil.
The follower may have originally intended nafil, but the prayer is treated as fard.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is a qiyas jaliy: the follower stands in the place of the imam (qaama maqam al-awwal), so what was obligatory on the imam becomes obligatory on the follower. This is supported by the consequence that if the follower leaves his prayer, it becomes corrupt and he must make up four rak'ah.
The text states: 'li-anna salat al-muqtadi akhadhat hukm al-fard bi-sabab al-iqtida.'
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The decisive point is the legal effect: the follower must make up what he missed (qada of the first shaf') and if he spoils his prayer, he must make up the full four rak'ahs. This shows the prayer is treated as fard.
These consequences would not follow if the prayer remained nafil.
4
Analyse the Objection and Response
An objection: if the prayer is fard, then the follower's recitation would be fard, but the follower is prohibited from reciting behind the imam. The response from Ghayat al-Bayan: recitation is prohibited (mahzurah), so it cannot be fard. The objection misapplies the hukm.
The objection is ruled invalid from its root ('saqit min aslihi').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرضاً في حق من أدرك أول الصلاة لمنع النفلية في حق الخليفة بل هما فرض عليه. ولذا لو تركهما فسدت لأنه قام مقام الأول فلزمه ما لزمه وكذا لا يرد المتنفل إذا اقتدى بالمفترض في الشفع الثاني فإنه يجوز مع أنه اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل في حق القراءة لكون صلاة المقتدي أخذت حكم الفرض بسبب الاقتداء، ولذا لزمه قضاء ما لم يدركه مع الإمام من الشفع الأول، ولذا لو أفسد على نفسه يلزمه قضاء الأربع. والتحقيق ما في غاية البيان من أن قراءة المأموم محظورة، فكيف يقال إنها مفروضة؟ فالحق أن الإيراد ساقط من أصله.
And it is fard in the right of the one who caught the beginning of the prayer to prevent nafliyyah in the right of the khalifa; rather both are fard upon him. So if he leaves them, his prayer becomes corrupt because he stands in the place of the first [imam], so what was obligatory upon the first becomes obligatory upon him. Similarly, the one performing nafil when he follows the one performing fard in the second shaf' – it is valid despite it being a following of a fard-performer by a nafil-performer with respect to recitation, because the prayer of the follower takes the ruling of fard due to the following. Therefore, he must make up what he missed with the imam from the first shaf'. Therefore, if he spoils it upon himself, he must make up four [rak'ahs]. The verified [position] is as in Ghayat al-Bayan: the recitation of the follower is prohibited, so how can it be said that it is fard? So the reply is invalid from its root.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the follower's prayer when he joins the imam in the second shaf' (i.e., the second set of two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, or the last two rak'ahs). The author asserts that the follower's prayer takes the ruling of fard, not nafil, because of his connection to the imam. This is proven by the consequences: if the follower leaves his own prayer (e.g., by speaking), it becomes corrupt and he must make up four rak'ahs, just like the imam. The objection that the follower's recitation is fard is refuted by citing Ghayat al-Bayan: the follower is prohibited from reciting behind the imam, so recitation cannot be fard for him. Thus the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
الخليفة (al-khalifah): The imam or leader of the prayer. In this context, it refers to the imam whose prayer is fard.
الشفع (al-shaf'): Two rak'ahs, a pair. The second shaf' means the second set of two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer.
محظورة (mahzurah): Prohibited. Here, it refers to the follower's recitation behind the imam being prohibited.
فرضاً (fardan): Obligatory. In this passage, it means the prayer takes the ruling of fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a follower joins the imam in the second shaf' (second set of two rak'ahs) of a four-rak'ah fard prayer, what is the ruling of the follower's prayer?
A) It remains nafil.
B) It takes the ruling of fard due to the following.
C) It becomes invalid unless he recites.
D) It becomes fard only if he intended fard initially.

Key Takeaway
A follower who joins the imam in the second shaf' of a fard prayer has his prayer treated as fard in ruling, with all its consequences, even if he intended nafil.

Invalid Following: Does the Follower Become a Starter?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on starting prayer after invalid following

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether a person whose following is invalid becomes a starter (shari') of his own prayer, and identify the mufta bihi view and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
When following is invalid, Muhammad says no start; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say yes — the mufta bihi is no start.

This passage lists eight scenarios where following the imam is invalid and then addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does the follower commence his own prayer? The answer determines important consequences, such as whether laughter invalidates his wudu and whether he must make up the prayer. The discussion shows how the school weighs the Zahir al-Riwaya texts of Imam Muhammad against qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight cases of invalid following
The passage begins by listing situations where following is invalid, e.g., a masbuq following a masbuq, a lahiq following a lahiq, two residents following a traveler then one following the other in qada', two people both intending to follow each other, and different fard prayers (Dhuhr behind Jumu'ah or vice versa). Recognize these as examples of corrupt following (fasad al-iqtida').
The exact number is eight, as indicated by the text.
2
Locate the dispute on becoming a starter
The author notes that after listing these cases, he did not specify whether the follower becomes a starter (shari') due to disagreement. Two narrations are cited: one authenticated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (he becomes a starter) and another in al-Muhit (he does not).
This is the core of the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the proofs for each position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that no start occurs because the prayer is a single act; if the following is invalid, the entire entry into prayer fails. He bases this on texts in al-Asl and examples like a reciter following an illiterate. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that prayer has two aspects (following and individual), so invalidity of following does not preclude an individual start. Their view relies on qiyas and the idea that multiple facets can coexist.
Note the pronoun reference: 'indahuma' (the two) likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
The commentator and al-Muhit authenticate Muhammad's view (no start). Al-Kafi, which collects Muhammad's statements from Zahir al-Riwaya, supports this. Thus the mufta bihi is that he does not become a starter.
The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwaya, which is the strongest layer in Hanafi transmission.
5
Apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The text explicitly states that the fruit of the disagreement appears in the invalidation of wudu by laughter: if he is a starter, laughter invalidates; if not, it does not. Additionally, if he is not a starter, he is not required to make up the prayer (even if he was a volunteer).
This concrete outcome shows why the dispute matters in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المجتبى وغيره : لا يصح اقتداء المسبوق بالمسبوق ولا اللاحق باللاحق وكذا المقيمان إذا اقتديا بالمسافر ثم اقتدى أحدهما بالآخر في القضاء. ولو صليا الظهر ونوى كل واحد منهما إمامة صاحبه صحت صلاتهما، ولو نويا الاقتداء فسدت ومن مختلفي الفرض الظهر خلف الجمعة أو عكسه. وذكر الأسبيجابي أن من اقتدى في موضع يجب عليه الانفراد كالمسبوق إذا اقتدى بمسبوق أو انفرد في موضع يجب عليه الاقتداء فسدت صلاته كما إذا قام المسبوق إلى قضاء ما سبق به ثم تذكر الإمام أن عليه سجدة التلاوة ولم يعد المسبوق إلى متابعة الإمام. ثم الله ذكر في هذه المواضع الثمانية فسد الاقتداء ولم يذكر هل يصير شارعاً أو لا للاختلاف قالوا فيه روايتان وصحح في السراج الوهاج أنه شارعاً . صلاة نفسه، يصير في وصحح في المحيط وغيره أنه لا يصير شارعاً. قال في المعراج وفي المحيط الصحيح هو الأول يعني عدم الشروع لأنه نص عليه محمد في الأصل حتى لو كان متطوعاً لا يلزمه القضاء. وذكر الشارح أن الأشبه أن يقال : إن فسد لفقد شرط الصلاة كالطاهر خلف المعذور لا يكون شارعاً فيه وإن كان للاختلاف بين الصلاتين ينبغي أن يكون شارعاً فيه غير مضمون بالقضاء لاجتماع شرائطه فصار كالظان وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في حق بطلان الوضوء بالقهقهة اهـ. ويرد هذا التفصيل ما ذكره الحاكم في كافيه من أن المرأة إذا نوت العصر خلف المقيم بعد الوقت بأنه اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل في حق القراءة كما سيأتي فتدبر. قوله : (ولم يعد المسبوق إلى متابعة الإمام أي قبل أن يتأكد انفراده بأن كان لم يسجد للركعة وإلا فلا يتابعه، وإن تابعه فسدت كما سيأتي. قوله : ويرد هذا التفصيل ما ذكره الحاكم الخ قال في النهر : قد قدم رحمه المحاذاة في عن السراج أن الصحيح فساد صلاته وجزم به غیر واحد .اهـ. والظاهر أن ما صححه الحاكم قول محمد لما سيأتي وبه صرح في الخلاصة كما في المنح حيث قال : وفي كل موضع لا يصح الاقتداء هل يصير شارعاً في صلاة نفسه؟ عند محمد لا، وعندهما يصير شراعاً لأن للصلاة جهتين عندهما ولها جهة واحدة عند محمد .اهـ. ومثله في البزازية فهو يفيد أنه قول محمد خاصة، وعزاه الزيلعي إلى بعض المشايخ وقال : ومنهم من قال في المسألة روايتان وهو ما مشى عليه المؤلف حيث في من مصلي الظهر لم تجز صلاتها ولم تفسد على الإمام صلاته .اهـ. فهو صريح في عدم صحة شروعها لاختلاف الصلاتين وقال في موضع آخر : رجل قارئ دخل في صلاة أمي تطوعاً أو في صلاة امرأة أو جنب أو على غير وضوء ثم أفسدها فليس عليه قضاؤها لأنه لم يدخل صلاة تامة .اهـ. فعلم بهذا أن المذهب تصحيح المحيط من عدم صحة الشروع لأن الكافي جمع كلام محمد في كتبه التي هي ظاهر الرواية
And in al-Mujtaba and others: The following of a masbuq (one who missed part of prayer) by another masbuq is not valid, nor of a lahiq (one who is ahead) by another lahiq, and likewise two muqeem (residents) when they follow a musafir (traveler), then one of them follows the other in qada' (make-up prayer). If two people pray Dhuhr and each intends to be imam of his companion, their prayers are valid; but if they intend to follow each other, their prayers are corrupt. And from different fard: Dhuhr behind Jumu'ah or vice versa. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that whoever follows in a place where it is necessary for him to separate, like a masbuq following a masbuq, or separates in a place where he must follow, his prayer becomes corrupt, as when a masbuq stands to make up what he missed, then the imam remembers that he owes a sajdat al-tilawa, and the masbuq does not return to follow the imam. Then [the author] mentioned in these eight places that the following is corrupt, but did not mention whether he becomes a starter [of his own prayer] or not due to disagreement. They said there are two narrations. It is authenticated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that he becomes a starter. In his own prayer, he becomes [a starter]. And it is authenticated in al-Muhit and others that he does not become a starter. He said in al-Mi'raj and al-Muhit: the correct is the first, i.e., not starting, because it is explicitly stated by Muhammad in al-Asl, even if he was mutatawwi' (voluntary), he is not required to make it up. And the commentator mentioned that the more appropriate is to say: if it is corrupt due to missing a condition of prayer, like a pure person behind an excused person, he does not become a starter; but if due to a difference between the two prayers, he should become a starter, but it is not guaranteed by qada' because its conditions are met, so it becomes like [؟]. And the fruit of the disagreement appears in the invalidation of wudu by laughter. End. This detail is refuted by what al-Hakim mentioned in his Kafi: that if a woman intends Asr behind a muqeem after the time [؟], it is a following of a fard-performer by a nafil-performer with respect to recitation, as will come, so ponder. His statement: 'and the masbuq does not return to follow the imam' means before his separation is confirmed, i.e., as long as he did not prostrate for the rak'ah; otherwise he does not follow him, and if he follows, it is corrupt as will come. His statement: 'this detail is refuted by what al-Hakim mentioned' - he said in al-Nahr: may he have mercy, he presented the [؟] from al-Siraj that the correct is the corruption of his prayer, and more than one affirmed it. And apparent is that what al-Hakim authenticated is the saying of Muhammad as will come, and it is explicitly stated in al-Khulasa as in al-Minh: 'In every place where following is not valid, does he become a starter in his own prayer? According to Muhammad, no; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually 'indahuma' means the two, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Wait, it says 'indahu' for Muhammad and 'indahuma' for the two, but then 'indahuma' might refer to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? Actually, 'indahuma' usually refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The text says 'indaha' for the two, and 'indahu' for Muhammad. But it says 'عندهما' and 'عند محمد'. So it's the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?) No, in Hanafi, 'indahuma' often means Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. But here it contrasts with Muhammad alone, so 'indahuma' likely means Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa? The text is ambiguous. It says: 'عند محمد لا، وعندهما يصير شراعاً'. So Muhammad says no, the two (probably Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say he becomes a starter. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. End. Similar in al-Bazzaziyya, it indicates it is specifically the saying of Muhammad. And al-Zayla'i attributed it to some mashayikh, and said: some of them said there are two narrations in the matter, and that is what the author followed. Regarding the woman who intended Dhuhr [congratulation?], her prayer is not valid, and it does not corrupt the imam's prayer. End. So it is explicit in the invalidity of her starting due to the difference of the two prayers. And he said in another place: a reciter entered into the prayer of an ummi (illiterate) voluntarily, or into the prayer of a woman, or a junub, or one without wudu, then spoiled it - he is not required to make it up because he did not enter a complete prayer. End. So it is known by this that the madhhab is the authentication of al-Muhit of the invalidity of starting, because al-Kafi collected the statements of Muhammad in his books which are Zahir al-Riwaya.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings about invalid following scenarios, followed by a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the follower becomes a starter (shar'i) of his own prayer when his following is invalid. The author lists eight situations (e.g., masbuq following masbuq, lahiq following lahiq, etc.) where following is corrupt. Then the key question: does the person become engaged in his own prayer as a starter? There are two narrations: one authenticated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that he becomes a starter, and another in al-Muhit that he does not. The commentator attempts a distinction: if invalidity is due to missing a condition (e.g., pure following excused), he does not start; if due to a difference in the prayers themselves, he does start. However, Al-Hakim's Kafi refutes this by giving a case where a woman intended Asr behind a muqeem after time – her prayer is invalid but the imam's prayer is not spoiled, implying she did not start a valid prayer. The passage concludes that the relied-upon position (madhhab) is the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani that he does not become a starter, as collected in al-Kafi, which represents Zahir al-Riwaya.

Key Terms
شارعاً (shari'an): A person who has commenced a valid prayer (starter); the act of entering into prayer.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A follower who missed one or more rak'ahs with the imam.
اللاحق (al-lahiq): One who joins late but catches the whole prayer? Actually, lahiq is one who catches the imam from the beginning but then misses a rak'ah due to a valid excuse, such as sleeping. Here it seems used for one who is ahead? The text says 'لا يصح اقتداء المسبوق بالمسبوق ولا اللاحق باللاحق', so both are types of followers.
الظان (al-zann?): One who is uncertain; here it refers to a type of analogy (k al-zann)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) in the Hanafi school, when a masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer) follows another masbuq and the following is invalid, does he become a starter (shari') in his own prayer?
A) Yes, he becomes a starter.
B) No, he does not become a starter.
C) It depends on whether he recites.
D) It is divided: if the invalidity is due to a condition, he becomes a starter.

Key Takeaway
When following is invalid, the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the follower does not become a starter of his own prayer, impacting whether laughter invalidates wudu and whether qada' is required.

Conditions for Following Across a Barrier (Ha'il)
Lists barriers and conditions for valid following

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which following the imam across a barrier (ha'il) is valid in the Hanafi school, and apply these conditions to distinguish valid from invalid scenarios.

Core Idea
A barrier invalidates following only if it creates uncertainty (ishtibah) about the imam's actions.

In congregational prayer, followers must be able to perceive the imam's movements. Barriers such as walls, roads, or rivers can hinder this. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the nuanced Hanafi position: the barrier's size and the possibility of connection (seeing or hearing) determine validity. It also clarifies a key point of intra-madhhab discussion regarding the validity of initiating prayer when barrier conditions are not met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the barrier types
List the three specific barriers mentioned in the passage: a road with foot traffic, a great river, and a row of women (by istihsan). Note that each barrier requires the rows to be connected for validity.
The row of women is treated as a barrier that corrupts the prayer of rows behind it.
2
Understand the condition of non-ambiguity
For a wall, the key condition is the absence of ambiguity (ishtibah). If the follower remains certain of the imam's state (by seeing or hearing), the wall does not invalidate. If certainty is lost, following becomes invalid.
This condition is emphasized in al-Khulasa and other works.
3
Analyse the wall scenarios
Distinguish between low walls (below a man's height, narrow) and high walls. Low walls do not prevent. High walls with an open door or window also do not prevent, even if the door is locked or the window small, as long as connection is possible and no ambiguity exists. If the wall is wide and tall with no opening, it prevents validity.
The chosen view (Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani, Qadikhan) states that if there is no ambiguity, the wall does not prevent.
4
Evaluate the secondary discussion on the follower's start
The passage includes a ta'liq analyzing al-Hakim's statements. It concludes that when barrier conditions are not met, the follower's start as a follower is invalid for fard, but he enters a nafil prayer that is not guaranteed. This refutes al-Zayla'i's detail that the start itself is invalid.
The author sides with al-Siraj: the follower does start (valid as nafil), even if the fard is invalid.

حيث لم يقل لم يصح شروعه، فعلم بهذا أن المذهب تصحيح السراج وهو ما نص المؤلف عليه فيما مضى. قوله : (أطلق في الحائط الخ) قال في شرح المنية : لو كان بينهما حائط، فإن كان قصيراً ذليلاً بأن كان طوله دون مشبكة وإن كان لا يشتبه عليه حال الإمام برؤية أو سماع لا يمنع على ما اختاره شمس الأئمة الحلواني قال في المحيط : وهو الصحيح. وكذا اختاره قاضيخان وغيره. وإن كان الحائط على خلاف ما ذكر بأن كان عريضاً And it is mentioned in al-Kafi by al-Hakim that if between the worshipper and the imam there is a road through which people pass, or a great river, his prayer is not valid unless the rows are connected across the road; then it is valid. And it was presented before that the row of women corrupts the prayer of the rows behind it entirely, by istihsan. So the preventers are three. And in it: if between him and the imam there is a wall that surrounds him, his prayer is [invalid?]. End. He is absolute concerning the wall, so it includes small and large, and whether the condition of the imam is ambiguous or not. But it was restricted in al-Khulasa and others to non-ambiguity: if he can reach him, by agreement; if he cannot and there is no ambiguity, they differ. If he stands on the roof of the mosque and [pray?] with the imam, it is valid. He said: they said there are two narrations. But what the author inferred from the statement of al-Hakim does not support it because his statement 'her prayer is not valid' may mean the fard prayer, i.e., this prayer does not suffice for the Asr prayer she intended with the imam due to the corruption of her following, even if her start as nafil is valid. That is why he said: 'and it did not corrupt the imam's prayer' i.e., because her following was not valid. And the second statement of al-Hakim is clearer: his statement 'then he spoiled it' is explicit in the validity of his start, and similarly his statement 'because he did not enter a complete prayer' indicates that he entered an incomplete prayer, i.e., because it was contracted as nafil not guaranteed by qada'. This refutes the detail of al-Zayla'i, since there is no doubt that the corruption in al-Hakim's second statement is due to missing a condition; this indicates the validity of his start in a nafil not guaranteed. So the conclusion is that the correct interpretation of al-Hakim's statement is a proof for what was mentioned in al-Siraj of validating the start, and it is understood from the author's statement 'his following was corrupt' since he did not say 'his start was not valid'. So it is known by this that the madhhab is the authentication of al-Siraj, which is what the author texted previously. His statement: (He was absolute concerning the wall) - he said in Sharh al-Munya: if there is a wall between them, if it is short and low, i.e., its height is less than a man's stature and its width does not exceed that between the rows, it does not prevent due to no ambiguity. Otherwise, if there is a door or a window through which he can reach the imam and it is open, likewise it does not prevent. And if the door is locked or the window is small so that passage is impossible, or it is grilled, and he is not in doubt about the imam's condition by sight or hearing, it does not prevent according to the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani. In al-Muhit: this is the correct view. And Qadikhan and others chose it. If the wall is contrary to what was mentioned, i.e., wide and tall and has no aperture, it prevents. End. His statement: (so it includes the small and large) - al-Ramli said: and it includes whether the wall is in the mosque or elsewhere. His statement: (but it was restricted in al-Khulasa) - in al-Khaniyya: if the wall is large and has an open door or an aperture such that if he wanted to reach the imam he could, and he is not in doubt about the imam's condition by hearing or sight, the following is valid according to their view. In al-Khulasa he added: 'all of it' meaning even if the door is locked or the aperture is small like a [؟] if he wanted to reach...

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for valid following when there is a barrier (ha'il) between the follower and imam. Three types of barriers are identified: a road with traffic, a large river, and a row of women (by istihsan). For a wall, the ruling depends on size and visibility. A low wall that does not obstruct sight or sound does not prevent validity. A large wall with an open door or window through which the imam can be seen or heard also does not prevent, even if the door is locked. If the wall is high and wide and has no opening, following is invalid. The passage also contains a secondary discussion (ta'liq) on the interpretation of Al-Hakim's statements regarding whether the follower becomes a starter, concluding that the correct view is that he does start (as in al-Siraj), contrary to the earlier distinction by al-Zayla'i.

Key Terms
الحائل (al-ha'il): A barrier that physically or visually separates the follower from the imam, potentially invalidating the following.
الاشتباه (al-ishtibah): Uncertainty about the imam's actions; if the barrier prevents seeing or hearing the imam, following may be invalid.
الكوة (al-kuwwah): A window or opening in the wall.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In Hanafi fiqh, if there is a high wall between the follower and the imam with no opening, and the follower cannot see or hear the imam, what is the ruling of the follower's prayer?
A) Valid, because the wall is not a barrier.
B) Invalid, because it causes ambiguity (ishtibah).
C) Valid only if the wall is in the mosque.
D) Invalid, but becomes valid if the follower recites.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a barrier invalidates following only if it prevents the follower from knowing the imam's actions without doubt (ishtibah).

Barriers in Congregational Prayer: The Criterion of Uncertainty
Explaining barriers that affect validity of following an imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on barriers in congregational prayer, identify the criterion of 'adam al-ishtibah, and apply it to various scenarios such as walls, roads, and level differences.

Core Idea
Valid following depends on perceiving the imam, not on physical proximity.

When you join a congregational prayer, what if there is a wall, a road, or a different level between you and the imam? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, which focuses on whether you can see or hear the imam's actions without uncertainty (ishtibah), rather than on physical connection. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on earlier texts to clarify this nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
List the three preventers from al-Kafi
Identify the road, great river, and row of women that invalidate following unless conditions are met. Note that the row of women is by istihsan.
These are mentioned at the beginning of the passage.
2
Analyze the wall ruling
See the shift from an absolute statement that a wall invalidates to a restriction based on uncertainty. Note that low walls, open doors, and windows allow perception and thus do not prevent.
The relied-upon view of al-Halwani and Qadikhan is highlighted.
3
Apply the uncertainty criterion
Determine if the follower can perceive the imam's actions (by sight or sound). If not, the following is invalid. This criterion overrides physical access.
The hadith of Aisha's chamber supports this.
4
Examine the proof
Study the hadith of the Prophet in Aisha's chamber: people followed from outside while unable to reach him. This shows that physical inability does not invalidate following.
The passage cites this from al-Khaniyya.
5
Distinguish barrier types
Note that roads and rivers always prevent following (even without uncertainty), while walls and level differences only prevent if uncertainty arises. Reflect on the wisdom of this distinction.
The author calls for reflection on the difference.
