المسجد بخلاف ما إذا اقتدى من سطح داره المتصلة بالمسجد فإنه يصح مطلقاً . وفي المحيط : ولو اقتدى بالإمام في الصحراء وبينهم قدر صفين فصاعداً لا الاقتداء، ودونه يصح . وصحح أن النهر العظيم ما تجري فيه يصح السفن. وفي المجتبى وفناء المسجد له حكم المسجد يجوز الاقتداء فيه وإن لم تكن الصفوف صحن ما من متصلة ولا تصح في دار الضيافة إلا إذا اتصلت الصفوف .اهـ. وبهذا علم أن الاقتداء الخانقاه الشيخونية بالإمام في المحراب صحيح وإن لم تتصل الصفوف لأن الصحن فناء المسجد، وكذا اقتداء من بالخلاوي السفلية صحیح لأن أبوابها في فناء المسجد ولم يشتبه حال الإمام، وأما اقتداء من بالخلاوي العلوية بإمام المسجد فغير صحيح حتى الخلوتين اللتين فوق الإيوان الصغير وإن كان مسجداً لأن أبوابها خارجة عن فناء المسجد سواء اشتبه حال الإمام أو لا كالمقتدي من سطح داره المتصلة بالمسجد فإنه لا مطلقاً يصح وعلله في المحيط باختلاف المكان . يصح إلى الإمام لا يمكنه لكن لا يشتبه عليه حال الإمام اختلفوا فيه ذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن العبرة في هذا لاشتباه حال الإمام وعدمه لا للتمكن من الوصول إلى الإمام لأن الاقتداء متابعة ومع هذا الاشتباه لا يمكنه المتابعة .اهـ. ونحوه في الخلاصة .والفيض قال في الخانية: والذي يصحح الاختيار ما روينا أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي في حجرة عائشة رضي الله عنها والناس يصلون بصلاته، ونحن نعلم أنهم ما كانوا يتمكنون من الوصول إلى حجرة عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها اهـ. وفيه تأمل. قوله: (بخلاف ما إذا اقتدى من سطح داره (الخ أي لأن بين المسجد وبين سطح داره كثير التخلل فصار المكان مختلفاً، أما في البيت مع المسجد لم يتخلل إلا الحائط ولم يختلف المكان. كذا في الدرر إذ لا فاصل من طريق واسع أو نهر كبير. كذا في شرح الدرر للشيخ اسمعيل . قال في أنه الشرنبلالية : هذا خلاف الصحيح لأنه ذكر مثله في مختصر الظهيرية ثم قال : والصحيح الاقتداء نص عليه في باب الحدث اهـ. والظاهر أن وجهه أن لا يحصل به اختلاف المكان السطح فلا يعد فاصلاً كما لو اقتدى على سطح المسجد أو من بيته وبينه وبين المسجد حائط ولم يحصل اشتباه والحاصل أن اختلاف المكان مانع عند الاشتباه وإن لم يشتبه لا يمنع ولا عبرة بالوصول وعدمه، وأما الفاصل من طريق أو نهر أو فضاء فإنه مانع ولو لم يشتبه فليتأمل في الفرق. قوله : وصحح أن النهر العظيم ما تجري فيه السفن قال الرملي وذكر كثير في الطريق أنه ما تمر فيه العجلة. قوله : (وأما اقتداء من بالخلاوي العلوية الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية : تفريع على غير الصحيح والصحيح صحة الاقتداء لما ذكرناه ولما قاله في البرهان: لو كان بينهما حائط كبير لا يمكن الوصول منه إلى الإمام ولكن لا يشتبه حاله عليه بسماع أو رؤية لانتقالاته لا يمنع صحة الاقتداء في
Concerning the woman praying Zuhr: her prayer is not valid and she does not spoil the imam's prayer... It is explicit in the invalidity of her start due to the difference of the two prayers. And he said elsewhere: A literate man entered the prayer of an illiterate as a voluntary act, or in the prayer of a woman, or a junub, or without wudu, then he spoiled it; he does not have to make it up because he did not enter a complete prayer... So it is known that the madhhab is the correction of al-Muhit regarding the invalidity of the start, because al-Kafi collected the words of Muhammad in his books which are Zahir al-Riwayah, and the author did not mention what prevents following: the barrier. And it is mentioned in al-Kafi by al-Hakim that if between the worshipper and the imam there is a road where people pass, or a great river, his prayer is not valid unless the rows are continguous over the road, then it is allowed. And before that it mentioned that the row of women spoils the prayer of the rows behind it all by istihsan. So the preventers are three. And in it: if between him and the imam there was a wall, it would invalidate his prayer... He spoke generally about the wall, so it includes small and large, and whether the imam's state is uncertain or not. But it was restricted in al-Khulasa and others by the absence of uncertainty: if he can reach him, they agree; if he cannot reach him but there is no uncertainty, they differed. And if he stood on the roof of the mosque, his prayer with the imam is correct. He said: they said there are two narrations. But what the author adduced from the words of al-Hakim does not indicate that, because his saying 'her prayer is not valid' may mean the obligatory prayer, i.e. this prayer does not suffice for the Asr prayer she intended with the imam due to the corruption of her following even though her start was valid as a supererogatory act. Hence he said: 'and she does not spoil the imam's prayer' i.e. because her following was not valid. And the second expression of al-Hakim is clearer in that: his saying 'then he spoiled it' is explicit in the validity of his start; similarly his saying 'because he did not enter a complete prayer' indicates he entered an incomplete prayer, i.e. it was contracted as a non-mandatory supererogatory act not requiring make-up. This refutes the detail of al-Zaylai... So the correct view is that the words of al-Hakim indicate what was mentioned in al-Siraj of validating the start, which is understood from the author's saying 'his following was corrupted' where he did not say 'his start was not valid'. So it is known that the madhhab is the correction of al-Siraj, which is what the author stated previously. His saying: (He spoke generally about the wall etc.) He said in Sharh al-Munyah: If between them there is a wall, if it is short and humble, i.e. its height less than a cubit and its width not exceeding the space between rows, it does not prevent due to absence of uncertainty. Otherwise, if it has a door or window from which one can reach the imam and it is open, then likewise it does not prevent. If the door is closed or the window is too small to pass through, or it is grilled, even if the imam's state is not uncertain by sight or hearing, it does not prevent according to the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. Al-Muhit said: That is the correct view. Qadikhan and others chose it too. If the wall is contrary to what was mentioned, i.e. wide and long with no opening, it prevents. End. His saying: (So it includes small and large) Al-Ramli said: It includes whether the wall is in the mosque or elsewhere. His saying: (But it was restricted in al-Khulasa etc.) In al-Khaniyya: If the wall is large and has an open door or hole through which he can reach the imam if he wants, and the imam's state is not uncertain by hearing or sight, the following is valid according to their statement. Al-Khulasa added: unanimously. If it has a closed door or a small hole like a window, if he wants to reach and follows the imam, or from the minaret following the imam in the mosque: if they have a door in the mosque and there is no uncertainty, it is valid according to their statement. If from outside the mosque with no uncertainty, there is a difference. In al-Khulasa, validity is chosen. Similarly, on a wall between his house and the mosque, unlike if he follows from the roof of his house connected to the mosque, it is valid absolutely. In al-Muhit: If one follows the imam in the desert with a distance of two rows or more, no following; less than that, it is valid. And it is established that a great river is one in which ships sail. In al-Mujtaba: The courtyard of the mosque has the same ruling as the mosque; following is allowed in it even if rows are not connected. It is not valid in a guest house unless rows are connected. End. Thus it is known that following from the Khanqah Shaykhuuniyyah with the imam in the mihrab is valid even if rows are not connected because the courtyard is the courtyard of the mosque. Similarly, following from the lower cells is valid because their doors are in the courtyard of the mosque and the imam's state is not uncertain. As for following from the upper cells with the imam of the mosque, it is invalid, even the two cells above the small iwan if it is a mosque, because their doors are outside the courtyard of the mosque, whether the imam's state is uncertain or not, like one who follows from the roof of his house connected to the mosque, it is not valid absolutely. Al-Muhit explained it by difference of place. He said: (If he cannot reach the imam but his state is not uncertain, they differed about it.) Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned that the criterion in this is the uncertainty of the imam's state or its absence, not the ability to reach the imam, because following is imitation, and with this uncertainty he cannot imitate. End. Similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Fayd. He said in al-Khaniyya: What validates the choice is what we have narrated: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to pray in the chamber of Aisha رضي الله عنها and the people prayed following his prayer, and we know that they were not able to reach the chamber of Aisha رضي الله عنها. End. There is reflection in it. His saying: (Unlike if he follows from the roof of his house etc.) i.e. because between the mosque and the roof of his house there is much intervening space, so the place becomes different. As for the house with the mosque, only the wall intervenes and the place does not differ. Thus in al-Durar, for there is no separator of a wide road or big river. Thus in Sharh al-Durar by Shaykh Ismail. He said in al-Sharnablaliyya: This is contrary to the correct view, because he mentioned similar in Mukhtasar al-Zahiriyya then said: What is correct is the validity of following as stated in the chapter on hadath. End. The apparent reasoning is that the roof does not cause a difference of place, so it is not considered a separator, just as if he followed from the roof of the mosque or from his house with only a wall between him and the mosque and no uncertainty. The upshot is that difference of place is a preventer when there is uncertainty; if there is no uncertainty, it does not prevent, and no regard is given to ability or inability to reach. As for a separator of a road, river, or open space, it is a preventer even without uncertainty. So one should reflect on the difference. His saying: (And it is established that the great river is one in which ships sail.) Al-Ramli said: Many mentioned regarding the road that it is one through which a cart passes. His saying: (As for following from the upper cells etc.) He said in al-Sharnablaliyya: It is a branch based on the incorrect view; the correct view is the validity of following because of what we mentioned and because of what was said in al-Burhan: If between them there is a large wall from which it is not possible to reach the imam, but his state is not uncertain by hearing or sight of his movements, it does not prevent the validity of following.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discusses the conditions for valid following (iqtida') in congregational prayer, specifically when there is a barrier (ha'il) between the follower and the imam. The passage type is an expansion probe, as it elaborates on rulings from earlier texts like al-Kafi and al-Muhit. The core issue is whether a barrier invalidates the following due to preventing knowledge of the imam's actions. The Hanafi position, as detailed here, is that the critical factor is whether the follower can see or hear the imam's movements (i.e., lack of uncertainty, 'adam al-ishtibah), not necessarily physical proximity or ability to reach the imam. The passage begins by citing al-Hakim's statement from al-Kafi: if there is a road or great river between the worshipper and the imam, the prayer is invalid unless rows are connected across it. Three preventers are identified: road, river, and row of women (by istihsan). However, regarding a wall, the text notes that it was initially stated absolutely that a wall invalidates, but then restricted: if the wall is low (less than a cubit high and not wide) it does not prevent; if it has an open door or window allowing visual or auditory connection, it also does not prevent. The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is that of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, adopted by Qadikhan and others: a large wall with no opening that causes uncertainty prevents, but if the follower can see or hear the imam despite the wall, it is valid. The passage then discusses similar issues for following from a roof, minaret, upper cells, etc. The principle: difference of place (ikhtilaf al-makan) prevents only when it leads to uncertainty about the imam's actions. The anecdote about the Prophet praying in Aisha's chamber while people followed from outside demonstrates that inability to physically reach the imam does not necessarily invalidate following, as long as the imam's actions are known. The passage concludes by distinguishing between a separator like a road or river (always prevents, even without uncertainty) versus a wall or difference in level where uncertainty is the criterion. This ruling is found in Zahir al-Riwayah sources like al-Kafi and al-Muhit, though there is some ikhtilaf among later scholars.

Key Terms
الحائل (al-ḥāʾil): Any physical barrier (wall, road, river, etc.) between the follower and the imam that may affect the validity of following.
الاشتباه (al-ishtibāh): Uncertainty or confusion about the imam's actions in prayer, such that the follower cannot properly follow.
فناء المسجد (fanāʾ al-masjid): The courtyard or forecourt of a mosque, which has the same ruling as the mosque itself for the validity of following.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon criterion for whether a wall between follower and imam invalidates the following?
A) The height of the wall
B) Whether the follower can physically reach the imam
C) Whether the follower can see or hear the imam without uncertainty
D) Whether the wall is inside or outside the mosque

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of following in congregational prayer depends on the follower's ability to perceive the imam's actions without uncertainty, not on physical proximity.

Spatial Separation in Following the Imam: Confusion as the Criterion
Commentary on physical barriers: river, road, wall, roof, courtyard, khanqah cells.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on following an imam when barriers like a wall, roof, road, or river separate them, and APPLY the criterion of confusion to determine validity of the prayer.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, valid following requires no confusion, not physical proximity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical concern: can you pray behind an imam if there is a river, road, wall, or roof between you? The text clarifies that the key is whether you can observe the imam's actions without confusion, not your ability to reach him. We will explore the nuanced rulings on different types of barriers and the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the criterion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (iqtida following the imam) and what the default ruling is for each scenario (roof, wall, courtyard, cells, river, road).
Note that the ruling varies: some barriers invalidate absolutely, others only if there is confusion.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited for the principle that confusion is the criterion. The text quotes the hadith of the Prophet praying in Aisha's room while companions followed from outside.
Consider the epistemological weight of this hadith (ahad, zanni thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove that inability to reach the imam does not invalidate? The companions could not enter the room but still followed correctly because they could track his actions.
This is the core of the proof: following is emulation, and confusion prevents emulation, not distance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement: some scholars require ability to reach the imam (difference of place invalidates), while Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and others say confusion is the only criterion.
Also note the distinction between barriers like a wall (doesn't invalidate if no confusion) vs. a road/river (invalidates regardless).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which view is relied upon for fatwa. The text cites al-Burhan and al-Shurnbulaliyya supporting Halwani's view, making it the mufta bihi.
Practical consequence: followers in upper cells of Khanqah Shaykhuniyya can pray behind the imam if they can see or hear him without confusion.

والحاصل أن اختلاف المكان مانع عند الاشتباه وإن لم يشتبه لا يمنع ولا عبرة بالوصول وعدمه، وأما الفاصل من طريق أو نهر أو فضاء فإنه مانع ولو لم يشتبه فليتأمل في الفرق. قوله : وصحح أن النهر العظيم ما تجري الاقتداء بإمام المسجد الحرام في المحال المتصلة به وإن كانت أبوابها من خارج المسجد. قوله : ( وإن كان مسجداً الخ) قال الرملي : يعكر عليه ما في الضياء المعنوي شرح مقدمة الغزنوي : ولو قام الإمام على سطح المسجد والقوم في المسجد ولا يشتبه عليهم حال الإمام صح ا الاقتداء وإن لم يكن له باب لكن لا يشتبه عليهم حال الاقتداء اهـ. وأنت على علم أنه إذا كان على سطح المسجد والقوم في المسجد أو عكسه الإمام صح لم يختلف المكان لأن لسطح المسجد حكم المسجد فكان الكل كبقعة واحدة بخلاف سطح داره تأمل . وينبغي أن يحكم الخ ) قال في النهر : لكن علل الشارح البطلان في الاثني عشرية بأن إمامه قادر على الماء بإخباره واعلم أن المراد بالفساد هنا هو فساد الوصف فقد قال في المحيط : المتوضىء خلف المتيمم إذا رأى الماء أو كان على الإمام فائتة لا يذكرها أو صلى إلى غير القبلة وهو لا يعلم ذلك
And he follows the imam while on the minaret, following the imam in the mosque. If both have a door in the mosque and there is no confusion, it is permissible according to their statement. If [the follower] is outside the mosque and there is no confusion, then it is according to disagreement. In al-Khulasa, validity is chosen, and likewise on a wall between his house and the mosque, contrary to if he follows from the roof of his house connected to the mosque, then it is absolutely valid. In al-Muhit: If he follows the imam in the desert and between them is the distance of two rows or more, there is no following; less than that is valid. And it is corrected that the great river is that in which ships sail. In al-Mujtaba: The courtyard of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque; following is allowed in it even if the rows are not connected, and it is not valid in a guesthouse unless the rows are connected. From this it is known that following in the Khanqah Shaykhuniyya with the imam in the mihrab is valid even if the rows are not connected because the courtyard is the courtyard of the mosque, and likewise the following of those in the lower cells is valid because their doors open into the courtyard of the mosque and the state of the imam is not ambiguous. As for the following of those in the upper cells with the imam of the mosque, it is invalid, including the two cells above the small iwan even if it is a mosque, because their doors are outside the courtyard of the mosque, whether the state of the imam is ambiguous or not, like the one following from the roof of his house connected to the mosque, for it is absolutely invalid, and al-Muhit explains it due to difference of place. He cannot reach the imam but there is no confusion about the state of the imam; they differed on this. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned that the consideration in this is the confusion about the state of the imam or its absence, not the ability to reach the imam because following is emulation and with this confusion he cannot emulate. Similar in al-Khulasa. Al-Fayd said in al-Khaniyya: What validates the choice is what we narrated that the Messenger of Allah prayed in the room of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, and the people prayed with his prayer, and we know that they were not able to reach the room of Aisha. There is consideration in it. His saying: (contrary to if he followed from the roof of his house) meaning because between the mosque and the roof of his house there is much penetration, so the place becomes different. As for the house with the mosque, there is no penetration except the wall and the place does not differ. Thus in al-Durar, as there is no barrier of a wide road or a large river. Thus in Sharh al-Durar by Sheikh Isma'il. He said in al-Shurnbulaliyya: This is contrary to the correct because he mentioned the like in Mukhtasar al-Zahiriyya then said: The correct is following, as stated in the chapter of hadath. The apparent is that its aspect is that the roof does not cause a difference in place so it is not considered a barrier, just as if he followed on the roof of the mosque or from his house and between him and the mosque is a wall and no confusion occurs. The conclusion is that difference of place prevents when there is confusion, and if there is no confusion it does not prevent. Consideration is not given to arrival or its absence. As for a barrier of a road, river, or open space, it prevents even if there is no confusion; let one reflect on the difference. His saying: And it is corrected that the great river is that in which ships sail. Al-Ramli said, and many mentioned in the road that it is that in which a cart passes. His saying: (As for the following of those in the upper cells) He said in al-Shurnbulaliyya: It is a branch on the incorrect, and the correct is the validity of following for what we mentioned and for what he said in al-Burhan: If between them there is a large wall, there is no way from it to the imam but his state is not confused upon him by hearing or seeing his movements, it does not prevent the validity of following according to the correct, and it is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. And on the correct, it is valid to follow the imam of Masjid al-Haram in the connected places even if their doors are outside the mosque. His saying: (And if it is a mosque) al-Ramli said: What challenges it is in al-Diya' al-Ma'nawi: If the imam stood on the roof of the mosque and the people are in the mosque and there is no confusion about the state of the imam, the following is valid even if there is no door for him, but there is no confusion about their following. And you know that if he is on the roof of the mosque and the people in the mosque or vice versa, the following is valid, as the place does not differ because the roof of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque, so all is like one place, contrary to the roof of his house, reflect. And it is appropriate that one judges. He said in al-Nahr: But the commentator explained the invalidity in the twelfth [issue] that his imam is able to have water by informing him, and know that what is meant by corruption here is corruption of the description, as al-Muhit said: The one with wudu behind the mutayammim if he sees water or there is a missed prayer on the imam that he does not remember, or he prays towards other than the qibla while he does not know that.
Source pages p. 635

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the conditions for valid following (iqtida) when there is spatial separation. The author first addresses a person on a minaret following an imam in the mosque: if both have doors opening into the mosque and no confusion occurs, it is permissible according to the two shaykhs. If the follower is outside the mosque, there is disagreement. Al-Khulasa prefers validity. The same applies to a wall between house and mosque. However, if on the roof of a house connected to the mosque, it is absolutely valid per al-Muhit. In the desert, a distance of two rows or more invalidates following. A large river is defined as navigable by ships, acting as a barrier. The courtyard of the mosque is treated as part of the mosque. In the Khanaqah Shaykhuniyya, the mihrab is in the courtyard, so following is valid even if rows are not connected. Lower cells opening into the courtyard are valid; upper cells are invalid because their doors are outside the courtyard, analogous to a roof. The key principle is whether the follower can track the imam's actions. The hadith of Aisha (RA) shows that the Companions followed the Prophet from outside her room without reaching him, proving that inability to reach does not invalidate if there is no confusion. The text also distinguishes between barriers like a road or river (which invalidate even without confusion) and a wall (which does not invalidate if no confusion). The commentary ends with a note that 'corruption' mentioned is fasad al-wasf, not the prayer itself.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida): Following the imam in prayer by intention and action.
اشتباه (ishtibah): Confusion about the imam's actions, such that the follower cannot properly emulate.
اختلاف المكان (ikhtilaf al-makan): Difference of place caused by a barrier like a road, river, or open space that prevents valid following even without confusion.
فساد الوصف (fasad al-wasf): Corruption of the description (i.e., the prayer is valid but its perfection is reduced), not corruption of the prayer itself.
فناء المسجد (fina' al-masjid): The courtyard or open space connected to the mosque, which has the same ruling as the mosque for following.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented, what is the ruling if a person follows an imam from the roof of his house connected to the mosque, with no confusion about the imam's actions?
A) Invalid because the place is different.
B) Valid because the roof is connected to the mosque.
C) Valid if he can see or hear the imam without confusion.
D) Invalid unless the rows are connected.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of following an imam with spatial separation hinges on the absence of confusion about the imam's actions, not on physical proximity or eliminating all barriers.

Following a Mutayammim Imam: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on following a mutayammim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on a person with wudu following a mutayammim imam, identify the usul basis of each view, and state the mufta bihi with its conditions.

Core Idea
Following a mutayammim imam is valid because substitution is between instruments, not purities; the hadith of Amr ibn al-As confirms it.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a person who has performed wudu can validly pray behind an imam who used tayammum. The disagreement hinges on a fundamental usul question: is substitution (khilafiyya) between the instruments (water and dust) or between the resulting purities? By working through the different positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with the key hadith evidence, you will understand the preferred ruling in the school and the practical conditions that apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The matn states 'no following of a person with wudu by a mutayammim,' but the commentator explains this means it does not corrupt. Muhammad holds it invalid (fasid), while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it valid.
The dispute is only in prayers other than janaza; janaza is unanimously valid.
2
Understand the usul basis of the dispute
The disagreement is built on whether substitution (khilafiyya) is between the instruments (water and dust) or between the purities (wudu and tayammum). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf take the first view; Muhammad takes the second.
If substitution is between instruments, both purities are equal; if between purities, wudu is 'stronger' and tayammum 'weaker'.
3
Analyze the dalil: Hadith of Amr ibn al-As
The hadith: Amr led his people with tayammum due to fear of cold while they had wudu, and the Prophet did not order repetition upon learning. This supports validity, as the Prophet approved.
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and conditions
Practically, one may pray behind a mutayammim imam, but the condition from al-Mujtaba is that the followers have no water. If they have water, they cannot follow because they would consider the imam's prayer invalid.
If the follower sees water during prayer but the imam does not, the follower's prayer becomes corrupt (fasad al-wasf) if he thinks the imam knows.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the rationale
The madhhab preferred the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf due to the hadith of Amr. The ruling is validity, but restricted to followers without water.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin; the tarjih is based on the action of a Companion and the Prophet's tacit approval.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا اقتداء متوضىء بمتيمم) أي لا يفسد أطلقه فشمل الاقتداء في صلاة الجنازة أو غيرها، ولا خلاف في صحته في صلاة الجنازة كما في الخلاصة. واختلفوا في غيرها فذهب محمد إلى فساده وذهبا إلى صحته والخلاف مبني على أن الخلفية هل هي بين الآلتين وهما الماء والتراب وبه قالا، أو بين الطهارتين وبه أخذ محمد؛ فعنده هو بناء القوي على الضعيف، وعندهما الطهارتان سواء، وتمامه في الأصول وترجح المذهب بفعل عمرو بن العاص حين صلى بقومه بالتيمم لخوف البرد من غسل الجنابة وهم متوضؤون ولم يأمرهم عليه الصلاة والسلام بالإعادة حين علم، وشمل ما إذا كان مع المتوضئين ماء أو لا لكن قيده في المجتبى بأن لا يكون مع المتوضئين أن يحكم أن محل الفساد عندهم إذا ظن علم إمامه به لأن اعتقاده فساد صلاة إمامه بذلك اهـ. ثم اعلم أن في طهارة التيمم جهة الإطلاق باعتبار عدم توقتها وجهة الضرورة وباعتبار أن المصير إليها ضرورة عدم القدرة على الماء، فاعتبر محمد جهة الضرورة في هذا الباب احتياطاً وجهة الإطلاق في باب الرجعة احتياطاً وهما اعتبرا جهة الإطلاق هنا لحديث عمرو بن العاص وجهة الضرورة في الرجعة كما سيأتي إيضاحه فيها إن شاء الله تعالى. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى أبي بكر الرازي جواز إمامة من توضأ بسؤر الحمار وتيمم المتوضئين. قوله : (وغاسل بماسح) لاستواء حالهما لأن الخف مانع سراية الحدث إلى القدم وما حل بالخف يزيله المسح بخلاف المستحاضة لأن الحدث موجود حقيقة وإن جعل في حقها معدوماً للضرورة. أطلق الماسح فشمل ماسح الخف وماسح الجبيرة وهو أولى بالجواز لأنه كالغسل لما ماء تحته . الصحيح، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني .اهـ. وعلى الصحيح يصح الاقتداء بإمام المسجد الحرام في المحال المتصلة به وإن كانت أبوابها من خارج المسجد. قوله : ( وإن كان مسجداً الخ) قال الرملي : يعكر عليه ما في الضياء المعنوي شرح مقدمة الغزنوي : ولو قام الإمام على سطح المسجد والقوم في المسجد ولا يشتبه عليهم حال الإمام صح ا الاقتداء وإن لم يكن له باب لكن لا يشتبه عليهم حال الاقتداء اهـ. وأنت على علم أنه إذا كان على سطح المسجد والقوم في المسجد أو عكسه الإمام صح لم يختلف المكان لأن لسطح المسجد حكم المسجد فكان الكل كبقعة واحدة بخلاف سطح داره تأمل . وينبغي أن يحكم الخ ) قال في النهر : لكن علل الشارح البطلان في الاثني عشرية بأن إمامه قادر على الماء بإخباره واعلم أن المراد بالفساد هنا هو فساد الوصف فقد قال في المحيط : المتوضىء خلف المتيمم إذا رأى الماء أو كان على الإمام فائتة لا يذكرها أو صلى إلى غير القبلة وهو لا يعلم ذلك
His saying: (There is no following of a person with wudu by a mutayammim) meaning it does not corrupt; he generalized it so it includes following in funeral prayer or other. There is no disagreement on its validity in funeral prayer as in al-Khulasa. They disagreed in other than funeral prayer: Muhammad went to its corruption, and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) went to its validity. The disagreement is built on whether substitution is between the two instruments, water and dust, as the two said, or between the two purities, as Muhammad took. According to him, it is building the strong on the weak, and according to them, the two purities are equal. Its full discussion is in usul. The madhhab is preferred by the action of Amr ibn al-As when he prayed with his people using tayammum due to fear of cold from washing janaba while they had wudu, and the Prophet did not order them to repeat when he knew. It includes whether the wudu performers have water or not, but al-Mujtaba restricts that they have no water; if they have water, they cannot follow. Al-Fath al-Qadir mentions that this restriction is based on a branch: if the wudu-performer following a mutayammim sees water during prayer without the imam seeing it, his prayer becomes corrupt because he believes the imam's prayer is corrupt due to the presence of water. The corruption occurs if he thinks the imam knows about the water; otherwise not. Then know that in the purity of tayammum there is an aspect of unrestrictedness (jihah al-itlaq) due to its lack of time limit, and an aspect of necessity (jihah al-darurah) because resorting to it is a necessity due to inability to use water. Muhammad considered the aspect of necessity in this chapter as a precaution, and the aspect of unrestrictedness in the chapter of revocable divorce (raj'ah) as a precaution. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) considered the aspect of unrestrictedness here due to the hadith of Amr ibn al-As, and the aspect of necessity in raj'ah, as will be explained. In al-Mujtaba, attributed to Abu Bakr al-Razi, it is permissible to follow an imam who performed wudu with the leftover water of a donkey, and the mutayammim's following of those with wudu. His saying: (And one who washes [his foot] by one who wipes [his khuff]) because their states are equal; the khuff prevents the spread of hadath to the foot, and what reaches the khuff, the wipe removes it, contrary to a mustahada because hadath exists in reality although it is considered non-existent for her due to necessity. He generalized the wiper to include the one who wipes the khuff and the one who wipes the splint (jabira), and it is more deserving of permissibility because it is like washing due to what is under it. The correct [view] is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. On the correct, it is valid to follow the imam of Masjid al-Haram in the connected places even if their doors are outside the mosque. His saying: (And if it is a mosque) al-Ramli said: What challenges it is in al-Diya' al-Ma'nawi: If the imam stood on the roof of the mosque and the people are in the mosque and there is no confusion about the state of the imam, the following is valid even if there is no door for him, but there is no confusion about their following. And you know that if he is on the roof of the mosque and the people in the mosque or vice versa, the following is valid because the place does not differ since the roof of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque, so all is like one place, contrary to the roof of his house, reflect. And it is appropriate that one judges. He said in al-Nahr: But the commentator explained the invalidity in the twelfth [issue] that his imam is able to have water by informing him, and know that what is meant by corruption here is corruption of the description, as al-Muhit said: The one with wudu behind the mutayammim if he sees water or there is a missed prayer on the imam that he does not remember, or he prays towards other than the qibla while he does not know that.
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a person with wudu (mutawaddi) following an imam who performed tayammum (mutayammim). The matn states 'no following', which the commentator explains means it does not corrupt the prayer, but there is disagreement over its validity in prayers other than janaza. Muhammad b. al-Hasan holds it invalid because he considers tayammum a weaker purity, so following is building the strong on the weak. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it valid because both wudu and tayammum are pure in their own right; the substitution is between the instruments (water and dust), not the purities. They support their view with the practice of Amr ibn al-As, who led the prayer with tayammum while his followers had wudu, and the Prophet approved. However, a condition from al-Mujtaba is that the followers have no water; if they have water, they cannot follow because they would consider the imam's prayer invalid. If during prayer the follower sees water, his prayer is corrupted if he thinks the imam also knows, but the corruption is of the description (fasad al-wasf), not the prayer itself. The text also discusses the two aspects of tayammum: unrestricted (due to no time limit) and necessity. Muhammad applies the necessity aspect here for caution, while the two apply the unrestricted aspect due to the hadith. The passage also covers related sub-rulings: following an imam who used donkey's leftover water is permissible, and the ruling of a person who washed his foot (ghasil) following one who wiped his khuff (masih) is valid because both are equal in removing hadath. The correct view overall is that a mutawaddi can follow a mutayammim.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who performs tayammum (dry ablution) due to lack of water or inability to use it.
خلفية (khilafiyya): The concept of substitution: whether it is between two instruments (water and dust) or between two purities (wudu and tayammum).
جهة الإطلاق (jihah al-itlaq): The aspect of unrestrictedness of tayammum, i.e., it is not limited by time and can be used for any prayer until water is found.
جهة الضرورة (jihah al-darurah): The aspect of necessity of tayammum, i.e., it is a concession for necessity, so it should be treated with caution.
فساد الوصف (fasad al-wasf): Corruption of the description, meaning the prayer is valid but lacks perfection; not requiring repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical effect of the condition from al-Mujtaba regarding a mutawaddi following a mutayammim?
A) The follower must have performed tayammum as well.
B) The follower must not have water available at the time of prayer.
C) The follower must repeat the prayer after finding water.
D) The prayer is always valid regardless of water availability.

Key Takeaway
A person with wudu may validly follow a mutayammim imam only if he has no water available, based on the hadith of Amr ibn al-As and the Hanafi usul of substitution between instruments.

Ruling on a Person with Wudu Following a Mutayammim Imam
Intra-Hanafi dispute over following a mutayammim imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a person with wudu following a mutayammim imam, explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the qualified ruling with the exception when followers have water.

Core Idea
A person with wudu can follow a mutayammim imam – the two purifications are equal instruments before the Law.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks an internal Hanafi dispute over the validity of a person with wudu (mutawaddi') praying behind an imam who has performed tayammum. While the matn states it is invalid, the commentary reveals that the relied-upon position is validity, based on the practice of a Companion and a key difference in how the substitution (khilafiyyah) between water and earth is understood. You will learn the arguments of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus Imam Muhammad, and the crucial qualification when the followers themselves have water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of the matn and its absolute wording
The matn states 'no following of a mutawaddi' by a mutayammim', which appears absolute, covering all prayers including janazah.
The author immediately notes this is absolute (atlaqa).
2
Locate the exception for janazah prayer
There is consensus (la khilaf) that following a mutayammim imam in janazah prayer is valid; the dispute is only for other prayers.
This shows the matn's generality is not meant for janazah.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds it invalid (fasid); Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) hold it valid (sahih). The dispute is over the nature of substitution (khilafiyyah).
Know the positions of the three main Hanafi imams.
4
Analyze the theoretical basis: instruments vs. purifications
The Sahibayn view the substitution as between the two instruments (water and earth), making both purifications equal. Imam Muhammad views it as between the two purifications, making tayammum weaker.
This usul concept determines whether the follower's strong purification is built on a weak one.
5
Examine the dalil: hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As
The Prophet did not order a repeat when 'Amr led people with tayammum while they had wudu. This taqrir (tacit approval) is the primary evidence for the Sahibayn.
The hadith overrides the analogy (qiyas) that Imam Muhammad uses.
6
Apply the qualification: water with the followers invalidates
The ruling is valid only when the followers do not have water. If they have water, following is invalid. A branch discusses the follower's belief about the imam's knowledge of water.
This qualification is critical for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا اقتداء متوضىء بمتيمم) أي لا يفسد أطلقه فشمل الاقتداء في صلاة الجنازة أو غيرها، ولا خلاف في صحته في صلاة الجنازة كما في الخلاصة. واختلفوا في غيرها فذهب محمد إلى فساده وذهبا إلى صحته والخلاف مبني على أن الخلفية هل هي بين الآلتين وهما الماء والتراب وبه قالا، أو بين الطهارتين وبه أخذ محمد؛ فعنده هو بناء القوي على الضعيف، وعندهما الطهارتان سواء، وتمامه في الأصول وترجح المذهب بفعل عمرو بن العاص حين صلى بقومه بالتيمم لخوف البرد من غسل الجنابة وهم متوضؤون ولم يأمرهم عليه الصلاة والسلام بالإعادة حين علم، وشمل ما إذا كان مع المتوضئين ماء أو لا لكن قيده في المجتبى بأن لا يكون مع المتوضئين ماء، أما إذا كان ماء فلا معهم الاقتداء. وذكر في فتح القدير أن هذا التقييد يبتنى على فرع إذا رأى المتوضيء المقتدي بمتيمم في الصلاة لم يره الإمام فسدت صلاته لاعتقاده فساد صلاة الإمام لوجود الماء، وينبغي أن يحكم أن محل الفساد عندهم إذا ظن علم إمامه به لأن اعتقاده فساد صلاة إمامه بذلك اهـ. ثم اعلم أن في طهارة التيمم جهة الإطلاق باعتبار عدم توقتها وجهة الضرورة وباعتبار أن المصير إليها ضرورة عدم القدرة على الماء، فاعتبر محمد جهة الضرورة في هذا الباب احتياطاً وجهة الإطلاق في باب الرجعة احتياطاً وهما اعتبرا جهة الإطلاق هنا لحديث عمرو بن العاص وجهة الضرورة في الرجعة كما سيأتي إيضاحه فيها إن شاء الله تعالى. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى أبي بكر الرازي جواز إمامة من توضأ بسؤر الحمار وتيمم المتوضئين.
His statement: (No following of a mutawaddi' by a mutayammim) meaning it is invalid. He made it absolute, so it includes following in janazah prayer or otherwise. There is no dispute about its validity in janazah prayer as in al-Khulasa. They differed regarding other prayers: Muhammad ruled it invalid, while they two ruled it valid. The dispute is based on whether the substitution is between the two instruments, namely water and earth, as they said, or between the two purifications, as Muhammad held. According to him, it is building the strong upon the weak; according to them, the two purifications are equal. Its full discussion is in Usul. The school is strengthened by the action of 'Amr ibn al-'As who prayed with his people using tayammum due to fear of cold from ghusl janabah while they had wudu, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not order them to repeat when he learned. It includes whether the followers have water or not, but al-Mujtaba qualified it that the followers should not have water; if they have water, then following is not valid. In Fath al-Qadir, it is mentioned that this qualification is based on a branch: if the follower sees water while behind the mutayammim imam but the imam does not see it, his prayer is invalid because he believes the imam's prayer is invalid due to the presence of water. It should be judged that the place of invalidity according to them is when he thinks the imam knows about it, because his belief that the imam's prayer is invalid is due to that. Then know that tayammum's purification has an aspect of absoluteness due to not being time-bound and an aspect of necessity, and because resorting to it is a necessity of inability to get water. So Muhammad considered the aspect of necessity in this chapter as a precaution, and the aspect of absoluteness in the chapter of revocable divorce as a precaution, while they two considered the aspect of absoluteness here due to the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As, and the aspect of necessity in revocable divorce as will be clarified later. In al-Mujtaba, attributed to Abu Bakr al-Razi, is the permissibility of an imam who performed wudu with the left-over water of a donkey leading those who performed tayammum.
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person with wudu following an imam who performed tayammum. The matn states it is invalid, but the commentary explains that the ruling is not absolute. For janazah prayer, there is consensus on validity. For other prayers, Imam Muhammad holds it invalid, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it valid. The dispute is rooted in a theoretical difference: are water and earth both means of purification (so tayammum equals wudu in rank), or is tayammum a purification of necessity (so it is weaker)? The Sahibayn view the substitution as between the two instruments, so a person with water (mutawaddi') and a mutayammim are equal in purity. Imam Muhammad sees tayammum as a weaker purification, so it is building the strong on the weak, which is invalid. The tarjih (preference) is given to the Sahibayn's view based on the action of 'Amr ibn al-'As, reported in a hadith where he led people who had wudu while he was in a state of janabah and performed tayammum due to cold, and the Prophet did not order a repeat. However, this ruling is qualified: if the followers themselves have water, the following is invalid. The commentary also cites a branch from Fath al-Qadir about a follower who sees water but the imam does not, and discusses the basis of invalidity depending on the follower's belief about the imam's knowledge. Finally, the author notes the two aspects of tayammum's taharah: absoluteness (not time-bound) and necessity. Muhammad uses the necessity aspect here to invalidate following, while the Sahibayn use the absoluteness aspect due to the hadith. The passage also includes a separate fatwa from al-Mujtaba that it is permissible for an imam who performed wudu with water left over by a donkey to lead those who performed tayammum.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who performs dry ablution (tayammum) instead of wudu due to lack of water or inability to use it.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer; the validity conditions for such following.
خلفية (khilafiyyah): The principle of substitution; whether tayammum substitutes for water as a tool or for the purification act itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what basis do Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the validity of a mutawaddi' following a mutayammim?
A) They consider tayammum as a purification of necessity, weaker than wudu.
B) They consider the substitution to be between the two instruments, making both purifications equal.
C) They rely on qiyas that building the strong on the weak is valid.
D) They believe the matter is beyond dispute.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a person with wudu can validly follow a mutayammim imam, based on the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As, unless the followers themselves have water.
